Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Hujjiyah of Qiyas: Definition and Proof
Establishing qiyas as a valid proof with definition and scriptural evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of qiyas, identify the primary proof from the hadith of Mu'adh, and articulate the Hanafi response to the objection that the Quran is sufficient.

Core Idea
Qiyas is a necessary tool when texts are silent; its authority is rooted in Prophetic approval and consensus.

This lesson addresses a foundational question in usul al-fiqh: how do we derive rulings when no explicit text exists? The Hanafi school, following the practice of the Companions, holds that analogical reasoning (qiyas) is a valid and binding proof. The author presents the definition of qiyas, cites the famous hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal as direct evidence, and refutes the objections of those who reject qiyas entirely.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of qiyas
The author defines qiyas as transferring a ruling from an original case to a new case via a shared effective cause (illah) that is not merely linguistic.
The definition emphasizes that the illah is not purely verbal but a meaningful attribute.
2
Examine the primary scriptural proof
The hadith of Mu'adh: when the Prophet (SAW) asked Mu'adh how he would judge, Mu'adh outlined a sequence: Quran, then Sunnah, then ijtihad. The Prophet approved this, indicating that ijtihad (which includes qiyas) is permissible when texts are absent.
The Prophet's praise ("Praise be to Allah...") confirms the validity of this methodology.
3
Analyze the supporting evidence
The story of the Khath'ami woman: the Prophet analogized Hajj on behalf of an incapable person to paying a debt, thereby demonstrating qiyas in practice.
This shows the Prophet himself used analogical reasoning.
4
Address the objections
Some groups (Rawafid, Khawarij) reject qiyas citing Quran 16:89 ('We have sent down the Book as an explanation of everything'). The author responds that qiyas reveals what is implicit in the Book; it is not an addition. Also, Quran 4:59 ('refer disputes to Allah and the Messenger') implies that when no direct text exists, one must seek similarity (qiyas) with textual cases.
The response shows that qiyas is a method of uncovering the divine intent, not a human innovation.
5
Appreciate the consensus
The author notes that all Companions, Successors, and scholars of every age (except a few) have acted on qiyas, making it a matter of ijma.
This consensus adds weight to the authority of qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الرابع في القياس
فصل في حجية القياس:
القياس حجة من حجج الشرع يجب العمل به عند انعدام ما فوقه من الدليل في الحادثة، وقد ورد في ذلك الأخبار والآثار قال عليه المعاذ بن جبل الله حين بعثه إلى اليمن: "بم حجية القياس تقضي يا مُعَاذ؟ قال: بكتاب الله تعالى، قال: "فإن لم تجد" قال: بسنة رسول الله
- في تكبيرات العيد: اختلف الصحابة في تكبيرات العيدين، فقال بعضهم: يكبر تسعاً: ثلاثاً أصلياً: تكبيرة التحريمة، وتكبيرتي ركوعي ركعتين، وستاً زوائد، وهو قول ابن مسعود الله، وهو المختار عندنا، وقال بعضهم: يكبر ثلاثة عشر : ثلاثاً أصلياً، وعشر ،زوائد خمساً في الأولى، وخمساً في الثانية، وهو قول ابن عباس ، وهو مذهب الشافعي له، وقال بعضهم: يكبر خمسة عشر ثلاثاً أصلياً، واثنا عشر زوائد، في كل ركعة ستة. كما عُرف يعني إذا افتتح الإمام صلاة العيد وهو يرى تكبيرات ابن عباس فصلى ثم تبدل رأيه ورأى تكبيرات ابن مسعود يعمل به في المستقبل؛ لأن التكبيرات مما يحتمل الانتقال فأمكن نقل الحكم من مذهب إلى مذهب كنسخ النص، ولا يعيد ما مضى؛ لوقوعه صحيحاً كذا في "المعدن". في القياس: هو تعدية الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع بعلة متحدة بينهما، ولا تدرك بمجرد اللغة. يجب العمل يه: وهذا مذهب جميع الصحابة والتابعين وعلماء الأمة في كل عصر خلافاً لبعض أهل الهواء كالروافض والخوارج؛ لأن الله تعالى قال: ﴿وَنَزَّلْنَا عَلَيْكَ الْكِتَابَ تِبْيَاناً لِكُلِّ شَيْءٍ فلا يحتاج إلى القياس، والجواب: أن القياس كاشف عما في الكتاب ولا يكون مبايناً له، فكان المثبت هو القياس في الحقيقة، ولأن الله تعالى قال: ﴿فَإِنْ تَنَازَعْتُمْ فِي شَيْءٍ فَرُدُّوهُ إِلَى اللهِ وَالرَّسُول الآية، فقالوا: وجب رد المختلف إلى الكتاب والسنة دون القياس وأجيب بأن رد المختلف إلى المنصوص عليه إنما يكون بالتمثيل أي: طلب المماثلة بين الأصل والفرع والبناء عليه وهو القياس، ويؤيد ذلك الأمر بالرد بعد الأمر بطاعة الله وطاعة رسوله عليها، فإنه يدل على أن الأحكام ثلاثة مثبت بالكتاب والسنة، ومثبت بالرد إليهما على وجه القياس كذا في "البيضاوي". بن جبل إلخ وقال أبو موسى الأشعري حين وجهه إلى اليمن اقض بكتاب الله تعالى، فإن لم تجد فبسنة رسول الله، فإن لم تجد، فاجتهد برأيك، وقال علي لابن مسعود ه اقض بالكتاب والسنة إذا وجدتهما، فإن لم تجد الحكم فيهما فاجتهد برأيك" كذا في "كشف "المنار".

البحث الرابع في القياس
۲۰۱
فصل في حجية القياس
قال: "فإن لم تجد" قال: أجتهد برأيي فصوبه رسولُ الله عليه فقال: "الحمد الله الذي وفق رسول رسول الله على ما يُحبُّ ويَرْضاه ورُوي أن امرأةً خثعمية أتت إلى رسول الله الله فقالت: إن أبي كان شيخاً كبيراً أدركه رسول الحج ولا يَسْتمْسك على الراحلة أفيُجْزُتُنِي أَنْ أحُجَّ عنه؟ قال علي: " أرأيت لو كان على أبيك دَيْنٌ فقضيته أما كان يجزتُك" فقالت: بلى، فقال علي: "فَدَيْنُ الله أَحَقُّ وأولى .. ألحق رسول الله علي الحجّ في حق الشيخ الفاني بالحقوق المالية، وأشار إلى علة مؤثرة في فصوبه إلخ: فتصويبه لمعاذ الله وحمده الله تعالى دليل صريح على جواز العمل بالقياس عند فقدان النص من الكتاب والسنة، فإنه لو لم يكن القياس حجة موجبة للعمل بعد الكتاب والسنة لأنكره عليه، وفي الحديث دلالة قوية على جواز القياس ورد قبيح على من أنكرها أصلاً . قال الترمذي في "جامعه": هذا حديث لا نعرفه إلا من هذا الوجه، وليس إسناده عنده بمتصل، قلت: وبمثل هذا الجرح ليس جرحاً معتبراً، فإن الانقطاع من القرون الثلاثة كالعدل عندنا الثقاة هذا الحديث عده أهل الأصول من المشاهير مرتقياً من الآحاد، وقال الغزالي: من ثم تلقته الأمة بالقبول فصار كالمتواتر فلا شك في كونه من المشاهير والله اعلم. الحمد لله الذي إلخ فلو لم يكن القياس حجة موجبة للعمل بعد الكتاب والسنة لأنكر عليه رسول الله ، وإذا مدحه به حمد الله بتوفيقه لمعاذ بالعمل والاجتهاد دل على أنه حجة موجبة للعمل عند عدم النص من الكتاب والسنة كذا في "المعدن". أحُجَّ : بفتح الهمزة وضم الحاء أي: أحرم وأودي الأفعال عنه هذا المشهور من الرواية.

،
* أخرجه أبو داود في باب اجتهاد الرأي في القضاء رقم ،۳۵۹۲ ، والترمذي في باب ما جاء في القاضي كيف يقضي ، رقم: ۱۳۲۷ ، وأحمد في مسنده : ٢٣۰/۵ عن الحارث بن عمرو. أخرجه البخاري في باب وجوب الحج وفضله، رقم: ١٤٤٢ ، ومسلم في باب الحج عن العاجز لزمانه وهرم ونحوهما أو للموت، رقم: ۱۳۳۴ ، والترمذي في باب ما جاء في الحج عن الشيخ الكبير والميت، رقم: ۹۲۸ وأبوداود في باب الرجل يحج عن غيره، رقم ۱۸۰۹ ، والنسائي في باب حج المرأة عن الرجل، رقم: ٣٦٤١، وابن ماجه في باب الحج عن الحي إذا لم يستطع، رقم ۲۹۰۹ ، وأحمد في مسنده" ۲۱/۱) عن عبد الله بن عباس للماء
Fourth Investigation on Qiyas. Chapter on the Authority of Qiyas: Qiyas is a proof among the proofs of the Law, and acting upon it is obligatory when there is no higher evidence in the incident. Reports and traditions have come regarding this. He (the Prophet) said to Mu'adh ibn Jabal, may Allah be pleased with him, when he sent him to Yemen: 'By what will you judge, O Mu'adh?' He said: 'By the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' - Regarding the takbeers of Eid: The Companions differed concerning the takbeers of the two Eids. Some said: nine takbeers: three original: the takbeer of ihram, and the two takbeers of bowing in two rak'ahs, and six extra - this is the saying of Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, and it is the chosen view with us. Some said: thirteen: three original and ten extra, five in the first and five in the second - this is the saying of Ibn 'Abbas, and it is the madhhab of al-Shafi'i. Some said: fifteen: three original and twelve extra, six in each rak'ah. As is known: meaning if the Imam begins the Eid prayer while he holds the view of Ibn 'Abbas, then prays, then his opinion changes and he adopts the view of Ibn Mas'ud, he acts on it in the future because the takbeers admit of transition, so it is possible to transfer a ruling from one madhhab to another like abrogation of a text, and he does not repeat what is past because it occurred validly. This is from al-Ma'dan. In qiyas: it is transferring a ruling from the original to the branch by a common effective cause (illah) between them, and it is not grasped by mere language. Acting upon it is obligatory. This is the madhhab of all the Companions, Successors, and scholars of the Ummah in every age, contrary to some people of whims such as the Rawafid and Khawarij. Because Allah said: 'And We have sent down to you the Book as an explanation of everything' (16:89), so there is no need for qiyas. The answer: that qiyas reveals what is in the Book and is not contrary to it, so what is established is actually qiyas. And because Allah said: 'If you dispute concerning anything, refer it to Allah and the Messenger' (4:59). They said: it is obligatory to refer the disputed matter to the Book and Sunnah, not qiyas. It was answered: that referring the disputed to the explicit text is only by exemplification, i.e., seeking similarity between the original and the branch and building upon it, which is qiyas. This is supported by the command to refer after the command to obey Allah and His Messenger, for it indicates that rulings are of three types: established by the Book and Sunnah, and established by referring to them by way of qiyas. This is from al-Baydawi. Ibn Jabal etc. And Abu Musa al-Ash'ari said when he was sent to Yemen: 'Judge by the Book of Allah; if you do not find, then by the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah; if you do not find, then exert your opinion.' And 'Ali said to Ibn Mas'ud: 'Judge by the Book and Sunnah if you find them; if you do not find the ruling in them, then exert your opinion.' This is from Kashf al-Manar. For Mu'adh. [Page 202] He said: 'If you do not find' he said: 'I will exert my opinion.' So the Messenger of Allah approved him and said: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what He loves and is pleased with.' And it is narrated that a woman from Khath'am came to the Messenger of Allah and said: 'My father is a very old man; the obligation of Hajj has reached him but he cannot hold himself on the riding animal. Would it be sufficient for me to perform Hajj on his behalf?' He (the Prophet) said: 'Do you think that if your father had a debt and you paid it, would it be sufficient for him?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'So the debt of Allah is more deserving and prior.' The Messenger of Allah likened Hajj for a decrepit old man to financial rights, and pointed to an effective cause. His approval etc.: His approval of Mu'adh and his praise of Allah is clear evidence for the permissibility of acting on qiyas when there is no text from the Book and Sunnah. For if qiyas were not a proof requiring action after the Book and Sunnah, he would have objected to him. In the hadith there is strong evidence for the permissibility of qiyas and a refutation of those who deny it entirely. al-Tirmidhi said in his Jami': 'We do not know this hadith except from this chain, and its chain is not continuous according to him.' I say: such a defect is not a considered defect, because interruption in the first three centuries is like reliability with us trustworthy scholars. This hadith is considered by the scholars of usul to be mashhur, rising above ahad. al-Ghazali said: then the Ummah received it with acceptance, so it became like mutawatir. There is no doubt it is mashhur. And Allah knows best. 'Praise be to Allah who...' etc. For if qiyas were not a proof requiring action after the Book and Sunnah, the Messenger of Allah would have objected to him. And when he praised him and thanked Allah for guiding Mu'adh to action and ijtihad, it indicates that it is a proof requiring action when there is no text from the Book and Sunnah. This is from al-Ma'dan. 'Ahujja': with fatha on the hamza and damma on the ha, meaning 'I enter ihram and perform the actions on his behalf' – this is the well-known narration.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage opens the fourth investigation on Qiyas, specifically its authority (hujjiyah). The author defines qiyas as a valid proof of Sharia that must be acted upon when no higher evidence exists. He then provides scriptural proofs, most notably the hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal, where the Prophet (SAW) approved his intention to use ijtihad/ra'y when no text is found. The story of the Khath'ami woman further illustrates analogical reasoning: the Prophet likened Hajj on behalf of an incapable person to paying a debt. The passage also addresses and refutes objections from those who deny qiyas, such as the Rawafid and Khawarij, who claim that the Quran is sufficient. The author responds that qiyas merely uncovers what is already in the Book and is not contrary to it. Additionally, the text discusses the ikhtilaf of Sahaba on Eid takbeers as an example of ijtihad, though this appears to be a digression. The overall emphasis is that qiyas is a legitimate and necessary source of law, supported by consensus of the Companions and later scholars.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Transferring a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') by virtue of a shared effective cause (illah) that is not purely linguistic.
حجية (hujjiyah): The quality of being a proof (hujjah) that must be acted upon in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary proof (dalil) the author uses to establish qiyas as a hujjah?
A) The verse 'Today I have perfected your religion' (5:3)
B) The hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal and the Prophet's approval
C) The consensus of the Sahaba on takbeers of Eid
D) The story of Adam learning names of all things

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school affirms qiyas as a necessary and binding source of law, supported by the Prophet's approval and the consensus of the Companions.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Proof of Qiyas from the Hadith of Mu'adh and the Khath'ami Woman
Two hadith proofs for Qiyas with chain defense

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the textual evidence for the authority of Qiyas in Hanafi usul and apply the istinbat chain to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
The Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's ijtihad and his own analogical reasoning establish Qiyas as a binding source of law.

This lesson examines two hadith that form the primary textual evidence for the authority of Qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul. The Mu'adh hadith shows the Prophet's explicit endorsement of ijtihad when texts are absent, while the Khath'ami hadith demonstrates the Prophet himself using Qiyas. We will analyze these proofs and respond to a chain criticism, thereby strengthening the proof for Qiyas as a hujja.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two hadith proofs
Locate the Mu'adh hadith and the Khath'ami woman hadith in the source. Note that both are used to justify Qiyas.
2
Analyze the Mu'adh hadith
Examine the dialogue: Mu'adh states he will use Quran, then Sunnah, then exert his own opinion. The Prophet approves and praises him. This indicates that ijtihad (including Qiyas) is valid when no text is found.
The explicit approval (taqrir) is a strong proof.
3
Extract the legal principle
The Prophet's approval shows that Qiyas is a binding proof (hujja). If it were invalid, the Prophet would have objected.
4
Examine the Khath'ami hadith
The Prophet analogizes the obligation of Hajj for an elderly man to a financial debt. This is a direct example of Qiyas used by the Prophet himself, strengthening the proof.
The effective cause (illa) is the idea of 'settling a debt' (qada').
5
Address the chain criticism
Al-Tirmidhi criticized the Mu'adh hadith for discontinuity. The author argues that such discontinuity is not a defect because the narrators are trustworthy and the hadith is mashhur (well-known) and accepted by the ummah.
This defense upholds the hadith's authority.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في حجية القياس
قال: "فإن لم تجد" قال: أجتهد برأيي فصوبه رسولُ الله عليه فقال: "الحمد الله الذي وفق رسول رسول الله على ما يُحبُّ ويَرْضاه" ورُوي أن امرأةً خثعمية أتت إلى رسول الله الله فقالت: إن أبي كان شيخاً كبيراً أدركه رسول الحج ولا يَسْتمْسك على الراحلة أفيُجْزِتُنِي أَنْ أحُجَّ عنه؟ قال علي: " أرأيت لو كان على أبيك دَيْنٌ فقضيته أما كان يجزتُك" فقالت: بلى، فقال علي: "فَدَيْنُ الله أَحَقُّ وأولى .. ألحق رسول الله علي الحجّ في حق الشيخ الفاني بالحقوق المالية، وأشار إلى علة مؤثرة في الجواز وهي "القضاء" وهذا هو القياس. فصوبه إلخ: فتصويبه لمعاذ الله وحمده الله تعالى دليل صريح على جواز العمل بالقياس عند فقدان النص من الكتاب والسنة، فإنه لو لم يكن القياس حجة موجبة للعمل بعد الكتاب والسنة لأنكره عليه، وفي الحديث دلالة قوية على جواز القياس ورد قبيح على من أنكرها أصلاً . قال الترمذي في "جامعه": هذا حديث لا نعرفه إلا من هذا الوجه، وليس إسناده عنده بمتصل، قلت: وبمثل هذا الجرح ليس جرحاً معتبراً، فإن الانقطاع من القرون الثلاثة كالعدل عندنا الثقاة هذا الحديث عده أهل الأصول من المشاهير مرتقياً من الآحاد، وقال الغزالي: من ثم تلقته الأمة بالقبول فصار كالمتواتر فلا شك في كونه من المشاهير والله اعلم. الحمد لله الذي إلخ فلو لم يكن القياس حجة موجبة للعمل بعد الكتاب والسنة لأنكر عليه رسول الله ، وإذا مدحه به حمد الله بتوفيقه لمعاذ بالعمل والاجتهاد دل على أنه حجة موجبة للعمل عند عدم النص من الكتاب والسنة كذا في "المعدن". أحُجَّ : بفتح الهمزة وضم الحاء أي: أحرم وأودي الأفعال عنه هذا المشهور من الرواية.
Chapter on the Authority of Qiyas. He said: 'If you do not find [in the texts],' he said: 'I will exert my own opinion,' and the Messenger of Allah approved him, saying: 'Praise be to Allah who has guided the messenger of the Messenger of Allah to what He loves and is pleased with.' And it is narrated that a Khath'ami woman came to the Messenger of Allah and said: 'My father is a very old man, he has been overtaken by the obligation of Hajj and cannot stay on the mount. Will it suffice for me to perform Hajj on his behalf?' He said: 'Do you think that if your father had a debt and you paid it, would that suffice him?' She said: 'Yes.' He said: 'Then the debt of Allah is more deserving of being fulfilled.' The Messenger of Allah analogized Hajj for the old man to financial obligations, and pointed to an effective cause for permissibility, which is 'settling the debt.' This is Qiyas. His approval etc.: His approval of Mu'adh and Allah's praise of him is clear evidence for the permissibility of acting upon Qiyas when there is no text from the Book and Sunnah. For if Qiyas were not a binding proof after the Book and Sunnah, he would have objected to it. And in this hadith there is strong indication of the permissibility of Qiyas and a rebuttal against those who deny it entirely. Al-Tirmidhi said in his Jami': 'We do not know this hadith except from this chain, and its isnad is not continuous according to him.' I say: Such a criticism is not a valid defect. For discontinuity from the three generations is like reliability with us regarding trustworthy narrators. This hadith is considered by the scholars of usul as well-known (mashhur), rising above the level of ahad. Al-Ghazali said: The ummah received it with acceptance, so it became like mutawatir. There is no doubt it is among the mashhur. And Allah knows best. 'Praise be to Allah...' etc. For if Qiyas were not a binding proof after the Book and Sunnah, the Messenger of Allah would have objected to him. And when he praised him and thanked Allah for guiding Mu'adh to acting and ijtihad, it indicates that Qiyas is a binding proof at the absence of text from the Book and Sunnah. As in al-Ma'din. 'Ahujja': with fatha on the hamza and damma on the ha, meaning: I assume ihram and perform the actions on his behalf. This is the well-known recitation.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on the authority of Qiyas (analogical reasoning) as a source of Islamic law. The author presents two hadith proofs. First, the famous hadith of Mu'adh ibn Jabal when the Prophet sent him to Yemen. The Prophet asked him how he would judge, and Mu'adh replied that he would first use the Quran, then the Sunnah, and then exert his own opinion (ijtihad). The Prophet approved of this, indicating that ijtihad through Qiyas is valid after exhausting textual sources. The author emphasizes that if Qiyas were not a valid proof, the Prophet would have objected. Second, the hadith of the Khath'ami woman asking about Hajj on behalf of her elderly father. The Prophet analogized Hajj to financial debts, showing that Qiyas was used by the Prophet himself. The author then addresses a criticism from al-Tirmidhi regarding the chain of the Mu'adh hadith. The author defends the hadith, arguing that its discontinuity is not a fatal flaw because the narrators are trustworthy, and the hadith is considered mashhur (well-known) and accepted by the ummah, giving it strength. The passage establishes that Qiyas is a binding proof (hujja) when there is no explicit text from the Quran or Sunnah.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction: applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause (illa).
حجة (hujja): A proof that is binding in law; something that must be acted upon.
اجتهاد (ijtihad): Independent reasoning to derive a ruling from the sources; includes Qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet do when Mu'adh said he would exert his own opinion?
A) He objected and told him to only use texts.
B) He approved and praised him.
C) He remained silent.
D) He ordered him to follow the opinion of the Companions.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's approval of Mu'adh's ijtihad and his own use of Qiyas in the Khath'ami hadith establish Qiyas as a binding source of law in the absence of explicit texts.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Proof of Qiyas from the Hadith of Touching the Penis
Using the hadith 'هل هو إلا بضعة منك' as evidence for Qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify how the Prophet used Qiyas in the hadith of touching the penis, analyze the chain of transmission and authentication, and evaluate the Hanafi preference over the Shafi'i hadith of Busra.

Core Idea
The Prophet himself used Qiyas when he analogized the penis to any other body part, proving Qiyas is a valid source.

This lesson explores a key hadith that demonstrates the Prophet’s use of analogical reasoning (Qiyas). The passage from Usul al-Shashi presents the hadith of Qays ibn Talq as a proof that Qiyas is a legitimate source of Islamic law, and it also engages with a madhhab dispute regarding whether touching the penis nullifies wudu. By the end, you will understand how the Hanafi school uses this hadith to argue for the authority of Qiyas and to prefer their position over that of the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dalil and its type
Locate the hadith of Qays ibn Talq in the passage. Recognize that it is a hadith ahad (solitary) but has been authenticated by multiple scholars.
The hadith is narrated in Sunan Abi Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasai, and Muwatta Muhammad.
2
Extract the Qiyas used by the Prophet
Analyze the Prophet's response: 'هل هو إلا بضعة منه' (Is it not just a piece of him?). Understand that this is a rhetorical question that draws an analogy between the penis and any other body part.
The effective cause (illa) is that all body parts are alike; touching any part does not nullify wudu.
3
Examine the authentication and tarjih
Note the multiple narrations (Sunan, Muwatta, Sahih Ibn Hibban) and the statements of Tirmidhi, Tahawi, and others. See how the Hanafi scholar Ibn al-Humam argues that men's narrations are stronger than women's due to perceived superior memory.
This tarjih is used to prefer the hadith of Qays (man) over the hadith of Busra (woman) which claims the opposite.
4
Understand the madhhab dispute
Contrast the Hanafi position (no wudu required after touching the penis) with the Shafi'i position (wudu required), based on the hadith of Busra.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the practical ruling on wudu nullification.
5
Conclude the use of Qiyas
The passage states 'وهذا هو القياس' (This is Qiyas). Recognize that the Prophet himself performed Qiyas, thereby establishing its validity as a source of law.

البحث الرابع في القياس
فصل في حجية القياس
وروى ابن الصبّاغ - وهو من سادات أصحاب الشافعي لله - في كتابه المسمى "بالشامل" عن قيس بن طَلْقٍ بن علي أنه قال: جاء رَجُلٌ إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كأنه بدوي، فقال: يا نبي الله ما ترى في مس الرَّجُل ذكره بعدما توضاً؟ فقال: "هل هو إلا بضعة منه" *، وهذا هو القياس.
بلى: الفرق بين "بلى" و "نعم": أن موجب "نعم" تصديق ما قبله من الكلام منفياً كان أو مثبتاً، استفهاماً كان أو خبراً كما إذا قيل لك: أقام زيد أو لم يقم، فقلت: نعم كان تصديقاً لما قبله، وتخصيصاً لما بعد الهمزة، وموجب "بلي" إيجاب ما بعد النفي استفهاماً كان أو خبراً، فإذا قيل: لم يقم زيد، فقلت: "بلي" كان معناه قد قام، وقد يستعمل أحدهما مكان الآخر. وهذا: أي إلحاق الحج بالحقوق المالية مع بيان العلة المؤثرة المشتركة وهي "القضاء". وروى ابن الصباغ إلخ أقول: وأيضاً روى هذا الحديث أصحاب السنن إلا ابن ماجه عن ملازم بن عمرو عن بن بدر عن قيس بن طلق بن علي عن أبيه عن النبي أنه سئل عن الرجل يمس ذكره في الصلاة، فقال: "هل هو إلا بضعة منك"، ورواه ابن حبان في صحيحه ، وقال الترمذي: هذا الحديث أحسن شيء يروى في هذا الباب وفي الباب عن أبي إمامة، وروى محمد بن الحسن الشيباني في "موطاه" قال: أخبرنا أيوب بن التيمي قاضي اليمامة من قيس بن طلق أن أباه حدثه أن رجلاً سأل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن رجل مس ذكره أيتوضأ قال: "هل هو إلا بضعة من جسدك. ورواه محمد بن الحسن الشيباني في "موطاه" وابن حبان في "صحيحه" وقال الطحاوي مستقيم الإسناد، وروي أن عمر ه سأل النبي عليه عن قبلة الصائم، فقال: "لو تمضمضت ثم محجت كان يضرك"، وعمل الصحابة ومناظراتهم في القياس أشهر من أن يخفى
بضعة منه إلخ: وفي رواية: مضغة منه أي مسه كمس عضو وجزء آخر من البدن في عدم الحدث، قال الفلاس ليه : هو أثبت عندي من حديث بسرة، قال ابن الهمام ويترجح أيضاً بأن حديث الرجال أقوى من حديث النساء لنقصان في الحفظ والضبط والعقل، ولهذا جعلت شهادة امرأتين كشهادة رجل واحد، فثبت من هذا الحديث
Fourth Topic: on Qiyas. Chapter on the Authority of Qiyas. Ibn al-Sabbagh – who is from the leading companions of al-Shafi'i – narrated in his book called al-Shamil from Qays ibn Talq ibn Ali: A man came to the Messenger of Allah, appearing to be a Bedouin, and said: 'O Prophet of Allah, what do you think about a man touching his penis after performing wudu?' He said: 'Is it not just a piece of him?' This is Qiyas. 'Bala': The difference between 'bala' and 'na'am' is that 'na'am' affirms what precedes it, whether negated or affirmed, whether interrogative or declarative. For example, if it is said to you: 'Did Zaid stand?' or 'Did he not stand?' and you say 'na'am', it affirms what precedes it and specifies what follows the question word. The function of 'bala' is to affirm what comes after negation, whether interrogative or declarative. So if it is said: 'Zaid did not stand,' and you say 'bala', it means he stood. Sometimes one is used in place of the other. And this: i.e., analogy of Hajj to financial rights with an explanation of the effective cause which is 'settling the debt'. Ibn al-Sabbagh narrated etc. I say: Also, the authors of the Sunan except Ibn Majah narrated this hadith from Mulazim ibn Amr from Ibn Badr from Qays ibn Talq ibn Ali from his father from the Prophet that he was asked about a man touching his penis during prayer, and he said: 'Is it not just a piece of you?' Ibn Hibban narrated it in his Sahih. Al-Tirmidhi said: 'This is the best thing narrated on this topic, and on this topic from Abu Umamah.' Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani narrated in his Muwatta' from Ayyub ibn al-Taymi, judge of Yamamah, from Qays ibn Talq that his father told him that a man asked the Messenger of Allah about a man who touched his penis – does he need to perform wudu? – and he said: 'Is it not just a piece of your body?' Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani narrated it in his Muwatta', and Ibn Hibban in his Sahih. Al-Tahawi said: Its chain is sound. And it is narrated that 'Umar asked the Prophet about kissing while fasting, and he said: 'If you were to rinse your mouth and then spit it out, would it harm you?' And the practice of the Companions and their debates using Qiyas are too well-known to be hidden. 'A piece of him' etc.: In another narration: 'a piece of flesh', meaning that touching it is like touching any other limb of the body in terms of not nullifying wudu. Al-Fallas said: It is more authentic to me than the hadith of Busra. Ibn al-Humam said: It is also preferable because the hadith of men is stronger than the hadith of women due to deficiency in memory, accuracy, and intellect. For this reason, the testimony of two women is made equal to that of one man. So it is established from this hadith...
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage continues the chapter on the authority of Qiyas. It presents a third hadith proof: the hadith of Qays ibn Talq from his father, where a man asked the Prophet about touching his penis after wudu. The Prophet replied, 'Is it not just a piece of him?' meaning that it is like any other body part and does not break wudu. The author points out that this is Qiyas: the Prophet analogized the penis to other body parts based on the common characteristic of being part of the body. The passage also includes a linguistic note on the difference between 'bala' and 'na'am', though this seems less central. Then it returns to the Khath'ami hadith's analogy, connecting the effective cause of 'settling the debt.' It then provides extensive authentication for the hadith of touching the penis, citing multiple narrations and scholars who deemed it sound, including al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Hibban, al-Tahawi, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The author argues that this hadith is stronger than the hadith of Busra (a hadith narrated by a woman that says touching the penis breaks wudu), because men's narrations are given more weight due to perceived strengths in memory and intellect. This is a Hanafi position that favors this hadith over the opposing one. The passage firmly establishes that Qiyas was used by the Prophet and is thus a valid source of law.

Key Terms
بضعة (bida'a): A piece, part, or limb of the body.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause (illa).
مَنْطُوق (mantuq): Explicit speech: the literal meaning that is directly conveyed by the words.

The Prophet's use of Qiyas in the hadith of touching the penis establishes Qiyas as a valid source of Islamic law, and the Hanafi school prefers this hadith over the Shafi'i hadith of Busra, resulting in the ruling that touching the penis does not nullify wudu.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
The Authority of Qiyas (Hujjiyat al-Qiyas) and the Ruling on Touching the Penis
Proving qiyas via hadith and applying it to wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the prophetic hadith used to prove qiyas, explain the Hanafi qiyas argument for the ruling on touching the penis, and compare it with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The Prophet's rhetorical question 'Is it anything but a piece of you?' is a direct use of qiyas, establishing its validity as a source of law.

This lesson delves into the Hanafi proof for the authority of qiyas (analogical reasoning) by examining a specific hadith where the Prophet himself performed an analogy. The passage also illustrates the practical application of qiyas by deriving the ruling that touching the penis does not break wudu, and contrasts the Hanafi view with that of the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of qiyas proof
Locate the hadith of Qays ibn Talq in the passage and recognise it as a prophetic use of analogy. The Prophet's response 'هل هو إلا بضعة منه' (Is it anything but a piece of him?) is the core evidence.
This hadith is narrated through multiple chains, including by Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Muhammad al-Shaybani in his Muwatta.
2
Analyse the qiyas structure
Break down the analogy: the original case (asl) is any other body part, which does not break wudu when touched; the branch (far') is the penis; the common cause (illah) is the absence of impurity (najasa). Hence, touching the penis does not break wudu.
The Hanafi school classifies this as qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) because the illah is evident.
3
Understand the tarjih between conflicting hadiths
The Shafi'i school relies on the hadith of Busra ('من مس ذكره فليتوضأ') to require wudu. The Hanafi response argues that the hadith of Qays is stronger in chain (rijal vs. nisa') and that the testimony of two women equals that of one man in Islamic law, so the male narrators' version is preferred.
Ibn al-Humam and al-Tahawi both support this preference.
4
Derive the fiqh ruling and note the madhhab difference
Applying the qiyas, the Hanafi ruling is that wudu is not invalidated by touching the penis. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is clear: a Hanafi does not need to renew wudu, while a Shafi'i does.
The passage also notes that the majority of Companions (Umar, Ali, Zayd ibn Thabit, etc.) held the Hanafi view.

البحث الرابع في القياس الجواز وهي "القضاء" وهذا هو القياس. فصل في حجية القياس وروى ابن الصبّاغ - وهو من سادات أصحاب الشافعي - في كتابه المسمى "بالشامل" عن قيس بن طَلْقٍ بن علي أنه قال: جاء رَجُلٌ إلى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كأنه بدوي، فقال: يا نبي الله ما ترى في مَس الرَّجُل ذكره بعدما توضأ؟ فقال: "هل هو إلا بضعة منه" *، وهذا هو القياس. بلى: الفرق بين "بلى" و "نعم": أن موجب "نعم" تصديق ما قبله من الكلام منفياً كان أو مثبتاً، استفهاماً كان أو خبراً كما إذا قيل لك: أقام زيد أو لم يقم، فقلت: نعم كان تصديقاً لما قبله، وتخصيصاً لما بعد الهمزة، وموجب "بلى" إيجاب ما بعد النفي استفهاماً كان أو خبراً، فإذا قيل: لم يقم زيد، فقلت: "بلى" كان معناه قد قام، وقد يستعمل أحدهما مكان الآخر. وهذا: أي إلحاق الحج بالحقوق المالية مع بيان العلة المؤثرة المشتركة وهي "القضاء". وروى ابن الصباغ إلخ أقول: وأيضاً روى هذا الحديث أصحاب السنن إلا ابن ماجه عن ملازم بن عمرو عن ابن بدر عن قيس بن طلق بن علي عن أبيه عن النبي ﷺ أنه سئل عن الرجل يمس ذكره في الصلاة، فقال: "هل هو إلا بضعة منك"، ورواه ابن حبان في صحيحه، وقال الترمذي: هذا الحديث أحسن شيء يروى في هذا الباب، وفي الباب عن أبي أمامة، وروى محمد بن الحسن الشيباني في "موطاه" قال: أخبرنا أيوب بن التيمي قاضي اليمامة عن قيس بن طلق أن أباه حدثه أن رجلاً سأل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن رجل مس ذكره أيتوضأ قال: "هل هو إلا بضعة من جسدك". ورواه محمد بن الحسن الشيباني في "موطاه" وابن حبان في "صحيحه" وقال الطحاوي: مستقيم الإسناد. وروي أن عمر سأل النبي ﷺ عن قبلة الصائم، فقال: "لو تمضمضت ثم مججته كان يضرك"، وعمل الصحابة ومناظراتهم في القياس أشهر من أن يخفى. بضعة منه إلخ: وفي رواية: مضغة منه أي مسه كمس عضو وجزء آخر من البدن في عدم الحدث، قال الفلاس: هو أثبت عندي من حديث بسرة، قال ابن الهمام ويترجح أيضاً بأن حديث الرجال أقوى من حديث النساء لنقصان في الحفظ والضبط والعقل، ولهذا جعلت شهادة امرأتين كشهادة رجل واحد، فثبت من هذا الحديث أنه لا ينقض الوضوء من مس الذكر، وهو مذهبنا، وهو قول عمر وعلي وزيد بن ثابت وحذيفة وعمران بن حصين وأبي الدرداء وأبي هريرة وسعد بن أبي وقاص، وقال الطحاوي: لا نعلم أحداً من الصحابة أفتى بالوضوء منه غير ابن عمر، وقد خالفه أكثرهم فيه، قال الشافعي وأحمد وداود: يجب الوضوء منه، واختلف أصحاب مالك فيه، وقال الترمذي: هو قول غير واحد من الصحابة والتابعين، وبه يقول أحمد والأوزاعي والشافعي وإسحاق وغيرهم كذا في "الحصول". وهذا هو القياس: لأنه قاس هذا العضو على سائر الأعضاء لا ينقض الوضوء فكذا هذا، والجامع هو عدم النجاسة كذا في "المعدن". * أخرجه أبو داود في باب الرخصة في ذلك أي مس الذكر، رقم: ۱۸۲، والترمذي في باب ما جاء في ترك الوضوء من مس الذكر، رقم ٨٥، والنسائي في باب ترك الوضوء من ذلك، رقم: ١٦٥ عن قيس بن طلق بن علي.
The fourth research on qiyas: permissibility, and it is 'al-qada' (judgment). This is qiyas. Section on the authority of qiyas: Ibn al-Sabbagh, one of the leading followers of al-Shafi'i, narrated in his book called 'al-Shamil' from Qays ibn Talq ibn Ali that he said: A man came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) as if he was a Bedouin, and said: O Prophet of Allah, what do you see regarding a man touching his penis after performing wudu? He said: 'Is it anything but a piece of him?' This is qiyas. Bala: the difference between 'bala' and 'na'am' is that the force of 'na'am' is to affirm what precedes it, whether negated or affirmed, interrogative or declarative, as when it is said to you: Did Zayd stand or not? And you said: 'Na'am' it affirms what preceded it and specifies what follows the interrogative particle. The force of 'bala' is to affirm what follows a negation, whether interrogative or declarative. So when it is said: Zayd did not stand, you say: 'Bala', meaning he did stand. Sometimes one is used in place of the other. And this: meaning annexing the proof to financial rights with explanation of the effective common cause, which is 'al-qada'. And Ibn al-Sabbagh etc. I say: Also, the compilers of the Sunan except Ibn Majah narrated this hadith from Mulazim ibn Amr from Ibn Badr from Qays ibn Talq ibn Ali from his father from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he was asked about a man touching his penis during prayer, and he said: 'Is it anything but a piece of you?' Ibn Hibban narrated it in his Sahih, and al-Tirmidhi said: This hadith is the best thing narrated on this topic, and on the topic from Abu Umamah. Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani narrated in his Muwatta: he said: Ayyub ibn al-Taymi, the judge of al-Yamamah, informed us from Qays ibn Talq that his father told him that a man asked the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) about a man who touched his penis: should he perform wudu? He said: 'Is it anything but a piece of your body?' Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani narrated it in his Muwatta, and Ibn Hibban in his Sahih, and al-Tahawi said: its chain is sound. It is narrated that Umar asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about a fasting person kissing, and he said: 'If you rinsed your mouth and then spat it out, would it harm you?' The practice of the Companions and their debates on qiyas are too famous to be hidden. 'Bid'a minhu etc.' In one narration: 'mudgha minhu' meaning his touching it is like touching any other limb of the body in not causing impurity. Al-Fallas said: It is more authentic to me than the hadith of Busra. Ibn al-Humam said: It is also preponderant because the hadith of men is stronger than the hadith of women due to deficiency in memory, accuracy, and intellect; for this reason the testimony of two women is made equivalent to the testimony of one man. So it is established from this hadith that touching the penis does not invalidate wudu, and this is our school, and it is the saying of Umar, Ali, Zayd ibn Thabit, Hudhayfah, Imran ibn Husayn, Abu al-Darda, Abu Hurayra, and Sad ibn Abi Waqqas. Al-Tahawi said: We do not know any Companion who gave a fatwa requiring wudu for it other than Ibn Umar, and the majority opposed him. Al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and Dawud said: Wudu is required for it. The companions of Malik differed on it. Al-Tirmidhi said: It is the saying of many Companions and Successors, and Ahmad, al-Awza'i, al-Shafi'i, Ishaq, and others hold it, as in 'al-Husul'. And this is qiyas: because he analogized this organ to the rest of the organs that do not invalidate wudu, so this is similar, and the commonality is the absence of impurity, as in 'al-Madin'.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This is a key passage in Hanafi usul proving the authority of qiyas. The text begins by defining qiyas analogical reasoning. It then presents a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) used qiyas himself: when asked about touching the penis after wudu, he replied, 'Is it anything but a piece of him?' implying that just as touching any other body part does not break wudu, touching the penis likewise does not. The commentator then discusses the linguistic distinction between 'bala' and 'na'am', clarifying that 'bala' is used to affirm a negation. This grammatical note serves to explain the precise meaning of the Prophet's response. The passage then provides multiple chains of transmission for the hadith, strengthening its authenticity. It quotes al-Tahawi's validation of the chain and mentions that this hadith is stronger than the hadith of Busra, which the Shafi'is use to argue for wudu. The Hanafi position is that touching the penis does not nullify wudu, and this is supported by the analogy to other body parts, with the illah being the absence of impurity (najasa). The text also records the disagreement among scholars, noting that the Shafi'is and Hanbalis require wudu, while the majority of Companions are with the Hanafi view. The passage concludes by reinforcing that this ruling is derived through qiyas, making it a practical example of using analogy in Islamic law.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): إلحاق حكم فرع بأصل بعلة مشتركة (annexing a branch to an original ruling via a common cause)
بلى (bala): أداة تستعمل لإيجاب ما بعد النفي (a particle used to affirm what follows a negation)
بضعة (bid'a): قطعة من اللحم (a piece of flesh/body part)
علة (illah): الوصف الذي يترتب عليه الحكم (the attribute upon which the ruling is based)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's use of analogy in the hadith of Qays ibn Talq establishes qiyas as a valid source of law, and applying this qiyas yields the Hanafi ruling that touching the penis does not break wudu.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
First Two Conditions for Valid Qiyas
Listing and explaining the first two conditions for qiyas validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first two conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul and apply them to evaluate whether a given qiyas is valid.

Core Idea
Qiyas cannot contradict a clear text; it must operate within the bounds of revelation.

This lesson introduces the foundational discipline of qiyas in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. After a concrete example from the Companion Ibn Mas'ud, the text lists the first two conditions that ensure qiyas remains a controlled tool of reasoning, not arbitrary opinion. Understanding these conditions is essential for any mujtahid or student of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule's context
The passage opens with a practical case from Ibn Mas'ud. Note that this illustrates the proper use of qiyas when no explicit text exists.
Ibn Mas'ud's ijtihad is an example of applying qiyas correctly.
2
State the first condition
Qiyas must not oppose a clear text (nass). A 'nass' includes the Quran, mutawatir hadith, ahad hadith from jurist narrators, and Companions' statements on matters not subject to opinion.
If qiyas contradicts any of these, it is invalid.
3
State the second condition
Qiyas must not be contradictory to another text. The 'change' (taghyir) prohibited is altering the linguistic meaning of a text, not the necessary generalization from specific to general (which is inherent in qiyas).
Generalizing a ruling is allowed and even required in qiyas.
4
Apply the conditions to the example
Ibn Mas'ud's qiyas for mahr al-mithl did not oppose any text because no explicit ruling existed for that specific case, so it satisfied both conditions.
5
Note the remaining conditions
There are five conditions total; this lesson covers the first two. The others will be addressed in subsequent lessons.

فصل في شروط صحة القياس وسُئِلَ ابنُ مسعود عمَّن تزوج امرأةً ولم يُسَمَّ لها مهراً وقد مات عنها زوجها قبل الدخول، فاستَمْهَل شهراً ثُمَّ قال: أجتهد فيه برأيي، فإن كان صواباً فمن الله، وإن كان خطأً فمن ابن أم عبد، فقال أرى لها مهر مثل نسائها لا وكس فيها ولا شطط. فصل في شروط صحة القياس: شروط صحة القياس خمسة: أحدها: أن لا يكون في مقابلة النص. والثاني: أن لا يكون القياس معارضا له. فيه خروج ابن أم عبد: هو كنية ابن مسعود من قبل أمه؛ إذ أمه أم عبد وهو على قوله تعالى: مَا أَصَابَكَ مِنْ حَسَنَةٍ فَمِنَ الله وَمَا أَصَابَكَ مِنْ سَيِّئَة فَمِنْ نَفْسِكَ. أحدها إلخ أي الأول أن لا يكون القياس الظني الذي له شبه من الرأي معارضاً ومنافياً للنص الصحيح المعمول به كالآية، وخبر الراوي الفقيه أو مطلقاً على ما حققنا، وكذا بإزاء قول الصحابي فيما لا يدرك عندنا كذا في "الحصول". والثاني إلخ والمراد بالتغيير: تغير المعنى المفهوم من النص لغة دون التغيير الحاصل من الخصوص إلى العموم، فإنه من ضروريات التعليق؛ إذ لا فائدة فيه إلا تعميم حكم النص كذا في بعض الحواشي.
Section on the conditions for the validity of qiyas. Ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married a woman without specifying a dower, and her husband died before consummation. He asked for a month's delay, then said: I will exert my own opinion in it. If it is correct, it is from Allah; if it is error, it is from Ibn Umm Abd. He said: I think she is entitled to the mahr of her peers, without reduction or excess. Section on the conditions for the validity of qiyas: The conditions for the validity of qiyas are five: First: that it does not oppose a text. Second: that the qiyas is not contradictory to it. Therein is the issue of Ibn Umm Abd: he is the kunya of Ibn Mas'ud from his mother's side; his mother was Umm Abd, and this is according to His saying: 'Whatever good befalls you is from Allah, and whatever evil befalls you is from yourself.' 'First, etc.' meaning the first condition is that the probable qiyas that has a resemblance to opinion should not be in opposition and contradiction to a sound text that is acted upon, like the verse or the report of a jurist narrator, or absolutely as we have verified, and likewise in the presence of a Companion's statement in matters not subject to opinion, as in 'al-Husul'. 'Second, etc.' and what is meant by 'change' is the change in the meaning understood from the text linguistically, not the change resulting from specificity to generality, for that is a necessity of annexation; there is no benefit in it except generalizing the ruling of the text, as in some glosses.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage introduces the conditions for a valid qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul. It begins with an example from Ibn Mas'ud, who performed ijtihad to determine the mahr for a woman whose husband died before consummation without specifying a dower. He used qiyas to give her the mahr of her peers (mahr al-mithl). This story illustrates the proper use of qiyas. Then the text lists the first two conditions: (1) Qiyas must not contradict a clear text (nass), meaning it cannot oppose a definitive source like the Quran or mutawatir hadith, nor a report from a jurist narrator, nor a Companion's statement on matters not subject to ijtihad. (2) Qiyas must not be in opposition to another text, meaning the qiyas itself should not conflict with a valid textual ruling. The commentary explains that 'change' (taghyir) in the second condition refers to altering the linguistic meaning of a text, not the necessary generalization when annexing a ruling (since that is inherent in qiyas). The passage shows that qiyas is a disciplined tool, not arbitrary opinion, and must operate within the bounds of revelation.

Key Terms
نص (nass): النص الصحيح المعمول به (a sound authoritative text that is acted upon)
قياس ظني (qiyas zanni): القياس الذي له شبه من الرأي (qiyas that has a resemblance to opinion, i.e., probabilistic analogy)
تغيير (taghyir): تغير المعنى المفهوم من النص لغة (changing the meaning linguistically understood from the text)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the first condition for the validity of qiyas?
A) The qiyas must be based on a clear illah
B) The qiyas must not oppose a clear text
C) The qiyas must be accepted by the majority of scholars
D) The qiyas must be performed by a qualified mujtahid

Key Takeaway
The first two conditions for valid qiyas are that it must not oppose a definitive text and that it must not contradict another text—ensuring qiyas remains subordinate to revelation.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Five Conditions for the Validity of Qiyas
Lists and explains five conditions for valid analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five conditions for valid qiyas, apply them to a sample case, and compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i views on linguistic qiyas.

Core Idea
Qiyas is valid only if it does not oppose a text, does not alter the text's ruling, and uses a legal cause that is rationally intelligible.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi begins with a story of Ibn Mas'ud using ijtihad in a marriage case, demonstrating that qiyas is a legitimate tool when no clear text exists. It then lays down five essential conditions that every valid qiyas must satisfy. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly applying analogical reasoning in deriving legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five conditions
Read the list of five conditions in the passage. Write them down in order, noting the exact phrasing for each.
The first condition is the most fundamental: qiyas cannot oppose a clear text (nass).
2
Explain each condition
For each condition, paraphrase its meaning and explain what it prohibits or requires. Pay special attention to the second condition's distinction between changing the meaning of the text versus generalizing its ruling.
The commentary clarifies that 'changing a ruling' means altering the linguistic meaning, not the application to a broader set.
3
Distinguish ta'lil and qiyas
Identify the passage's discussion on the difference between causation (ta'lil) and qiyas. Note that ta'lil is the identification of the cause within a text, while qiyas is the extension of that cause to a new case.
This distinction is crucial: causation precedes qiyas in the reasoning process.
4
Analyze the dispute on linguistic qiyas
Read the passage's critique of linguistic qiyas attributed to some Shafi'i scholars. Identify the Hanafi position and the basis for rejecting linguistic qiyas as a source of legal rulings.
The Hanafi view is that qiyas only applies to legal rulings, not to linguistic definitions.
5
Evaluate the Ibn Mas'ud case using the conditions
Take the marriage case from the beginning of the passage. Test Ibn Mas'ud's reasoning against each of the five conditions to see why it was a valid qiyas.
Consider: was there a text? Did he change a ruling? Was the cause rationally intelligible? Was it legal? Was the cause extracted from a text?

صواباً فمن الله، وإن كان خطاً فمن ابن أم عبد، فقال أرى لها مهر مثل نسائها لا وكس فيها ولا شَطَطَ. قطط. الزيادة على مهر المثل فصل في شروط صحة القياس: شروط صحة القياس خمسة: أحدها: أن لا يكون في مقابلة الظني الذي له شبه من الرأي معارضاً ومنافياً للنص الصحيح المعمول به كالآية، وخبر الراوي الفقيه أو مطلقاً على ما حققنا، وكذا بإزاء قول الصحابي فيما لا يدرك عندنا كذا في "الحصول". والثاني إلخ والمراد بالتغيير: تغير المعنى المفهوم من النص لغة دون التغيير الحاصل من الخصوص إلى العموم، فإنه من ضروريات التعليق؛ إذ لا فائدة فيه إلا تعميم حكم النص كذا في بعض الحواشي. لا يكون المعدى حكماً إلخ ثابتاً بأحد الأصول الثلاثة، وفيه إشارة إلى أن حكم الأصل لا يجوز أن يكون ثابتاً بالقياس؛ لأنه إن اتحدت العلة بالقياسين فذكر الواسطة ضائع وإن لم يتحد بطل أحد القياسين لابتنائه على غير العلة التي اعتبرها الشارع في الحكم كذا قيل. يَقَعَ التعليل إلخ الفرق بين التعليل والقياس بالاعتبار لا بالذات؛ لأن حكم مواضع النصوص إذا تعلل بعلة يسمى تعليلاً، وإذا تعدى الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع، وتقرر فيه يسمى قياساً، فيكون التعليل في الابتداء والقياس في الانتهاء كذا في "المعدن". لحكم شرعي إلخ لأن القياس حجة شرعية فيتعرف به الحكم الشرعي دون الحكم اللغوي؛ لأن الشيء إنما يعرف ما هو من بابه، ألا ترى أن الدلائل النحوية لا يعرف بها أحكام الشرع، فكذا بالقياس الشرعي لا يعرف إلا ما كان حكماً شرعياً، وعن ابن شريح وجماعة من أصحاب الشافعي: أنه يجوز إثبات الأسامي بالقياس اللغوي، ثم يترتب عليه الأحكام وهو مذهب أهل العربية، والدليل على فساد هذا النوع من القياس يأتي في المتن فانتظره كذا في "المعدن" أن لا يكون الفرع إلخ لأن التعدية إن كانت على وفاق النص الذي في الفرع فلا فائدة فيه؛ لأن النص يغني عنه، وإن كانت على خلافه فهو باطل لمناقضة حكم النص، وهذا مختار عامة المشايخ، وأما مختار مشائخ سمر قند الله أنه يجوز التعليل على موافقة النص وهو الأشبه؛ لأن فيه تأكيد النص على معنى أنه لولا النص لكان الحكم ثابتاً بالتعليل ولا مانع في الشرع والعقل عن تعاضد الأدلة وتأكد بعضها ببعض، فإن الشرع قد ورد بآيات كثيرة وأحاديث متعددة في حكم واحد وملأ السلف كتبهم بالتمسك بالنص والمعقول في حكم و لم ينقل عن أحد نكير، فكان إجماعاً على جوازه هذا توضيح كلام "المعدن".
The fourth research on qiyas. A chapter on the conditions for the validity of qiyas. Ibn Mas'ud was asked about a man who married a woman without specifying a dowry and then died before consummation. He waited a month and then said: I will exert my opinion in it; if it is correct, it is from Allah, and if it is wrong, it is from Ibn Umm Abd. He said: I think she is entitled to a dowry like the women of her peers, without excess or deficiency. The increase over the dowry of peers. Chapter on conditions for the validity of qiyas: The conditions for the validity of qiyas are five: First: that it does not oppose a text. Second: that it does not involve changing a ruling from the rulings of the text. Third: that the branch ruling is not something whose meaning is unintelligible. Fourth: that the causation is for a legal ruling, not a linguistic matter. Fifth: that the extraction of the cause from the branch is not specified by a text. An example of qiyas opposing a text: It is narrated that al-Hasan ibn Ziyad was asked about laughing out loud in prayer, and he said: ablution is nullified by it. The questioner said: if someone slanders a chaste person in prayer, it does not nullify... therein lies the departure of qiyas. Ibn Umm Abd: the kunya of Ibn Mas'ud from his mother; his mother is Umm Abd, and it is according to His statement: 'Whatever good befalls you is from Allah, and whatever evil befalls you is from yourself.' One of them etc., meaning the first is that the speculative qiyas that resembles opinion should not contradict or oppose a sound text that is acted upon, such as a verse, or the report of a jurist narrator, or absolutely according to what we have verified, and similarly against the statement of a Companion in matters not subject to reason, as in 'al-Husul'. The second etc., and what is meant by change is the change in the meaning understood from the text linguistically, not the change resulting from particular to general, for that is necessary for a conditional statement; there is no benefit in it except generalizing the ruling of the text, as in some glosses. The third condition is that the branch ruling is established by one of the three primary sources, and it indicates that the ruling of the original case cannot be established by qiyas; for if the cause is the same in both analogies, mentioning the intermediary is futile, and if it is not the same, one of the two analogies is invalid because it is based on a cause not considered by the Lawgiver in the ruling, as it is said. The fourth condition: The difference between causation and qiyas is by consideration not by essence; for when the ruling of a textual case is attached to a cause, it is called causation, and when the ruling is extended from the original to the branch and established there, it is called qiyas. Thus causation is at the beginning and qiyas at the end, as in 'al-Ma'dan'. For a legal ruling etc., because qiyas is a legal proof, and through it legal rulings are known, not linguistic rulings; for a thing is known only from its own category. Do you not see that grammatical proofs do not lead to legal rulings? Similarly, legal qiyas leads only to legal rulings. Ibn Shurayh and a group of Shafi'i scholars hold that it is permissible to establish names by linguistic qiyas, and then rulings follow from them, and this is the school of the grammarians. The proof of the invalidity of this type of qiyas will come in the text, so wait for it, as in 'al-Ma'dan'. The fifth condition: because if the extension is in accordance with the text in the branch, there is no benefit in it; the text suffices. If it is contrary to it, it is invalid due to contradiction of the text's ruling. This is the choice of the majority of scholars. As for the choice of the scholars of Samarkand, they permit causation in accordance with the text, and this is more appropriate; because it involves reinforcing the text, meaning that if not for the text, the ruling would be established by causation, and there is no legal or rational impediment to mutual support of proofs and reinforcement of one by another. Indeed, the law has come with many verses and multiple hadiths for a single ruling, and the predecessors filled their books with adherence to text and reason in a ruling, and no objection is reported from anyone; thus it is considered consensus on its permissibility. This is an explanation of the words of 'al-Ma'dan'.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi is a classic statement of the conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author begins with a historical anecdote about Ibn Mas'ud's ijtihad in a case of marriage without a specified dowry, demonstrating that qiyas is a legitimate tool when a clear text is absent. Then the five conditions are listed and explained. Condition one: qiyas must not contradict a clear text (nass). Condition two: it must not involve changing the ruling of the text in its essence; it only applies the text's ruling to a new case. Condition three: the ruling in the branch case must be rationally intelligible. Condition four: the causation (ta'lil) must be for a legal ruling, not a linguistic one. Condition five: the extraction of the cause from the branch must not be predetermined by a text. The commentary expands on each condition, clarifying that the change prohibited is in the meaning of the text, not the application to a specific case. It also distinguishes between causation (ta'lil) and qiyas—ta'lil is identifying the cause within the text, qiyas is extending it to a new case. The passage includes a critique of linguistic qiyas, attributed to some Shafi'is, and defends the Hanafi position that only legal rulings can be derived via qiyas. A key sub-discussion is whether qiyas can be used when there is already a text on the branch; the majority view is that it is unnecessary but permissible to reinforce the text, a position favored by the Samarkand scholars.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning used to extend a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared effective cause (illa).
النص (al-nass): A clear textual ruling from the Quran or Sunnah that is definitive in meaning and applicable.
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that justifies the ruling and allows its extension to new cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the fourth condition for the validity of qiyas?
A) That it does not oppose a text.
B) That it does not involve changing a ruling of the text.
C) That the branch ruling is rationally intelligible.
D) That the causation is for a legal ruling, not a linguistic matter.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is a valid tool only when it satisfies five conditions, chief among them that it must not oppose any clear text and must be based on a legal cause, not a linguistic one.

Conditions for Valid Qiyas and Invalid Examples
Explains five conditions for valid qiyas and gives examples of invalid qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions for valid qiyas in Hanafi usul and identify when qiyas is invalid due to contradiction with a text or unintelligible ruling.

Core Idea
Qiyas is invalid if it contradicts the text or relies on an unintelligible ruling.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, the author outlines the necessary conditions for analogical reasoning to produce a valid legal ruling. He also provides concrete examples of qiyas that fails these conditions, especially when it opposes explicit scriptural texts. Understanding these conditions is crucial for correctly applying qiyas in deriving new rulings.

Guided Path
1
List the conditions for valid qiyas
Identify each condition mentioned in the passage (the author lists five, with the third, fourth, and fifth detailed). State them in your own words.
The first two conditions may be implied from the general definition of qiyas.
2
Explain why each condition is necessary
For each condition, consider what would go wrong if it were absent. For example, if the ruling is not intelligible, qiyas cannot extend it because the cause is unknown.
Focus on the third condition (intelligibility) and the fifth (branch not explicitly ruled).
3
Analyze the examples of invalid qiyas
Examine the two examples: laughter vs. slander in prayer, and women traveling with trustworthy women. Determine which condition each violates.
The first example violates the third condition; the second violates the fifth (and also the first condition if the text is explicit).
4
Understand the debate on qiyas muwafiq
The passage touches on whether qiyas that agrees with the text is permissible. Note the majority view and the Samarkand view, and the author's preference.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الرابع في القياس فصل في شروط صحة القياس يتضمَّن تغيير حكم من أحكام النص، والثالث: أن لا يكون المعدى حكماً لا يُعقل معناه. والرابع: أن يَقَعَ التعليل الحكم شرعي لا لأمر لغوي. والخامس: أن لا يكون الفرع منصوصاً عليه. ومثال القياس في مقابلة النص: فيما حُكي أن الحسن بن زياد سُئِلَ عن القَهْقَهَة في الصَّلاة، فقال: انتَقَضَت الطهارة بها، قال السائلُ: لو قذف محصنَةٌ في الصَّلاة لا ينتقض به الوضوء مع أن قذف المحصنة أعظمُ جناية، فكيف ينتقض بالقهقهة وهي دونه؟ فهذا قياس في مقابلة النص، وهو حديث الأعرابي الذي في عينه سوء. وكذلك إذا قلنا: جاز حج المرأة مع المحرم، فيجوز مع الأمينات، كان هذا قياساً بمقابلة النص، وهو قوله عليه: "لا يحل لامرأة تؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر أن تسافر فوق ثلاثة أيام ولياليها إلا ومعها أبوها أو زوجها، أو ذو رَحْمٍ محرم منها". ومثال الثاني: وهو ما يتضمن تغيير حكم من أحكام النص، ما يقال: النية شرط في الوضوء. لا يقال: بل ينتقض الطهارة بالقذف قياساً على القهقهة؛ لكونه أعظم جناية؛ لأن شرط القياس أن يكون المعدى حكماً يعقل معناه، وحديث القهقهة ورد غير معقول المعنى؛ لأن الانتقاض إنما يكون بخروج النجاسة، والقهقهة ليست بنجاسة حتى ينتقض بها، ولا يعقل معنى الانتقاض بها كذا في "المعدن". حديث الأعرابي: وهو فيما روي أن أعرابياً في عينه سوء دخل المسجد فتعثر في مشيته فوقع على الأرض، وكان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي بالناس إماماً، فضحك الناس خلفه في الصلاة، فقال لهم: "ألا من ضحك منكم قهقهة فليعد الوضوء والصلاة جميعا". [أخرجه الدار قطني ٥٦٤/١] كان هذا قياساً إلخ وجه المقابلة: أن الشارع حرم المسافرة على العموم، واستثنى منه المسافرة فكان المسافرة مع غيرهما داخلة تحت التحريم على الإطلاق، سواء كانت مع الرجل أو مع المرأة الأمينة وغيرها، و للخصم أن يقول: أن الأمينات ألحقت بها فكانت في معناهما، ومثله لا يفيد مخالفة النص كما في قوله عليه: "إنما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعًا" ألحقت صورة الإتكاء بالاضطجاع مع أن كلمة "إنما" للحصر. لا يحل إلخ رواه الطبراني عن أبي أمامة رفعه: "لا يحل لامرأة مسلمة أن تحج إلا مع زوج أو ذي رحم محرم"، ورواه محمد في "الآثار" برواية أبي سعد، وفي آخره: "ولا تسافر المرأة إلا مع زوجها، أو مع ذي رحم محرم"، وهو قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وقال مالك والشافعي رحمهما إذا خرجت في رفقه ومعها نساء ثقاة بحصول الأمن بالمرافقة فيجوز، وإلا لا كذا في "الحصول".
The fourth research on qiyas. Chapter on conditions for the validity of qiyas. It includes changing a ruling from among the rulings of the text. The third condition: that the transferred ruling is not a ruling whose meaning is not intelligible. The fourth: that the causation occurs for a shar'i ruling, not for a linguistic matter. The fifth: that the branch is not explicitly ruled upon. An example of qiyas in opposition to the text: It is narrated that al-Hasan ibn Ziyad was asked about loud laughter in prayer, and he said: ablution is invalidated by it. The questioner said: If one slanders a chaste woman in prayer, does ablution not break? While slander is a greater sin, so how is it broken by laughter which is lesser? This is qiyas in opposition to the text, which is the hadith of the Bedouin who had poor eyesight. Similarly, if we say: A woman may perform hajj with a mahram, so she may perform it with trustworthy women, this is qiyas in opposition to the text, which is his statement: 'It is not permissible for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel more than three days and nights except with her father, her husband, or a mahram relative.' And an example of the second type, which entails changing a ruling from among the rulings of the text: what is said: intention is a condition for ablution. It is not said: Rather ablution breaks by slander by analogy to laughter because it is a greater sin. Because the condition of qiyas is that the transferred ruling has an intelligible meaning, and the hadith of laughter came as unintelligible meaning, because breaking occurs only by something impure, and laughter is not impure to break by it, nor is the meaning of break understood by it, as in 'al-Ma'din'. The hadith of the Bedouin: It is narrated that a Bedouin with poor eyesight entered the mosque, stumbled in his walking, and fell to the ground. The Messenger of Allah was leading the people in prayer, and the people laughed behind him in prayer. He said: 'Whoever among you laughed loudly, let him repeat both ablution and prayer.' [Al-Daraqutni 1/564] This was qiyas etc. The aspect of opposition: The Lawgiver prohibited travel in general and exempted from it traveling with the two, so traveling with others falls under absolute prohibition, whether with a man or a trustworthy woman or others. And the opponent may say: Trustworthy women are attached to them and thus are in their meaning, and such does not contradict the text, as in his statement: 'Ablution is only required for the one who sleeps lying down,' the case of reclining was attached to lying down even though the word 'innama' indicates restriction. It is not permissible etc. Narrated by al-Tabarani from Abu Umama marfu': 'It is not permissible for a Muslim woman to perform hajj except with a husband or a mahram relative.' And Muhammad narrated it in al-Athar with the narration of Abu Sa'd, and at its end: 'And a woman may not travel except with her husband or a mahram relative.' This is the statement of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. Malik and al-Shafi'i said: If she goes out in a caravan and with trustworthy women such that safety is achieved by accompaniment, it is permissible, otherwise not, as in al-Husul.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a usul al-fiqh exposition on the conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in the Hanafi school, followed by examples of invalid qiyas. The author lists five conditions, with the third, fourth, and fifth detailed. The third condition: the transferred ruling (al-mu'adda) must be a ruling whose meaning is intelligible (ma'qul al-ma'na); otherwise qiyas cannot be applied. The fourth: the ruling being causally explained (ta'lil) must be a shar'i ruling, not a linguistic one, because qiyas is a shar'i proof. The fifth: the branch (far') must not be explicitly ruled upon by a text (nass), because if it is, there is no need for qiyas. The passage then gives two examples of qiyas in opposition to the text (qiyas muqabil al-nass). First, the case of laughter in prayer: a text states that loud laughter invalidates both ablution and prayer. Someone argued by analogy that slander should also invalidate because it is more sinful, but this is invalid because the text's ruling is not intelligible by reason—it is an exception. Second, the prohibition of women traveling without a mahram: some analogize trustworthy women to a mahram, but this contradicts the explicit text. The passage also distinguishes between two types of qiyas muqabil al-nass: one that directly contradicts the text, and one that changes a ruling from the text. The commentary includes a defense of the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i view that qiyas can confirm a text, citing the opinion of the Samarkand scholars.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Extending a ruling from an original to a branch due to a common effective cause.
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause that necessitates the ruling and is common to both original and branch.
الفرع (al-far'): The new case or act for which a ruling is sought via qiyas.
الأصل (al-asl): The original case with an established ruling from a text or consensus.
مقابلة النص (muqabilat al-nass): Qiyas that contradicts an explicit textual ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for a transferred ruling (al-mu'adda) in qiyas according to this passage?
A) It must be a ruling from the Quran.
B) Its meaning must be intelligible.
C) It must be from consensus.
D) It must be a linguistic ruling.

Key Takeaway
For qiyas to be valid, the ruling must be intelligible, the cause must be shar'i, and the branch must not be explicitly ruled by a text.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Invalid Qiyas: The Rule Against Opposing the Text (Muqabalat al-Nass)
Section on conditions of qiyas with examples of qiyas opposing the text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a case of qiyas that directly contradicts an explicit text (qiyas fi muqabalat al-nass) and explain why it is invalid according to Hanafi usul, using the examples of qahqaha and woman traveling.

Core Idea
Qiyas that opposes a clear text is void — even a stronger analogy cannot override a divinely given ruling.

In this passage, Imam al-Shashi introduces a critical condition for valid qiyas: it must not oppose an explicit text (nass). He provides two vivid examples from fiqh: the invalidation of wudu by loud laughter (qahqaha) and the prohibition of a woman traveling without a mahram. These illustrate that even a seemingly stronger analogy cannot override a ruling that is either purely textual (ta'abbudi) or explicitly limited. Understanding this rule preserves the primacy of revelation over human reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two examples of invalid qiyas
Locate the two scenarios given: (1) comparing qadhf to qahqaha to argue that qadhf should also invalidate wudu, and (2) comparing trustworthy women to mahram to allow a woman to travel without a mahram.
Both are attempts to extend a textual ruling by analogy.
2
Identify the explicit text being opposed
For qahqaha, the text is the hadith of the Bedouin that ties invalidation of wudu and prayer to qahqaha. For travel, the text is the hadith/verse that permits travel only with a mahram.
These texts are clear and specific.
3
Understand why the qiyas fails
The qahqaha example fails because the ruling is not rationally understood (ghayr ma'qul al-ma'na) — it is a purely devotional (ta'abbudi) ruling. The travel example fails because the text's exception is exhaustive; extending it would change the law.
The condition for qiyas is that the underlying meaning (ma'na) must be rationally comprehensible and the qiyas must not contradict the text.
4
Examine the opponent's counterargument
The opponent argues that trustworthy women are attached (mulhaq) to mahram because they serve the same purpose of safety. The author rebuts by noting that such attachment (ilhaq) does not violate the text, as shown in the example of 'innama al-wudu 'ala man nama muttadi'an' where leaning was attached to lying down.
But here, the text explicitly limits the exception, so attachment would be opposition.
5
Note the madhhab difference
Abu Hanifah strictly follows the text, requiring a mahram. Malik and al-Shafi'i permit travel with trustworthy women if safety is assured, based on the underlying reason (safety). This illustrates different usul approaches to extending a text by qiyas.
The Hanafi response: the text's ruling is based on the specific relationship, not solely on safety.

Source Text

فصل في شروط صحة القياس
به الوضوء مع أن قذف المحصنة أعظمُ جناية، فكيف ينتقض بالقهقهة وهي دونه؟ فهذا قياس في مقابلة النص، وهو حديث الأعرابي الذي في عينه سوء.
وكذلك إذا قلنا: جاز حج المرأة مع المحرم، فيجوز مع الأمينات، كان هذا قياساً بمقابلة النص، وهو قوله علي: "لا يحل لامرأة تؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر أن تسافر فوق ثلاثة أيام ولياليها إلا ومعها أبوها أو زوجها، أو ذو رَحْمٍ محرم منها".
فهذا قياس في مقابلة إلخ لا يقال: بل ينتقض الطهارة بالقذف قياساً على القهقهة؛ لكونه أعظم جناية؛ لأن شرط القياس أن يكون المعدى حكماً يعقل معناه، وحديث القهقهة ورد غير معقول المعنى؛ لأن الانتقاض إنما يكون بخروج النجاسة، والقهقهة ليست بنجاسة حتى ينتقض بها، ولا يعقل معنى الانتقاض بها كذا في "المعدن". حديث الأعرابي: وهو فيما روي أن أعرابياً في عينه سوء دخل المسجد فتعثر في مشيته فوقع على الأرض، وكان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي بالناس إماماً، فضحك الناس خلفه في الصلاة، فقال لهم: "ألا من ضحك منكم قهقهة فليعد الوضوء والصلاة جميعا". [أخرجه الدار قطني ٥٦٤/١] [الشافي: ص ٢٥٨]
كان هذا قياساً إلخ وجه المقابلة: أن الشارع حرم المسافرة على العموم، واستثنى منه المسافرة فكان المسافرة مع غيرهما داخلة تحت التحريم على الإطلاق، سواء كانت مع الرجل أو مع المرأة الأمينة وغيرها، و للخصم أن يقول: أن الأمينات ألحقت بها فكانت في معناهما، ومثله لا يفيد مخالفة النص كما في قوله عليه: "إنما الوضوء على من نام مضطجعًا" ألحقت صورة الإتكاء بالاضطجاع مع أن كلمة "إنما" للحصر. لا يحل إلخ رواه الطبراني عن أبي أمامة رفعه: "لا يحل لامرأة مسلمة أن تحج إلا مع زوج أو ذي رحم محرم"، ورواه محمد في "الآثار" برواية أبي سعد، وفي آخره: "ولا تسافر المرأة إلا مع زوجها، أو مع ذي رحم محرم"، وهو قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، وقال مالك والشافعي رحمها إذا خرجت في رفقه ومعها نساء ثقاة بحصول الأمن بالمرافقة فيجوز، وإلا لا كذا في "الحصول".

Section on the conditions for the validity of qiyas. [Example]: wudu [being invalidated] by [qahqaha] whereas the accusation of a chaste woman is a greater offense, so how can it be invalidated by qahqaha which is lesser? This is qiyas opposing the text, and it is the hadith of the Bedouin who had a defect in his eye. Similarly, if we say: it is permissible for a woman to perform Hajj with a mahram, so it is permissible with trustworthy women, this is a qiyas opposing the text, which is His statement, 'It is not lawful for a woman who believes in Allah and the Last Day to travel more than three days and nights except with her father, her husband, or a mahram relative.' So this is qiyas opposing, etc. It cannot be said: Rather, purification is invalidated by qadhf by analogy to qahqaha because it is a greater offense, because the condition for qiyas is that the transmitted ruling has a rational meaning, and the hadith of qahqaha came without a rational meaning, because invalidation occurs only by the emission of impurity, and qahqaha is not an impurity so that it invalidates, and the meaning of invalidation by it is not rationally understood, as in al-Ma'din. The hadith of the Bedouin: It is narrated that a Bedouin with a defect in his eye entered the mosque and stumbled in his walk and fell to the ground, and the Messenger of Allah was leading the people in prayer, so the people laughed behind him in prayer, and he said to them, 'Whoever among you laughed qahqaha should repeat both wudu and prayer.' [Recorded by al-Daraqutni 1/564] [al-Shafi: p. 258]. This was a qiyas, etc. The aspect of opposition: that the Lawgiver prohibited travel generally, and exempted from it [travel with mahram], so travel with other than them falls under the absolute prohibition, whether with a man or with a trustworthy woman or others. And the opponent may say: that trustworthy women are attached to them, so they are in their meaning, and such does not entail violation of the text, as in his statement, 'Wudu is only required for one who sleeps lying down,' and the case of leaning was attached to lying down even though the word 'innama' indicates exclusivity. It is not lawful, etc. Narrated by al-Tabarani from Abu Umamah raised: 'It is not lawful for a Muslim woman to perform Hajj except with a husband or a mahram relative,' and Muhammad narrated it in al-Athar with the narration of Abu Sa'd, and at its end: 'And a woman should not travel except with her husband or a mahram relative.' And this is the saying of Abu Hanifah, may Allah have mercy on him. And Malik and al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on them, said: if she goes out with a safe company and with trustworthy women, and safety is achieved by accompaniment, it is permissible, otherwise not, as in al-Husul. * Recorded by Muslim in the chapter on a woman traveling with a mahram for Hajj and other purposes, no. 827, 1340; and al-Tirmidhi in the chapter on the dislike of a woman traveling alone, no. 1169, who said: this hadith is hasan sahih; and Ibn Majah in the chapter on a woman performing Hajj, no. 2898, from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage begins the section on the conditions for the validity of qiyas (analogical reasoning). The author, Imam al-Shashi, first identifies a type of invalid qiyas: qiyas that directly opposes the text (قياس في مقابلة النص). He gives two examples.

The first example concerns the invalidation of wudu by a loud laugh (qahqaha) in prayer. Some might argue by qiyas that since falsely accusing a chaste woman (qadhf) is a greater sin, the invalidation by qahqaha should be even more severe, but this is rejected because the hadith about qahqaha is not rationally understood—it is a purely textual ruling. The condition for valid qiyas is that the underlying reason (ma'na) be rationally comprehensible. Since qahqaha is not an impurity, its effect cannot be analogized.

The second example concerns a woman traveling for Hajj. The text explicitly permits it only with a mahram. Some might extend this by qiyas to travel with trustworthy women (aminat), claiming they provide equal safety. This is invalid because it directly opposes the explicit text. The author then presents the opponent's argument that trustworthy women are attached to the mahram because they serve a similar purpose, but he rejects it, citing that such analogies do not violate the text, as in the case of 'innama al-wudu 'ala man nama muttadi'an' where leaning was attached to lying down.

The passage ends with a note on the scholarly difference: Abu Hanifah strictly requires a mahram, while Malik and al-Shafi'i allow travel with trustworthy women if safety is assured. The author confirms Abu Hanifah's position as the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.

This lesson illustrates a key usul principle: qiyas cannot override a clear textual ruling, and the condition of rational meaning (ta'qil al-ma'na) is essential.

Key Terms
قياس في مقابلة النص (qiyas fi muqabalat al-nass): Analogical reasoning that directly contradicts an explicit textual ruling
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter that invalidates wudu and prayer according to the hadith
محرم (mahram): A male relative whom a woman is permanently prohibited from marrying

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the passage, why is qiyas that compares qadhf (false accusation) to qahqaha (loud laughter) invalid?
A) Because qadhf is a lesser offense than qahqaha
B) Because the hadith on qahqaha is not rationally understood (ghayr ma'qul al-ma'na)
C) Because qiyas is never allowed in matters of worship
D) Because the hadith on qahqaha is weak

Key Takeaway
Qiyas cannot oppose an explicit text; if the text's ruling is not rationally understood (ta'abbudi), no analogy can extend it.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
