Invalid Qiyas on Non-Rational Rulings (Ma La Yu'qal Ma'anahu)
Third type of invalid qiyas: analogizing on a ruling that is not rationally understood

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a ruling that is 'ma la yu'qal ma'anahu' and explain why it cannot serve as the basis for qiyas in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Rulings established contrary to analogy are confined to their text and cannot be extended by qiyas.

In this lesson, we examine the third type of invalid qiyas: analogizing on a ruling whose rationale is not rationally comprehensible. The key example is the permissibility of wudu with nabidh (date drink). The Prophet performed wudu with nabidh when water was unavailable, but this act was contrary to the general analogy of purification. The Hanafi school holds that such exceptional rulings cannot be extended to other cases by qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exceptional ruling
Recognize that the permissibility of wudu with nabidh is established by text but contrary to the normal principle of purification (which requires water).
The ruling is an exception (khilaf al-qiyas).
2
Classify it as ma la yu'qal ma'anahu
Understand that the rationale behind the ruling is not rationally comprehensible; it is a specific dispensation from the Prophet.
Such rulings are not extendable by qiyas.
3
Apply the rule: no qiyas on exceptions
State the Hanafi principle: what is proven contrary to qiyas cannot be analogized to other instances.
The ruling is confined to its textual scope.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Observe that some early scholars (e.g., Zufar) allowed qiyas here, but the adopted Hanafi view (final position of Abu Hanifah) forbids it.
The majority (including Abu Yusuf, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) agree with non-permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثال الثالث: وهو ما لا يعقل معناه في حق جواز التوضي بنبيذ التمر، فإنه لو قال: جاز بغيره من الأنبذة بالقياس على نبيذ التمر، أو قال: لو شجّ في صلاته أو احتلم يبني. من الإطلاق إلخ وقد مر البحث عنها في فصل المقيد والمطلق، وحاصله : أن إطلاق آية الوضوء يقتضي حصول الوضوء من غير النية، واشتراطها بعدمه، وهو حكم من أحكامه؛ فإنه لا يجوز؛ لأنه نسخ، ونسخ النص لا يجوز بالقياس إجماعاً كذا في بعض الشروح. بالخبر : أي الحديث قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم "الطواف بالبيت صلاة إلا أن الله أحل فيه المنطق، فمن نطق فيه فلا ينطق إلا بخير". أخرجه الترمذي في الحج برقم: ٩٦٠، والدارمي في المناسك برقم: ۱٧٧٦ ، واللفظ له [الشافي: ص ٢٥٩] يوجب تغيير نص إلخ: لأن قوله تعالى: وليص بالبيت العتيق الآية مطلق في الطواف، وهو اسم الدوران حول البيت، فاشتراط الطهارة وستر العورة يوجب تغيير النص من الإطلاق إلى التقييد، وأنه لا يجوز أصلاً كذا في بعض الشروح إلى القيد: ومسألة الطواف والنية قد مر البحث عنهما في فصل المطلق والمقيد من هذا الكتاب.
في حق جواز إلخ فإنه روي أنه عليه توضأ به حين لم يجد الماء، وقال بعض الناس: جاز التوضي بغيره من الأنبذة بالقياس على نبيذ التمر، قلنا: إن جواز التوضي بنبيذ التمر ثابت بالنص على خلاف القياس؛ لأنه ليس بماء حقيقة، ولهذا لا يسبق إلى الفهم عند إطلاق اسم الماء حتى لو أمر أحداً بإتيان الماء فجاء بنبيذ التمر يخطأ عادة، ولا معنى؛ لأنه ليس بقالع للنجاسة من المحل كالماء وما ثبت بخلاف القياس لا يقاس عليه غيره، بل يقتصر الحكم على مورد النص. بنبيذ التمر إلخ روى حديثه الأربعة إلا النسائي عن ابن مسعود من طريق أبي فزارة عن أبي زيد مولى عمرو بن حريث عنه مرا مرفوعاً: "فمرة طيبة وماء طهور زاد الترمذي "فتوضأ منه"، ثم جواز التوضي به مذهب الطرفين، وبه قال عكرمة والأوزاعي وحميد بن حبيب والحسن بن حي وإسحاق وزفر، وقال أبو يوسف له، وهو قول مالك والشافعي وأحمد وغيرهم من العلماء : إنه لا يجوز التوضي به، وهو مختار الطحاوي وصححه قاضي خان قال وهو قوله الأخير، وقد رجع إليه الإمام، وروى ابن قدامة في "المغني" عن علي : أنه لا يرى بأساً في الوضوء به، وبه قال الحسن كذا في "الحصول".
And the third example: it is that whose meaning is not rationally understood regarding the permissibility of performing wudu with nabidh (date drink). For if one said: it is permissible with other nabidh by analogy on nabidh of dates, or said: if one is wounded in his prayer or has a wet dream, he builds [on his prayer]. From the absolute, etc., and the discussion has already passed on this in the section on the restricted and absolute. The summary is that the absolute wording of the verse of wudu implies the attainment of wudu without intention, and stipulating it would negate that, which is a ruling of it. That is not permissible because it is abrogation, and abrogation of the text by qiyas is not permissible by consensus, as in some commentaries. By 'report': meaning the hadith, the Messenger of Allah said: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer except that Allah has permitted speech in it, so whoever speaks in it should speak only good.' Recorded by al-Tirmidhi in Hajj, no. 960, and al-Darimi in al-Manāsik, no. 1776, and the wording is his [al-Shafi: p. 259]. It necessitates changing the text, etc., because Allah's statement 'and let them circumambulate the Ancient House' is absolute regarding tawaf, which is the act of going around the House, so stipulating purity and covering of the private parts necessitates changing the text from absolute to restricted, and that is not permissible at all, as in some commentaries. And the issue of tawaf and intention has already been discussed in the section on the absolute and restricted of this book. Regarding the permissibility, etc., for it is narrated that he (peace be upon him) performed wudu with it when he did not find water, and some people said: it is permissible to perform wudu with other nabidh by analogy on nabidh of dates. We say: the permissibility of wudu with nabidh of dates is established by text contrary to qiyas, because it is not truly water, and for this reason it does not come to mind when the name 'water' is used absolutely, so much so that if one orders someone to bring water and he brings nabidh of dates, he is mistaken customarily. And it has no meaning because it is not a remover of impurity from the place like water. And what is established contrary to qiyas cannot be analogized to other than it; rather, the ruling is confined to the instance of the text. Regarding nabidh of dates, etc., its hadith was narrated by the four except al-Nasa'i from Ibn Mas'ud via the chain of Abu Fazarah from Abu Zayd, the freed slave of 'Amr ibn Hurayth, from him, raised: 'A good date and purifying water,' and al-Tirmidhi added 'and he performed wudu from it.' Then the permissibility of wudu with it is the position of both sides. It is held by 'Ikrimah, al-Awza'i, Humayd ibn Habib, al-Hasan ibn Hayy, Ishaq, and Zufar. Abu Yusuf says it is not permissible, and that is the saying of Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad, and other scholars. It is the choice of al-Tahawi and declared sahih by Qadi Khan, and he said it is his latter opinion, and the Imam (Abu Hanifah) returned to it. Ibn Qudamah narrated in al-Mughni from 'Ali that he saw no harm in wudu with it, and al-Hasan also said so, as in al-Husul.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents the third type of invalid qiyas: analogizing on a ruling that is not rationally understood (ma la yu'qal ma'anahu). The specific example is the permissibility of wudu with nabidh (date drink). According to a hadith, the Prophet performed wudu with nabidh when water was not available. Some people attempt to extend this ruling to other types of nabidh by qiyas. The author explains that this is invalid because the permissibility of wudu with nabidh is established by text (nass) contrary to analogy (khilaf al-qiyas). Nabidh is not water in reality and does not remove impurity in the way water does. Therefore, the ruling is confined to the specific case mentioned in the text and cannot be extended by qiyas. The author adds that what is proven by text but contrary to analogy cannot be used as a basis for qiyas; it remains limited to its textual scope.

The passage then lists the scholarly disagreement: Some early scholars (including Zufar, who is a Hanafi) permitted wudu with nabidh, while the majority (including Abu Yusuf, Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) did not. The author notes that Abu Hanifah's final position was to forbid it, according to Qadi Khan and al-Tahawi. This illustrates the principle that rulings established contrary to analogy are not analogizable.

Key Terms
ما لا يعقل معناه (ma la yu'qal ma'anahu): A ruling whose underlying rationale is not rationally comprehensible
نبيذ التمر (nabidh al-tamr): A drink made from dates (soaked in water)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it invalid to permit wudu with other types of nabidh by qiyas on nabidh of dates?
A) Because nabidh of dates is not water and its ruling is contrary to analogy
B) Because the hadith on nabidh is weak
C) Because qiyas is never allowed in matters of purification
D) Because all scholars agree it is invalid

Key Takeaway
Rulings proven by text but contrary to analogy cannot be extended by qiyas; they are confined to their textual instances.

Invalid Qiyas on Ta'abbudi Rulings
Discusses invalid qiyas on ta'abbudi rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a ruling as ta'abbudi (ma la yu'qalu ma'nahu) and explain why qiyas cannot be applied to extend it.

Core Idea
A ruling established contrary to qiyas is confined to its textual scope; it cannot be extended by analogy.

Some rulings in the Shari'ah are purely devotional (ta'abbudi) — their underlying rationale (illa) is not rationally understood. The Hanafis hold that such rulings cannot be extended by qiyas to new cases. This lesson examines the key example of wudu with date-nabidh and the principle that prevents analogical extension.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of ta'abbudi
Identify that a ta'abbudi ruling is one whose meaning/rationale is not rationally comprehensible. It is established by text (nass) and is often contrary to general principles.
The term 'ma la yu'qalu ma'nahu' literally means 'whose meaning is not understood'.
2
Examine the nabidh case
Wudu with date-nabidh is proven by a specific hadith. However, nabidh is not water and does not remove impurity like water. Thus it is a ruling contrary to qiyas.
The hadith: 'A good date and pure water' with the addition 'so he performed wudu from it'.
3
Why qiyas is invalid here
Since the ruling is established contrary to qiyas and its rationale is not understood, it must be confined to the textual instance. Extending it to other nabidh would be invalid qiyas.
This is the third type of invalid qiyas in Usul al-Fiqh.
4
Recognize the inter-madhhab dispute
Hanafis hold that wudu with nabidh is permissible but not extendable. Other schools (Malik, Shafi'i, Ahmad) reject the hadith or interpret it differently, and do not allow wudu with nabidh.
The dispute is about both the permissibility and the possibility of qiyas.
5
Apply the principle to the two qullahs example
The Shafi'i claim that two qullahs (a measure of water) remain pure when separated, analogizing to the hadith that water does not become impure if it reaches two qullahs. The Hanafi response: if the original ruling were established by text, its meaning might not be rationally understood, so qiyas is invalid.
The exact text of this example is uncertain due to OCR corruption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في حق جواز التوضي بنبيذ التمر، فإنه لو قال: جاز بغيره من الأنبذة بالقياس على نبيذ التمر، قلنا: إن جواز التوضي بنبيذ التمر ثابت بالنص على خلاف القياس؛ لأنه ليس بماء حقيقة، ولهذا لا يسبق إلى الفهم عند إطلاق اسم الماء حتى لو أمر أحداً بإتيان الماء فجاء بنبيذ التمر يخطأ عادة، ولا معنى؛ لأنه ليس بقالع للنجاسة من المحل كالماء وما ثبت بخلاف القياس لا يقاس عليه غيره، بل يقتصر الحكم على مورد النص. روى حديثه الأربعة إلا النسائي عن ابن مسعود من طريق أبي فزارة عن أبي زيد مولى عمرو بن حريث عنه مرا مرفوعاً: "فمرة طيبة وماء طهور" زاد الترمذي "فتوضأ منه"، ثم جواز التوضي به مذهب الطرفين، وبه قال عكرمة والأوزاعي وحميد بن حبيب والحسن بن حي وإسحاق وزفر، وقال أبو يوسف له، وهو قول مالك والشافعي وأحمد وغيرهم من العلماء: إنه لا يجوز التوضي به، وهو مختار الطحاوي وصححه قاضي خان قال وهو قوله الأخير، وقد رجع إليه الإمام، وروى ابن قدامة في "المغني" عن علي: أنه لا يرى بأساً في الوضوء به، وبه قال الحسن كذا في "الحصول". وبمثل هذا قال أصحاب الشافعي له: قلتان بجستان إذا اجتمعتا صارتا طاهرتين، فإذا افترقتا بقيتا على الطهارة بالقياس على ما إذا وقعت النجاسة في القُلّتين؛ لأن الحكم لو ثبت في الأصل كان غير معقول معناه. وهو عدم التنجيس. ومثال الثالث: وهو ما لا يعقل معناه في حق جواز التوضي بنبيذ التمر، فإنه لو قال: مثال قوات الشرط جاز بغيره من الأنبذة بالقياس على نبيذ التمر، أو قال: لو شجّ في صلاته أو احتلم يبني من الإطلاق إلخ وقد مر البحث عنها في فصل المقيد والمطلق. كذا في 'المعدن' و'الفصول'.
Regarding the permissibility of wudu with date-nabidh, for if one said: it is permissible with other nabidh by analogy on date-nabidh, we say: indeed the permissibility of wudu with date-nabidh is established by text contrary to analogy; because it is not water in reality, and for this reason it does not come to mind when the name 'water' is used absolutely, so if someone ordered another to bring water and he brought date-nabidh, he would be mistaken customarily, and there is no meaning [to the analogy] because it does not remove impurity from a place like water, and whatever is established contrary to analogy cannot have anything else analogized to it, rather the ruling is confined to the textual instance. His hadith was narrated by the four except al-Nasa'i from Ibn Mas'ud via Abu Fazarah from Abu Zayd, the freed slave of 'Amr ibn Hurayth, from him, marfu': 'A good date and pure water' — al-Tirmidhi added: 'so he performed wudu from it'. Then the permissibility of wudu with it is a view of both parties: 'Ikrimah, al-Awza'i, Humayd ibn Habib, al-Hasan ibn Hayy, Ishaq, and Zafar held it; Abu Yusuf said it is permissible; but Malik, al-Shafi'i, Ahmad and other scholars said it is not permissible to perform wudu with it, and that is the choice of al-Tahawi and authenticated by Qadi Khan, who said it is his later view, and the Imam [Abu Hanifa] retracted to it; and Ibn Qudamah narrated in 'al-Mughni' from 'Ali: that he saw no harm in wudu with it, and al-Hasan said the same as in 'al-Husul'. And similarly said the companions of al-Shafi'i to him: two qullahs in Jistan [?] when they combine become pure, and when they separate they remain pure, by analogy on when impurity falls into the two qullahs; because if the ruling were established in the original, it would be not rationally understood. And it is the absence of impurity-carrying. And the third example: that which is not rationally understood regarding the permissibility of wudu with date-nabidh, for if he said: the example of qawat al-shart [?] it is permissible with other nabidh by analogy on date-nabidh, or he said: if he is wounded in his prayer or he has a wet dream, he builds on the absolute etc. And research on this has passed in the chapter on restricted and absolute. Thus in 'al-Ma'din' and 'al-Fusul'.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage discusses the third type of invalid qiyas: qiyas on rulings whose rationale (ma'na) is not understood because they are established by text contrary to the general principles of qiyas. The main example is wudu with nabidh (date-infused water). The permissibility is proven by a specific hadith, but it is contrary to analogy because nabidh is not water and does not remove impurities. Therefore, it cannot be extended to other nabidh. The author then mentions a similar argument by Shafi'is regarding two qullahs (a measure of water) that are pure when combined but remain pure when separated, analogizing to the hadith that water does not become impure if it reaches two qullahs. The Hanafi response is that if the original ruling were established by a text, its meaning is not rationally understood (it is ta'abbudi), so qiyas is invalid. The passage also notes the disagreement among scholars on the validity of wudu with nabidh.

Key Terms
ما لا يعقل معناه (ma la yu'qalu ma'nahu): A ruling whose underlying rationale (illa) is not rationally understood, i.e., ta'abbudi.
نبيذ التمر (nabidh al-tamr): Date-infused water, a beverage made by soaking dates in water.
خلاف القياس (khilaf al-qiyas): Contrary to analogical reasoning; a ruling that does not follow from general principles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Can Names (Asma) Be Established by Qiyas? The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Usul dispute over the validity of qiyas in linguistic matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on establishing names by qiyas and explain the grammatical evidence used to support qiyas in linguistic matters.

Core Idea
Names are linguistic conventions; Hanafis reject qiyas for them, Shafi'is accept it based on grammatical analogy.

This lesson explores a foundational usul al-fiqh dispute: can qiyas (analogical reasoning) be used to establish names (asma) – linguistic terms or definitions – or is it restricted to sharia rulings? The Hanafi school holds that names are conventional and cannot be derived by analogy, while the Shafi'i school allows it, citing the practice of grammarians. Understanding this disagreement is crucial for how far qiyas extends in legal theory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Read the passage and identify the question: is it permissible to establish names (asma) by qiyas? Note the two opposing views.
The passage states the Hanafi position (and some Shafi'is) that it is not permissible, and the Shafi'i position that it is permissible.
2
Analyze the Shafi'i evidence
The Shafi'i evidence comes from grammarians: they use qiyas to derive that every subject (fa'il) is nominative and every object (maf'ul) is accusative, based on observed usage. This is presented as a proof that qiyas is valid for names.
The source quotes al-Fayruzabadi, a Shafi'i scholar, advancing this argument.
3
Understand the Hanafi response (implied)
The Hanafi response is not fully stated in this passage but is implicit: linguistic matters are conventional (tawqifi) and not subject to qiyas. The grammatical qiyas is a different type of analogy (qiyas nahwi) and does not transfer to sharia terminology.
Hanafis distinguish between linguistic analogy and legal analogy; only the latter is relevant for sharia rulings.
4
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Consider how this dispute affects fiqh: for example, can the word 'salah' (prayer) be extended through qiyas to mean supplication (du'a)? Hanafis would restrict it to the ritual prayer, while Shafi'is might allow the extension based on linguistic qiyas.
This shows that the dispute has real implications for defining legal terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثال الرابع: وهو ما يكون التعليل لأمر شرعي لا لأمر لغوي. في قولهم: المطبوخ قوات الشرط الشوافع في الأصل: أي في الحدث ثابت بالنص على خلاف القياس؛ لأن الحدث ينافي الصلاة؛ لأنه ينافي الطهارة، ولا صلاة إلا بالطهارة والشي لا يبقى مع منافيه وما ثبت بخلاف القياس لا يقاس عليه غيره كذا في 'المعدن' و'الفصول'. وهو ما يكون التعليل عندنا، وأصل الاختلاف أن إثبات الأسماء بالقياس يجوز أم لا، ومذهب الشافعي له: أن إثبات الأسماء بالقياس جائز، ومن أصحابه من قال لا يجوز وهو قول أصحاب أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، ولنا: أن النحويين أجمعوا على أن كل فاعل مرفوع وكل مفعول منصوب ولم يسمعوا ذلك من العرب، لكنهم لما وجدوهم مستمرين على رفع فاعل ونصب مفعول علموا أنهم رفعوا الفاعل؛ لكونه فاعلاً، ونصبوا المفعول؛ لكونه مفعولاً، فحملوا عليه كل فاعل وكل مفعول، فدل على جواز ذلك انتهى كلام الفيروز آبادي من الشافعية.
And the fourth example: that which is a legal reasoning for a matter of sharia, not for a linguistic matter. In their saying: 'cooked [food]? qawat al-shart? al-Shawafi'?' in the original: that is, concerning the hadath (ritual impurity) it is established by text contrary to analogy; because hadath is incompatible with prayer; because it is incompatible with purity, and prayer is only with purity, and a thing does not remain with its opposite, and what is established contrary to analogy cannot be analogized to anything else, as in 'al-Ma'din' and 'al-Fusul'. And it is what is the reasoning according to us, and the basis of the disagreement is whether the establishment of names by qiyas is permissible or not. The madhhab of al-Shafi'i is that establishment of names by qiyas is permissible, and among his companions are those who say it is not permissible, and that is the saying of the companions of Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him). And our evidence: that grammarians are agreed that every subject (fa'il) is nominative (marfu') and every object (maf'ul) is accusative (mansub), and they did not hear that from the Arabs, but when they found them consistently raising the subject and making the object accusative, they knew that they raised the subject because it is a subject, and made the object accusative because it is an object, so they applied that to every subject and every object. This indicates the permissibility of that. End of the speech of al-Fayruzabadi of the Shafi'is.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage discusses the fourth type of invalid qiyas: qiyas used for linguistic matters (asma) rather than sharia rulings. The author presents a Shafi'i example about 'cooked food' and 'hadath', but the text is corrupt. The key point is the usul dispute: can names (e.g., grammatically derived terms) be established by qiyas? The Hanafi position (and some Shafi'is) says no, because names are based on direct linguistic usage. However, the author of the commentary (al-Fayruzabadi? actually a Shafi'i) argues that grammarians do use qiyas to derive grammatical rules (e.g., all subjects are nominative), so it is permissible. The passage is truncated but presents the core disagreement.

Key Terms
إثبات الأسماء بالقياس (ithbat al-asma bi al-qiyas): Deriving or confirming the usage of a name (linguistic term) through analogical reasoning.
قياس نحوي (qiyas nahwi): Grammatical analogy used to derive linguistic rules from observed patterns.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts qiyas to sharia rulings; names are linguistic conventions not subject to analogy.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Condition of Rationally Understood Meaning (Ma'qul al-Ma'na) in Qiyas
Explaining the condition that qiyas requires a rationally understood meaning and the dispute over rulings contrary to analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a ruling must have a rationally understood meaning for valid qiyas, and distinguish between rulings that are ma'qul al-ma'na and those that are not.

Core Idea
If a ruling's rationale is beyond human comprehension, qiyas cannot extend it to new cases.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, we explore a fundamental condition for analogical reasoning: the original ruling must have a rationally intelligible cause (ma'qul al-ma'na). Rulings that are purely ta'abbudi or established by text contrary to analogy cannot be used for qiyas. This leads to an important dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is over the scope of such rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition stated for valid qiyas
Read the opening: qiyas on a ruling whose meaning is not rationally understood is invalid. The example is hadath nullifying prayer.
The ruling that hadath invalidates prayer is established by text against qiyas because hadath contradicts the essence of prayer, yet the text fixed it.
2
Understand why the ruling is 'ghayr ma'qul al-ma'na'
The ruling's rationale (why hadath nullifies) is not intellectually perceptible; it is a pure act of worship (ta'abbudi). Therefore, it cannot be extended to other situations by qiyas.
Hanafis hold that such rulings are confined to their specific case.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and their proof
Shafi'is attempt to use qiyas on the hadith of two qullas: water remains pure when joined, by analogy with impurity falling into two qullas. They argue the ruling (non-impurity) is ma'qul al-ma'na.
Hanafis respond that the hadith is weak and, even if accepted, the ruling is not ma'qul al-ma'na because remaining pure despite impurity is not rationally understood.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafi critique includes: the hadith is weak (Abu Dawud weakened it), it contradicts the practice of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Zubayr who ordered Zamzam to be drained, and the term 'qulla' is ambiguous. Thus qiyas on it is invalid.
The passage concludes that the ruling from text contrary to qiyas stays confined to its case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الرابع في القياس
فصل في شروط صحة القياس
على صلاته بالقياس على ما إذا سبقه الحدث لا يصح؛ لأن الحكم في الأصل لم يُعقَلْ معناه، فاستحال تعديته إلى الفرع وبمثل هذا قال أصحاب الشافعي له: قلتان بجستان إذا اجتمعتا صارتا طاهرتين، فإذا افترقتا بقيتا على الطهارة بالقياس على ما إذا وقعت النجاسة في القُلّتين؛ لأن الحكم لو ثبت في الأصل كان غير معقول معناه. وهو عدم التنجيس ومثال الرابع: وهو ما يكون التعليل لأمر شرعي لا لأمر لغوي، في قولهم: المطبوخ قوات الشرط الشوافع في الأصل: أي في الحدث ثابت بالنص على خلاف القياس؛ لأن الحدث ينافي الصلاة؛ لأنه ينافي الطهارة، ولا صلاة إلا بالطهارة والشي لا يبقى مع منافيه وما ثبت بخلاف القياس لا يقاس عليه غيره كذا في "المعدن" و الفصول". وبمثل هذا أي بمثل ما ذكرنا من أن الحكم الثابت بالنص على خلاف القياس غير معقول المعنى ينحصر على مورده عندنا خلافاً للشافعي الله كذا في "المعدن". في القُلتَين إلخ: فإنه لا يتنجس قوله عليه: "إذا بلغ الماء قلتين لم يحمل الخبث" أي: لا يحتمل نجساً، لكنا نقول هذا القياس غير صحيح؛ لأن الحكم لو ثبت في الأصل وهو ما إذا وقعت النجاسة في القلتين كان غير معقول معناه؛ لأن بقاء الطهارة مع وقوع النجاسة لا يعقل معناه، وإنما قال: لو ثبت في الأصل إشارة إلى أن هذا الحديث ليس بحجة؛ لأن في ثبوته خدشة؛ لأنه ضعفه أبو داود ؛ لأنه روي أن ابن عباس وابن الزبير أمرا بنزح زمزم، ولو كان هذا صحيحاً لاحتجوا عليهما، فعلم أنه شاذ في حادثة تعم به البلوى، فيرد كخبر الوضوء مما مسته النار، والقلة أيضاً اسم مشترك، فإنه اسم لرأس الجبل والجرة وغيرهما، فلذا قال المصنف له: إن هذا الحديث غير مسلم، وعلى تقدير التسليم فالقياس لا يصح كذا في "المعدن"و"الفصول". وهو ما يكون التعليل عندنا، وأصل الاختلاف أن إثبات الأسماء بالقياس يجوز أم لا، ومذهب الشافعي له: أن إثبات الأسماء بالقياس جائز، ومن أصحابه من قال لا يجوز وهو قول أصحاب أبي حنيفة رحلته، ولنا: أن النحويين أجمعوا على أن كل فاعل مرفوع وكل مفعول منصوب ولم يسمعوا ذلك من العرب، لكنهم لما وجدوهم مستمرين على رفع فاعل ونصب مفعول علموا أنهم رفعوا الفاعل؛ لكونه فاعلاً، ونصبوا المفعول؛ لكونه مفعولاً، فحملوا عليه كل فاعل وكل مفعول، فدل على جواز ذلك انتهى كلام الفيروز آبادي من الشافعية.

البحث الرابع في القياس
فصل في شروط صحة القياس المنصَّفُ حَمْرٌ؛ لأن الخَمْرَ إنما كان خمراً؛ لأنه يخامرُ العقل، وغيره يخامرُ العقل أيضًا، فيكون حمراً بالقياس. والسارقُ إنما كانَ سارقاً؛ لأنه أخذ مال الغير بطريقة الخفية، وقد شاركه النباش في هذا المعنى، فيكون سارقاً بالقياس، وهذا قياس في اللغة مع اعترافه أن الإسم لم يوضع له في اللغة. القياس في اللغة من الدهمة وهو السوداء والدليل على فساد هذا النوع من القياس: أن العرب يُسَمِّي الفرس "أدهم" لسواده. و"كميتاً" الحمرته، ثم لا يُطْلقُ هذا الاسم على الزنجي والثوب الأَحْمَر . من الكمت وهو الحمرة العرب ولو جَرَت المقايسة في الأسامي اللغوية لجاز ذلك لوجود العلة، ولأن هذا يؤدّي إلى من المنصف: المنصف العصير هو ما طبخ حتى بقي على النصف، كذا في "المصباح المنير : ١١٩/٢، ويحل شربه . أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف الحمل الالها لإزالة الغصة واستمراء الطعام والتداوي دون التلهي واللعب، وقال محمد محله: إنه مكروه، واتفق الكل على أنه لو سكر منه يجب الحد [الشافي: ص ٢٦٠] فيكون خمراً إلخ: أي فيجري عليه أحكام الخمر، وعند أصحابنا هو ليس بخمر وإنما الخمر، هو فيء من ماء العنب إذا صار مسكراً بالغليان والاشتداد، وهو اسم خالص له باتفاق أهل اللغة، وحرمته فوق حرمة غيره من الأشربة المحرمة، وهي المثلث والمنصف، ونقيع التمر ونقيع الزبيب إذا اشتد وغلى ولهذا يكفر مستحل الخمر ولا يكفر مستحلها، ويجب الحد بشرب قطرة من الخمر ولا يجب بشرب غيرها من الأشربة إلا أن يسكر، وهذا سماها خمراً بالقياس أعطاها حكمها فتدبر كذا في "المعدن" و "الفصول". ومن لأنه أخذ مالَ إلخ ولذا لم يكن على خائن ولا على منتهب ولا على مختلس قطع كما ورد في حديث جابر مرفوعاً، فعلم أن معنى الخفية معتبر في مفهوم السارق، والمعاني لنظم النصوص القرآنية تفسيرها الأخبار النبوية كذا قيل النباش لأنه يسرق ويأخذ المال وهو كفن الميت على طريق الخفية، فصدق عليه معنى السرقة، فيقطع يده كما هو مذهب الشافعي ومن تبعه. عندنا ه لجاز ذلك ذلك أي: إطلاق "الأدهم" على الزنجي، و"الكميت" على الثوب الأحمر، ولم يجز ذلك بالإجماع، فلم تجز المقايسة في اللغات كذا قيل. ولأن هذا يؤدي إلخ لا يقال: هذا يؤدي إلى بطلان القياس بالكلية؛
The fourth inquiry on qiyas. Chapter on the conditions for the validity of qiyas. ... (full translation would be very long; we provide a condensed literal version) ...
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Usul al-Shashi discusses the conditions for valid qiyas. It begins by stating that a ruling from the original (asl) must have a rationally understood meaning ('illa) for qiyas to extend it to a branch (far'). The first example: if an event (hadath) occurs during prayer, the ruling that prayer is invalidated is established by text contrary to qiyas (because hadath contradicts prayer, but the text fixed it). Since the meaning is not rationally understood, qiyas cannot be applied to other situations. The Hanafi position is that such rulings are confined to their specific case, unlike the Shafi'is who allow qiyas on them. The text then discusses the hadith 'If water reaches two qullas, it does not carry impurity' and disputes its authenticity and applicability. Later, it addresses qiyas in linguistic names: whether names like 'khamr' (wine) or 'sariq' (thief) can be extended by analogy. The Hanafis argue that linguistic names are not established by qiyas, as shown by Arabs not calling a black person 'adham' or a red garment 'kumayt' despite shared attributes. The passage concludes with examples of cooked wine (munassaf) and the graverobber (nabbash), showing the Shafi'i position that these can be called by those names via qiyas, while the Hanafis restrict them to their original linguistic meanings.

Key Terms
غير معقول المعنى (ghayr ma'qul al-ma'na): A ruling whose rationale is not intellectually perceptible; it is ta'abbudi (worshipped) and cannot be used for qiyas.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning in Islamic law: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared effective cause (illa).
خلاف القياس (khilaf al-qiyas): A ruling that is established by revealed text (nass) even though it conflicts with what analogical reasoning would suggest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is qiyas invalid on a ruling like the nullification of prayer by hadath (event)?
A) Because the hadith is weak.
B) Because the ruling's meaning is not rationally understood.
C) Because the ruling is based on qiyas already.
D) Because the ruling applies only to water.

Key Takeaway
A ruling must have a rationally understood meaning for valid qiyas; otherwise, it is confined to its specific case.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Qiyas in Linguistic Names: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Explaining the Hanafi position against qiyas in linguistic names and the dispute with the Shafi'i school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis reject extending linguistic names by qiyas, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf in practical cases like the graverobber and cooked wine.

Core Idea
Linguistic names are conventional, not rational; thus, qiyas cannot create new names.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi addresses a second condition for qiyas: it cannot be used to extend linguistic names (ishtiqaq). The Hanafi school firmly rejects qiyas in language, arguing that names are established by custom (wad') and Arab usage, not by analogy. The Shafi'i school, however, permits it in some cases. Practical examples include calling cooked wine 'khamr' and the graverobber 'sariq'—with consequences for hadd punishments.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the issue: qiyas in linguistic names
The passage asks whether names like 'khamr' (wine) or 'sariq' (thief) can be extended by analogy to other items sharing a characteristic (intoxication or secret taking).
This is not about legal rulings but about language itself: can we call cooked wine 'khamr' because it also intoxicates?
2
Identify the Shafi'i view and examples
Shafi'is argue that munassaf (cooked wine) can be called khamr because it intoxicates, and the nabbash (graverobber) can be called sariq because he takes property secretly. They analogize based on the shared cause (illa) of intoxication or secret taking.
The text records that some Shafi'is hold this view, though some of their own scholars disagree.
3
Understand the Hanafi counter-argument
Hanafis argue that linguistic names are conventional; Arabs did not extend names by analogy. For example, a black horse is called 'adham' but a black person is not; a red horse is 'kumayt' but a red garment is not. If qiyas in language were valid, these would be called by the same name, but they are not by consensus.
Thus, names are tied to specific usages, not to rational causes.
4
Apply to the examples: thamarah al-khilaf
Because Hanafis do not call cooked wine 'khamr', they do not apply the hadd punishment for drinking a drop of it—only if it intoxicates. And they do not cut the hand of the graverobber because he is not a 'sariq' in the linguistic sense that triggers the Quranic penalty.
Shafi'is, by extending the name, apply the same rulings.

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Usul al-Shashi discusses the conditions for valid qiyas. It begins by stating that a ruling from the original (asl) must have a rationally understood meaning ('illa) for qiyas to extend it to a branch (far'). The first example: if an event (hadath) occurs during prayer, the ruling that prayer is invalidated is established by text contrary to qiyas (because hadath contradicts prayer, but the text fixed it). Since the meaning is not rationally understood, qiyas cannot be applied to other situations. The Hanafi position is that such rulings are confined to their specific case, unlike the Shafi'is who allow qiyas on them. The text then discusses the hadith 'If water reaches two qullas, it does not carry impurity' and disputes its authenticity and applicability. Later, it addresses qiyas in linguistic names: whether names like 'khamr' (wine) or 'sariq' (thief) can be extended by analogy. The Hanafis argue that linguistic names are not established by qiyas, as shown by Arabs not calling a black person 'adham' or a red garment 'kumayt' despite shared attributes. The passage concludes with examples of cooked wine (munassaf) and the graverobber (nabbash), showing the Shafi'i position that these can be called by those names via qiyas, while the Hanafis restrict them to their original linguistic meanings.

Key Terms
القياس في اللغة (al-qiyas fi al-lugha): Extending a linguistic name to other items sharing a characteristic (e.g., calling cooked wine 'khamr' because it intoxicates).
المنصف (al-munassaf): Cooked wine (juice cooked until half remains); it is not considered khamr by the Hanafis unless it intoxicates.
النباش (al-nabbash): Graverobber who steals the shroud of a deceased person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of the Hanafi position on qiyas in language for the graverobber (nabbash)?
A) The graverobber's hand is cut because he is a thief.
B) The graverobber's hand is not cut because he is not linguistically a 'sariq'.
C) The graverobber is treated the same as any thief.
D) The graverobber receives a discretionary punishment instead.

Key Takeaway
Hanafis reject qiyas in linguistic names, confining names to their conventional usage, which leads to different legal outcomes in hudud and other rulings.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Invalidity of Linguistic Analogy (Qiyas fi al-Lugha)
Refutation of qiyas in language with examples and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects qiyas fi al-lugha and apply the distinction between linguistic names and legal causes.

Core Idea
Linguistic names are conventional; extending them by analogy destroys the specific legal causes set by the Law.

This lesson examines a critical usul principle: the invalidity of extending linguistic names by analogy (qiyas fi al-lugha). While qiyas is a valid source for extending legal rulings, it does not apply to the very names used in sacred texts. The passage refutes the idea that shared attributes (illa) can justify calling a new object by an existing name, using clear examples from Arab usage and highlighting the danger of undermining the specificity of legal causes (asbab shar'iyya). By the end, you will understand why the Hanafi school insists on the conventional nature of language in legal interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed analogy
Read the two examples: someone claims that 'munassaf' (concentrated grape juice) is called 'khamr' because it intoxicates, and that a grave-robber (nabbaash) is called 'sariq' because he takes property secretly. These are analogies based on shared attributes (illa).
Recognize that these are proposals to extend names, not rulings.
2
Understand the Hanafi refutation: linguistic convention
The text provides evidence from Arab usage: they call a black horse 'adham' but do not call a black person by that name. This shows that names are not universally applied based on attributes alone; they are conventional and restricted by custom.
The Arabs' non-extension disproves the analogy.
3
Understand the Hanafi refutation: legal cause specificity
If we extend names by analogy, the legal causes (e.g., theft as a cause for hadd) become more general. For instance, if 'sariq' is any secret taker, then the specific rules for theft would apply to grave-robbery, which was not intended by the Law. This invalidates the precise causes set by the Shariah.
The ruling is tied to the name, not the attribute alone.
4
Apply the principle to distinguish qiyas in language vs. qiyas in ahkam
Note that qiyas in rulings (qiyas shar'i) is valid when the illa is established from the text. But qiyas in language is invalid because names are fixed by convention (tawqif). Always check whether the analogy seeks to extend a name or a ruling.
This distinction prevents confusion in istinbat.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الرابع في القياس
فصل في شروط صحة القياس
المنصَّفُ حَمْرٌ؛ لأن الخَمْرَ إنما كان خمراً؛ لأنه يخامرُ العقل، وغيره يخامرُ العقل أيضًا، فيكون حمراً بالقياس.
والسارقُ إنما كانَ سارقاً؛ لأنه أخذ مال الغير بطريقة الخفية، وقد شاركه النباش في هذا المعنى، فيكون سارقاً بالقياس، وهذا قياس في اللغة مع اعترافه أن الإسم لم يوضع له في اللغة.
على السارق
القياس في اللغة
من الدهمة وهو السوداء
والدليل على فساد هذا النوع من القياس: أن العرب يُسَمِّي الفرس "أدهم" لسواده. و"كميتاً" الحمرته، ثم لا يُطْلقُ هذا الاسم على الزنجي والثوب الأَحْمَر .
من الكمت وهو الحمرة
العرب
ولو جَرَت المقايسة في الأسامي اللغوية لجاز ذلك لوجود العلة، ولأن هذا يؤدّي إلى إبطال الأسباب الشرعية؛ وذلك لأن الشرعَ جَعَل السرقة سبباً لنوع من الأحكام، فإذا علقنا الحكم بما هو أَعَمُّ من السرقة: وهو أخذُ مال الغير على طريق الخفية، تبيَّنَ أنَّ السبَبَ كان في الأصل معنى هو غير السرقة.
وهو ما يخامر العقل
وكذلك جَعَل شرب الخمر سبباً لنوع من الأحكام، فإذا علقنا الحكم بأمر أعم من الخَمْر تبيَّن أن الحكم كان في الأصل متعلّقاً بغير الخمر.
The fourth research on qiyas. Section on conditions for the validity of qiyas. Munassaf is khamr [by analogy]; because khamr is only khamr because it covers the mind, and other [drinks] also cover the mind, so it becomes khamr by qiyas. The thief is only a thief because he takes another's property secretly, and the grave-robber shares this meaning, so he becomes a thief by qiyas. This is qiyas in language while acknowledging that the name is not linguistically placed for it. The proof of the corruption of this type of qiyas: that the Arabs call a horse 'adham' because of its blackness, and 'kumayt' because of its redness, but they do not apply these names to a black person or a red garment. If analogy were applied in linguistic names, that would be permissible due to the existence of the cause, and because this leads to invalidating the legal causes; because the Law made theft a cause for a type of ruling, so if we attach the ruling to something more general than theft—namely taking another's property secretly—it becomes evident that the cause in the original was a meaning other than theft. Similarly, the Law made drinking khamr a cause for a type of ruling, so if we attach the ruling to something more general than khamr, it becomes evident that the ruling was originally attached to other than khamr.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage discusses the invalidity of qiyas in language (قياس في اللغة) as a method for extending linguistic names to new objects based on shared meanings. The author gives two examples: claiming that the drink 'munassaf' (a concentrated grape juice) is called 'khamr' because it intoxicates like wine, and claiming that a grave-robber is called 'sariq' (thief) because both take property secretly. Both are analogies based on the underlying cause (علة). The refutation is twofold: first, Arabs do not extend names by analogy (e.g., 'adham' for a black horse is not applied to a black person); second, such extension would undermine the specific legal causes (اسباب شرعية) set by the Law. For example, theft has specific rulings; if we extend 'sariq' to anyone taking secretly, we lose the specificity. Similarly for khamr. Thus, qiyas in language is invalid.

Key Terms
القياس في اللغة (al-qiyas fi al-lugha): Analogical extension of a linguistic name from its original object to another object sharing a common meaning (علة).
العلة (al-illa): The underlying cause or attribute that justifies the analogy.
المنصَّف (al-munassaf): A concentrated grape juice that intoxicates; used as an example in the passage.
النباش (al-nabbaash): A grave-robber; someone who steals from graves.
أدهم (adham): A black horse; used as evidence that Arabs do not extend the name to all black things.
كميت (kumayt): A red horse; similarly not applied to red garments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is qiyas in language invalid according to Hanafi usul?
A) Because Arabs never use analogical names
B) Because it would lead to invalidating the specific legal causes set by the Law
C) Because qiyas only applies to rulings, not names
D) Because it contradicts Quranic usage

Key Takeaway
Qiyas fi al-lugha is invalid because linguistic names are conventional, and extending them undermines the specificity of legal causes in the Shariah.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Fifth Condition of Qiyas: The Branch Must Not Be Explicitly Ruled
Fifth condition: far' must not be mansus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a proposed qiyas is invalid because the branch case has an explicit textual ruling (nass) and explain the Hanafi proof using the kaffarah example.

Core Idea
Qiyas cannot override a direct textual ruling; if the branch is ruled by nass, qiyas is invalid.

This lesson introduces the fifth condition of valid qiyas in Hanafi usul: the branch case (far') must not have an explicit ruling from a primary text (nass). When a text directly addresses the branch, there is no room for analogical extension. The classic example of freeing a slave in different expiations illustrates how this condition operates and how the Hanafi school defends it against objections.

Guided Path
1
State the condition
The fifth condition: for qiyas to be valid, the branch (far') must not be explicitly ruled by a text (nass). If it is, qiyas is impermissible because the text itself determines the ruling.
This condition prevents qiyas from overriding or contradicting a direct divine command.
2
Identify the attempted qiyas
Some scholars attempt to analogize freeing a disbelieving slave in kaffarah yamin and zihar to kaffarah qatl, where faith is required. They argue that since all expiations share the same purpose, the condition of faith should apply universally.
The opponent's position is that faith is necessary in all expiations via qiyas.
3
Examine the textual difference
The text for kaffarah qatl (Quran 4:92) explicitly requires a 'believing slave' (mu'mina). The texts for kaffarah yamin and zihar do not mention faith; they are unrestricted (mutlaq). This difference in the texts themselves is decisive.
The Hanafis argue that the unrestricted text for yamin and zihar indicates permissibility of any slave.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: qiyas is invalid because the branch has its own textual ruling. The unrestricted text (mutlaq) for yamin and zihar must be applied as it stands. Qiyas would effectively change that ruling, which is not allowed.
The condition ensures that textual rulings are not overridden by analogy.
5
Distinguish from other qiyas
The text addresses an objection: unlike this case, in other qiyas the ruling is extended to something not explicitly covered. Here, the branch is explicitly covered, so extension is unnecessary and invalid.
This distinction preserves the integrity of direct textual rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثالُ الشرط الخامس: وهو ما لا يكون الفَرْعُ منصوصاً عليه، كما يقال: إعتاق الرقبة الكافرة في كفارة اليمين والظهار لا يجوز بالقياس على كفارة القتل.
= لأنه أيضاً تعدية وهو يؤدي إلى إخراج النص من الخصوص إلى العموم؛ لأنا نقول: العلة في القياس الشرعي علم بخلاف ما ههنا فتفكر كذا قيل. فإذا علقنا الحكم إلخ: هذا منقوض بسائر الأقيسة؛ لأن الحكم لما تعدى إلى الفرع تعلق الحكم بأمر أعم من المنصوص وغيره؛ وذلك لأن أثر القياس في تغيير وصف الحكم من الخصوص إلى العموم لا في إثبات أصله، قلنا: فرق بين ما نحن فيه وبين الأقيسة الشرعية، وبين دلالات النصوص؛ لأن فيما نحن فيه إثبات الاسم الأعم أولاً، ثم جعل الحكم الأعم من النصوص تبعاً لإثبات الإثم، بخلاف سائر الأقيسة الشرعية ودلالات النصوص، فإنها ليست تعدية الاسم بل تعدية الحكم من الأصل إلى الفرع بعلة مشتركة بينهما، فإثبات الحكم في المنصوص لا النص، وفي المقيس بالعلة كذا في "شرح الحسامي". أعم من الخَمْر : هذا منقوض بسائر الأقيسة؛ لأن الحكم لما تعدى إلى الفرع تعلق الحكم بأمر أعم من المنصوص وغيره؛ وذلك لأن أثر القياس في تغيير وصف الحكم من الخصوص إلى العموم لا في إثبات أصله، وأيضاً هذا التعليل منقوض بالدلالات بأسرها كالقطع في الطرار، والجواب عنه ما قلنا كذا في كتب الأصول. ومثالُ الشرط الخامس: أي مثال فوات الشرط الخامس أنهم قالوا: لا يجوز إعتاق الرقبة الكافرة في كفارة اليمين والظهار بالقياس على كفارة القتل، فإن الإيمان شرط في كفارة القتل؛ لقوله تعالى: فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ قلنا: هذا القياس فاسد؛ لأن الرقبة في كفارة اليمين والظهار غير مقيدة بصفة الإيمان في النص، فكان موجب النص اجزاء =
And the example of the fifth condition: that the branch is not explicitly ruled upon by a text, as they say: It is not permissible to emancipate a disbelieving slave in the expiation of an oath and zihar by analogy with the expiation of killing. ... And the example of the fifth condition: i.e., the example of the absence of the fifth condition is that they said: It is not permissible to emancipate a disbelieving slave in expiation of an oath and zihar by analogy with expiation of killing, because faith is a condition in expiation of killing, due to His statement: 'So the freeing of a believing slave.' We say: This analogy is invalid because the slave in expiation of an oath and zihar is not restricted by the attribute of faith in the text, so the requirement of the text is that it suffices...
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage explains the fifth condition for the validity of qiyas (قياس) according to Hanafi usul: the branch case (فرع) must not have an explicit ruling in the primary texts (نص). The example given: some scholars (possibly Shafi'i) claim that emancipating a disbelieving slave in kaffarah yameen or zihar is not valid by analogy with kaffarah qatl, where faith (eman) is required by Quran (4:92). The Hanafi response is that the analogy is invalid because the text for kaffarah yameen and zihar does not restrict the slave by faith; hence the text itself indicates permissibility (ajza). The commentary then defends this position against objections, noting that qiyas transfers a ruling based on a shared cause, but if the branch already has a textual ruling, there is no need for qiyas. The passage also contrasts linguistic qiyas (which transfers names) with legal qiyas (which transfers rulings).

Key Terms
الشرط الخامس (ash-shart al-khamis): The fifth condition of qiyas: that the branch (far') is not explicitly ruled upon by a text (nass).

A) Because the text for kaffarah qatl is abrogated

C) Because qiyas cannot be applied to acts of worship (ibadat)
D) Because all expiations require a believing slave by consensus

Key Takeaway
The fifth condition of qiyas ensures that direct textual rulings are not overridden by analogical reasoning; where a nass exists, qiyas has no role.

The Fourth Condition of Qiyas: Invalidation of Legal Causes
Explains the fourth condition with examples of theft and wine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fourth condition of qiyas (ibṭāl al-asbāb al-sharʿiyya) and apply it to determine whether a qiyas is valid by preserving the specificity of the legal cause.

Core Idea
A valid qiyas must preserve the specific legal cause; broadening it invalidates the original cause.

The fourth condition of qiyas ensures that the legal cause (`illa) remains exactly as legislated, neither narrowed nor broadened. This passage explains why attaching a ruling to a more general category than the specified cause invalidates the cause itself, using the examples of theft and wine. The condition prevents the arbitrary redefinition of causes, maintaining the precision of Sharīʿa rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the fourth condition
Identify the condition: the legal cause must not be invalidated by redefining a more general category as the cause.
This is known as شرط إبطال الأسباب الشرعية.
2
Analyze the theft example
The Sharīʿa made theft (sariqa) the cause for cutting the hand. If we extend the ruling to the broader category 'taking property covertly', we imply that the real cause was not theft itself but that broader category, thus invalidating the original cause.
This would be invalid qiyas because the specific cause (theft) is ignored.
3
Analyze the wine example
Similarly, wine (khamr) is the cause for the ḥadd punishment. Broadening it to 'any intoxicant' would invalidate the specific cause of wine.
The ruling is tied to the substance, not the broader property of intoxication.
4
Examine the objection and response
An objection claims that all analogies broaden the description from particular to general. The response: analogy changes the ruling's applicability (from asl to farʿ) but does not alter the cause itself; the cause remains specific even though the ruling applies to a new case via the same cause.
The fourth condition only prohibits redefining the cause as something more general, not the natural extension of the ruling through qiyas.
5
Apply the condition
Given a new scenario, check whether the proposed cause matches the original cause exactly. If the cause is redefined to a broader category, the qiyas is invalid due to ibṭāl al-asbāb.
Practice with the examples in the practice tasks.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إبطال الأسباب الشرعية؛ وذلك لأن الشرعَ جَعَل السرقة سبباً لنوع من الأحكام، فإذا علقنا الحكم بما هو أَعَمُّ من السرقة: وهو أخذُ مال الغير على طريق الخفية، تبيَّنَ أنَّ السبَبَ كان في الأصل معنى هو غير السرقة. وهو ما يخامر العقل كذلك جَعَل شرب الخمر سبباً لنوع من الأحكام، فإذا علقنا الحكم بأمر أعم من الخَمْر تبيَّن أن الحكم كان في الأصل متعلّقاً بغير الخمر. أعم من الخَمْر : هذا منقوض بسائر الأقيسة؛ لأن الحكم لما تعدى إلى الفرع تعلق الحكم بأمر أعم من المنصوص وغيره؛ وذلك لأن أثر القياس في تغيير وصف الحكم من الخصوص إلى العموم لا في إثبات أصله، وأيضاً هذا التعليل منقوض بالدلالات بأسرها كالقطع في الطرار، والجواب عنه ما قلنا كذا في كتب الأصول.
Invalidation of legal causes: because the Law made theft a cause for a type of ruling, so if we attach the ruling to what is more general than theft – namely taking the property of another in a hidden manner – it becomes clear that the cause was in origin a meaning other than theft. This is what the mind perceives. Similarly, He made wine-drinking a cause for a type of ruling, so if we attach the ruling to something more general than wine, it becomes clear that the ruling was originally connected to other than wine. 'More general than wine': this is refuted by all analogies, because when the ruling extends to the branch, it attaches to something more general than what is textually stipulated and other than it; that is because the effect of analogy is to change the description of the ruling from particularity to generality, not to establish its origin. Also, this reasoning is refuted by all indications like cutting in pickpocketing. The response is what we said as in the books of Usul.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage explains the fourth condition for the validity of qiyas: the legal cause must not be invalidated. The author illustrates with two examples from the Sharia: theft and wine. If we take the ruling of theft (cutting of the hand) and attach it to a broader category like 'taking another's property secretly,' we would be invalidating the specific cause (theft) and implying that the ruling was actually based on a different meaning. Similarly, the ruling for wine (hadd) is tied to the specific substance, so broadening it invalidates the cause. The commentary then addresses a potential objection: that all analogies broaden the ruling, but the response is that analogy changes the ruling from particular to general without changing the cause. The fourth condition ensures that the cause remains specific and is not redefined by broader categories.

Key Terms
إبطال الأسباب الشرعية (Ibṭāl al-Asbāb al-Sharʿiyya): The invalidation of legal causes by attaching the ruling to a broader category than the specific cause.
قياس (Qiyas): Analogy in Islamic jurisprudence; extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') due to a shared effective cause (illa).
علة (ʿIlla): The effective cause or ratio legis that connects the ruling to the case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid to attach the ḥadd ruling of theft to the broader category of 'taking another's property covertly'?
A) Because theft is not included in that category
B) Because it invalidates the specific cause (theft) and implies the ruling was based on something else
C) Because qiyas cannot be applied to hudud punishments
D) Because the category is too narrow

Key Takeaway
The fourth condition of qiyas requires that the legal cause remain exactly as legislated; broadening it to a more general category invalidates the cause and renders the analogy invalid.

The Fifth Condition: The Branch Must Not Be Textually Ruled (Example 1: Oath and Zihar Expiation)
Explains first example of fifth condition: analogy to restrict mutlaq is invalid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fifth condition of qiyas by identifying that the branch case (oath/zihar expiation) has an absolute text and explaining why analogy to the restricted text (killing expiation) is invalid.

Core Idea
An absolute text cannot be restricted by analogy.

This lesson explains the first example of the fifth condition. The Hanafi school holds that the texts for oath and zihar expiation command freeing any slave without qualification. An attempt to analogize to killing expiation, which requires a believing slave, fails because it would contradict the absolute text. Understanding this requires careful parsing of mutlaq and muqayyad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposed analogy
The asl is killing expiation (requires believing slave). The far' is oath/zihar expiation. The illa is that both are expiations (kaffarah).
This is the qiyas that the Hanafis reject.
2
Recognize the Hanafi objection
The far' has an absolute text: 'free a slave' without qualification. Appending faith by analogy would nullify the mutlaq ruling.
The branch is textually ruled by the mutlaq verse.
3
Distinguish mutlaq from muqayyad
The verses for oath and zihar say 'free a slave'; the verse for killing says 'free a believing slave'. The first two are mutlaq, the last is muqayyad.
Key Quranic evidence.
4
Understand the ruling
The analogy is invalid because it would impose a condition not present in the text. The condition of faith cannot be added via qiyas.
Result: Any slave suffices for oath/zihar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومثالُ الشرط الخامس: وهو ما لا يكون الفَرْعُ منصوصاً عليه، كما يقال: إعتاق الرقبة الكافرة في كفارة اليمين والظهار لا يجوز بالقياس على كفارة القتل، فإن الإيمان شرط في كفارة القتل؛ لقوله تعالى: فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ قلنا: هذا القياس فاسد؛ لأن الرقبة في كفارة اليمين والظهار غير مقيدة بصفة الإيمان في النص، فكان موجب النص إجزاء مطلق الرقبة مؤمنة كانت أو كافرة، فكان شرط الإيمان إبطال موجب النص وهو إطلاق الحكم. كفارة اليمين إلخ آية كفارة اليمين قوله تعالى: ﴿فَكَفَّارَتُهُ إطْعَامُ عَشَرَة مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطَ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ أَوْ كِسْوَتُهُمْ أَوْ تَحْرِير رقبة، وآية كفارة الظهار قوله تعالى: ﴿وَالَّذِينَ يُظَاهِرُونَ مِنْ نِسَائِهِمْ ثُمَّ يَعُودُونَ لَمَا قَالُوا فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ ، وآية كفارة القتل قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ قَتَلَ مُؤْمِناً خَطَأَ فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ ، فالرقبة في الأوليين مطلقة، وفي كفارة القتل مقيدة بالإيمان يستأنف الإطعام أي عند الإمام الشافعي خلافاً لأبي حنيفة. بالقياس على الصوم فإنه يستأنف لو جامع في خلاله، والجامع أن كلاً منهما كفارة ظهار، قلنا: هذا القياس لا يجوز؛ لأن النص في الإطعام مطلق عن قيد المساس؛ وذلك لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مسكينا، فإنه شرط في الصيام خلوه عن المسيس، وأطلق الإطعام، فكان موجبه جواز الإطعام على الإطلاق، فلو شرط في الإطعام خلوه عن المسيس بالقياس على الصوم؛ لأن كل واحد منهما كفارة الظهار كان تركاً لإطلاق النص بالقياس، وذا لا يجوز. للمحضر الإحصار في اللغة: المنع والمحصر هو الممنوع، وشرعاً : المنع عن الحج والوقوف بعرفة معاً، أو العمرة بعد الإحرام بعذر شرعي أن يتحلل بالصوم إلخ: اعلم أن المحصر إذا لم يقدر على الهدي يبقى محرماً ولا يتحلل عندنا، وقال الشافعي له: حلل بالصوم أي يصوم ثلاثة أيام في الحج، وسبعة إذا رجع تلك عشرة كاملة والعلة الجامعة هي: العجز عن الهدي، قلنا: هذا القياس غير صحيح؛ لأن الفرع منصوص عليه، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُؤُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدْيُ مَحلَّهُ فيبقى محرماً. على قضاء رَمَضان: قلنا: هذا القياس غير صحيح؛ لأن الفرع منصوص عليه؛ لما روي أن عمر أذن رجلاً بالدم، قال له: تمتعت ولم أصم حتى مضى يوم عرفة، فقال: عليك الهدي، فقال الرجل: لا أجد فقال: سل عن قومك، فقال الرجل: ما ههنا أحد من قومي، فقال عمر لغلام: أعطه ثمن شاة حيث نص فيه بالهدي، فلا يجوز الصوم.
Example of the fifth condition: that the branch is not textually ruled. As it is said: Emancipating a disbelieving slave in the expiation of an oath and zihar is not permissible by analogy with the expiation of intentional killing, because faith is a condition in the expiation of killing due to His saying: 'free a believing slave.' We say: This analogy is invalid because the slave in the expiation of oath and zihar is not restricted by the attribute of faith in the text, so the import of the text is that any slave is sufficient, whether believing or disbelieving. So stipulating faith would nullify the import of the text, which is the absolute ruling. The verse of oath expiation is His saying: '... its expiation is feeding ten needy persons from the average of what you feed your families, or clothing them, or freeing a slave.' And the verse of zihar expiation: 'Those who pronounce zihar among you and then return to what they said, [the penalty is] freeing a slave.' And the verse of intentional killing: 'And whoever kills a believer by mistake, [the penalty is] freeing a believing slave.' So the slave in the first two is absolute, and in killing expiation it is restricted by faith. He restarts the feeding according to Imam al-Shafi'i, contrary to Abu Hanifa. By analogy with fasting, for he restarts if he has intercourse during it, and the commonality is that each is an expiation of zihar. We say: This analogy is not allowed because the text on feeding is absolute regarding the restriction of contact; due to His saying: 'For those who are unable, feeding sixty needy persons.' For he stipulated in fasting that it be free from sexual contact, and he made the feeding absolute. So its import is the permissibility of feeding absolutely. If one were to stipulate in feeding freedom from contact by analogy with fasting, because each is zihar expiation, that would be abandoning the absolute text by analogy, and that is not allowed. For the muhsar (one prevented): the preventer is the one prevented, and legally it is prevention from Hajj and standing at Arafah together, or from Umrah after ihram due to a legitimate excuse. He may perform the tahallul (release from ihram) by fasting: Know that the muhsar if he cannot afford the hady (sacrificial animal) remains in ihram and does not break it according to us, but al-Shafi'i says he breaks it by fasting, i.e., he fasts three days during Hajj and seven after returning, that makes ten complete, and the common illa is inability to afford the hady. We say: This analogy is invalid because the branch is textually ruled, i.e., His saying: 'And do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place,' so he remains in ihram. On the analogy of making up Ramadan: We say: This analogy is invalid because the branch is textually ruled; for it is narrated that Umar permitted a man to offer blood: the man said, 'I performed tamattu and did not fast until the day of Arafah had passed,' so Umar said: 'You must offer a hady.' The man said, 'I cannot find it.' He said: 'Ask your people.' The man said, 'There is no one here from my people.' So Umar told a boy: 'Give him the price of a sheep.' Since the text specifies the hady, fasting is not permissible.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This lesson explains the fifth condition for a valid qiyas: the branch (far') must not already have an explicit textual ruling. If it does, analogy cannot be applied. The author provides three examples where people attempted analogy but the Hanafi position rejects them because the branch has a clear text.

First example: Some argue that freeing a disbelieving slave in oath or zihar expiation is invalid by analogy to intentional killing expiation, where a believing slave is required. The Hanafi response: The verses for oath and zihar say 'free a slave' without qualification, so any slave suffices. Adding the condition of faith via analogy would contradict the absolute text. This is forbidden.

Second example: Intercourse during the feeding expiation of zihar does not require restarting the expiation by analogy with fasting, where intercourse invalidates it and requires a fresh fast. Imam al-Shafi'i holds this analogy, but the Hanafis reject it because the text on feeding is absolute and does not mention invalidation by intercourse, while the text on fasting explicitly requires seclusion from women. Adding a condition by analogy would be abandoning the absolute text.

Third example: The muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj) may not break his ihram by fasting by analogy with the mutamatti' (one performing tamattu') who fasts if unable to offer sacrifice. The Hanafis argue that the muhsar has a direct text in the Quran: 'Do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place.' So he cannot substitute fasting; he remains in ihram until he can offer a sacrifice.

Fourth example: The mutamatti' who fails to fast before the Day of Arafah cannot compensate by fasting after the days of Tashreeq by analogy with making up missed Ramadan fasts. The text, as shown by Umar's ruling, requires a sacrifice (hady) in this case, so the branch is textually ruled.

The core principle: Where the Sharia has provided a specific ruling for a case, qiyas ceases to operate. This is a fundamental Hanafi rule.

Key Terms
الفرع (al-farʻ): The branch case in qiyas that is not explicitly ruled in the texts but is compared to the original (asl).
منصوص عليه (manṣūṣ ʻalayhi): A case that has an explicit ruling in the Quran or Sunnah, which blocks the application of qiyas.
مطلق (muṭlaq): A text that is unrestricted; it applies without conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it invalid to require a believing slave in oath expiation by analogy with intentional killing expiation?
A) Because oath expiation is lighter than killing expiation
B) Because the text for oath expiation says 'free a slave' without qualification
C) Because there is no common illa between them
D) Because analogy is not applicable to expiations

Key Takeaway
Analogy cannot restrict an absolute text; the branch must not be textually ruled.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

The Fifth Condition: Further Examples (Zihar Feeding, Muhsar, and Tamattu')
Explains three more examples of fifth condition: all analogies invalid because branch textually ruled.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the fifth condition by identifying that the branch has an explicit text and explaining why analogies regarding zihar feeding, muhsar's tahallul, and tamattu' compensation are invalid.

Core Idea
When the text explicitly rules a case, qiyas is blocked, even if a common illa seems plausible.

This lesson covers the second, third, and fourth examples of the fifth condition. The second example deals with intercourse during the feeding expiation of zihar; the third with the muhsar (one prevented from Hajj); the fourth with the tamattu' pilgrim who fails to fast. In each, the Hanafi school rejects the analogy because the branch has a direct textual ruling.

Guided Path
1
Second example: Intercourse during zihar feeding
Identify the proposed analogy: asl = fasting in zihar expiation (intercourse invalidates and requires restart), far' = feeding in zihar expiation, illa = both are zihar expiations. The Hanafi objection: the text on feeding is absolute and does not mention invalidation by intercourse; the text on fasting explicitly requires seclusion from women. Adding a condition by analogy would abandon the absolute text.
The verse is 'feeding sixty needy' without mention of contact.
2
Third example: Muhsar's tahallul
Proposed analogy: asl = mutamatti' who cannot afford hady (fasts), far' = muhsar who cannot afford hady, illa = inability to sacrifice. Hanafi objection: the muhsar has a direct text 'do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place', so he remains in ihram until he can offer hady.
Text from Quran 2:196.
3
Fourth example: Tamattu' compensation
Proposed analogy: asl = making up missed Ramadan fasts, far' = tamattu' pilgrim who missed fasting before Arafah, illa = obligation to fast. Hanafi objection: the branch is textually ruled by the hadith of Umar: he required a sacrifice (hady) for the tamattu' who did not fast, not fasting compensation.
Branch is ruled by the Sunnah (Umar's ruling).

ومثالُ الشرط الخامس: وهو ما لا يكون الفَرْعُ منصوصاً عليه، كما يقال: إعتاق الرقبة الكافرة في كفارة اليمين والظهار لا يجوز بالقياس على كفارة القتل، فإن الإيمان شرط في كفارة القتل؛ لقوله تعالى: فَتَحْرِيرُ رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ قلنا: هذا القياس فاسد؛ لأن الرقبة في كفارة اليمين والظهار غير مقيدة بصفة الإيمان في النص، فكان موجب النص إجزاء مطلق الرقبة مؤمنة كانت أو كافرة، فكان شرط الإيمان إبطال موجب النص وهو إطلاق الحكم. كفارة اليمين إلخ آية كفارة اليمين قوله تعالى: ﴿فَكَفَّارَتُهُ إطْعَامُ عَشَرَة مَسَاكِينَ مِنْ أَوْسَطَ مَا تُطْعِمُونَ أَهْلِيكُمْ أَوْ كِسْوَتُهُمْ أَوْ تَحْرِير رقبة، رَقَبَةٍ مُؤْمِنَةٍ ، فالرقبة في الأوليين مطلقة، وفي كفارة القتل مقيدة بالإيمان يستأنف الإطعام أي عند الإمام الشافعي خلافاً لأبي حنيفة. بالقياس على الصوم فإنه يستأنف لو جامع في خلاله، والجامع أن كلاً منهما كفارة ظهار، قلنا: هذا القياس لا يجوز؛ لأن النص في الإطعام مطلق عن قيد المساس؛ وذلك لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَمَنْ لَمْ يَسْتَطِعْ فَإِطْعَامُ سِتِّينَ مسكينا، فإنه شرط في الصيام خلوه عن المسيس، وأطلق الإطعام، فكان موجبه جواز الإطعام على الإطلاق، فلو شرط في الإطعام خلوه عن المسيس بالقياس على الصوم؛ لأن كل واحد منهما كفارة الظهار كان تركاً لإطلاق النص بالقياس، وذا لا يجوز. للمحضر الإحصار في اللغة: رُؤُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدْيُ مَحلَّهُ فيبقى محرماً. على قضاء رَمَضان: قلنا: هذا القياس غير صحيح؛ لأن الفرع منصوص عليه؛ لما روي أن عمر أذن رجلاً بالدم، قال له: تمتعت ولم أصم حتى مضى يوم عرفة، Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Invalidity of Qiyas When the Branch Is Ruled by a Text
Shows that qiyas fails when the branch is already ruled by a nass

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when qiyas is invalid because the branch case is already ruled by a primary text (nass), and apply this principle to new cases involving ibadah and muamalat.

Core Idea
Qiyas is invalid when the branch is already ruled by a nass — text overrides analogy.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, qiyas is a valid source of law only when the branch case (far') has no explicit ruling from the Quran, Sunnah, or Ijma. If a text already governs the branch, qiyas cannot override it. This lesson examines two concrete examples from Hajj: the muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj) and the mutamatti' who fails to fast before 'Arafah. Both illustrate the principle that a nass on the branch blocks qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed qiyas
First, recognize that the Shafi'i school attempts to analogize the muhsar to the mutamatti' who cannot sacrifice, allowing fasting as a substitute. The common cause (illa) is 'inability to afford a sacrifice'.
2
Identify the branch case (far')
The branch is the muhsar (person prevented from Hajj). In the second example, the branch is a mutamatti' who did not fast before 'Arafah and wants to fast after it as a substitute.
3
Locate the nass that rules the branch
For the muhsar, the Quran says: 'Do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place' (2:196). This implies the muhsar must remain in ihram and cannot exit by fasting. For the mutamatti', the action of Umar (as narrated) shows that the ruling is fixed as a sacrifice, not fasting.
The nass may be from Quran, Sunnah, or even a Companion's ruling (which is treated as a nass in this context).
4
Conclude that qiyas is invalid
Because the branch is already ruled by a text, qiyas cannot override it. The claimed qiyas is rejected (man' al-far'). This is a key condition for the validity of qiyas in Hanafi usul.
This principle applies even if the 'illa is sound; the existence of a nass on the branch takes precedence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
للمحصر الإحصار في اللغة: المنع والمحصر هو الممنوع، وشرعاً : المنع عن الحج والوقوف بعرفة معاً، أو العمرة بعد الإحرام بعذر شرعي [حاشية الشيخ أكرم الندوي: ص ٢٢٧] أن يتحلل بالصوم إلخ: اعلم أن المحصر إذا لم يقدر على الهدي يبقى محرماً ولا يتحلل عندنا، وقال الشافعي له: حلل بالصوم أي يصوم ثلاثة أيام في الحج، وسبعة إذا رجع تلك عشرة كاملة والعلة الجامعة هي: العجز عن الهدي، قلنا: هذا القياس غير صحيح؛ لأن الفرع منصوص عليه، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُؤُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدْيُ مَحَلَّهُ﴾ فيبقى محرماً. على قضاء رَمَضان: قلنا: هذا القياس غير صحيح؛ لأن الفرع منصوص عليه؛ لما روي أن عمر رضي الله عنه أذن رجلاً بالدم، قال له: تمتعت ولم أصم حتى مضى يوم عرفة، فقال: عليك الهدي، فقال الرجل: لا أجد فقال: "سل عن قومك"، فقال الرجل: ما ههنا أحد من قومي، فقال عمر لغلام: "أعطه ثمن شاة" حيث نص فيه بالهدي، فلا يجوز الصوم.
For the one prevented (al-muhsar): al-ihsar linguistically means prevention, and the muhsar is the prevented one. Legally: prevention from Hajj and standing at Arafah together, or from Umrah after ihram due to a legitimate excuse [Hashiyah of Shaykh Akram al-Nadwi: p. 227]. That he may exit ihram by fasting, etc.: Know that the muhsar, if he cannot afford the sacrificial animal, remains in ihram and does not exit ihram according to us. And al-Shafi'i said to him: you may exit ihram by fasting, i.e., fast three days during Hajj and seven when you return, that is ten complete. And the common cause is inability to afford the sacrificial animal. We say: This analogy is not valid because the branch is ruled by text, which is His saying, Most High: 'And do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place.' So he remains in ihram. Regarding making up Ramadan: We say: This analogy is not valid because the branch is ruled by text; based on the narration that Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, granted a man permission for blood. He said: I performed tamattu' and did not fast until the Day of Arafah passed. He said: Upon you is a sacrificial animal. The man said: I cannot find [one]. He said: Ask your people. The man said: There is no one from my people here. So Umar said to his servant: Give him the price of a sheep. So he ruled by the sacrificial animal, thus fasting is not permissible.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage provides two further examples of invalid qiyas, both because the branch case is already ruled by a text (nass). The first case: a person prevented (muhsar) from completing Hajj. The Shafi'i school allows him to exit ihram by fasting by qiyas to the mutamatti' (one who performs tamattu') who cannot sacrifice. The common cause is inability to afford the sacrificial animal. The Hanafi response: this qiyas is invalid because the branch (the muhsar) is already ruled by the Quranic verse: 'Do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place.' This verse implies that the muhsar remains in ihram unless he sends a sacrifice; fasting is not an alternative. The second case: a mutamatti' who did not fast before the Day of Arafah wishes to fast after it by qiyas to making up missed Ramadan fasts. The Hanafi response: this qiyas is also invalid because the branch (fasting after 'Arafah as a substitute for the sacrificial animal) is already ruled by the action of Umar, who commanded a mutamatti' who could not sacrifice to give the price of a sheep, not to fast. Thus the ruling is already specified by the text (or practice of the Companion), and qiyas cannot override it. Both examples illustrate the principle that qiyas is only valid when the branch is not already covered by a nass.

Key Terms
محصر (muhsar): One who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to a legitimate excuse such as illness or enemy.
فرع منصوص عليه (far' mansus 'alayh): The branch case that is already ruled by a text (Quran, Sunnah, or Companion's ruling), making qiyas inapplicable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is invalid when the branch case is already governed by a primary text (Quran, Sunnah, or Companion's ruling), as seen in the muhsar and mutamatti' examples.
