Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
12 min
Definition of Qiyas and the Sources of the 'Illa
Defines legal analogy and explains the sources for identifying the effective cause

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas shar'i, identify the five valid sources for knowing the 'illa, and distinguish the Hanafi position that the ruling in the original case is by the text itself, not by the 'illa.

Core Idea
Qiyas applies a ruling to a new case due to a shared 'illa, but the ruling in the original case is by the text, not the 'illa.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi defines legal analogy (qiyas) and explains how the effective cause ('illa) is known. It also presents a key theoretical dispute among scholars: does the ruling in the original text attach by the text itself or by the 'illa? Understanding this distinction is essential for correct istinbat and determines the scope of qiyas in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition
The passage defines qiyas shar'i as 'the attachment of a ruling to an unstated case based on a meaning that is the effective cause for that ruling in the stated case.' Identify the four components: asl (original case), far' (new case), hukm (ruling), and 'illa (effective cause).
The definition explicitly ties the ruling in the branch to the 'illa in the original.
2
Identify the sources of the 'illa
The 'illa is known from five sources: the Quran, the Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), ijtihad, and deduction (istinbat). These are the only valid ways to establish that a particular attribute is the effective cause.
3
Analyze the Quranic example
The verse (24:58) states there is no blame upon entering at three times, and the cause is given as 'frequent comers' (طوافون). The Prophet (peace be upon him) applied this same cause to the cat's leftover (sawr al-hirra), concluding that its impurity is removed due to the frequency of the cat's movement.
The original case: slaves and maids frequent coming; ruling: no blame. The branch: cat frequent coming; ruling: no impurity.
4
Compare the two theoretical positions
The Iraq scholars (Hanafis) hold that the ruling in the original case is established by the very text itself, not by the 'illa. The Samarqand scholars and al-Shafi'i hold that the ruling is established by the 'illa, and the text merely indicates the 'illa. This difference affects whether the 'illa can be used to extend the ruling independently of the text.
5
Determine the Hanafi tarjih
The author sides with the Iraq (Hanafi) position: the ruling is by the text, and the 'illa is only for extension. This is the default in Hanafi usul and restricts qiyas by requiring the 'illa to be extracted from the text, not the text itself.
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah and other Hanafi works follow this view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في القياس الشرعي: القياسُ الشرعي: هو ترتب الحكم في غير المنصوص عليه على معنى هو علة لذلك الحكم في المنصوص عليه. ثم إنما يُعرفُ كون المعنى علة بالكتاب، وبالسنَّة، وبالإجماع، وبالإجتهاد، وبالإستنباط. فمثال العلة المعلومة بالكتاب: كثرة الطواف، فإنها جُعَلَتْ علةً لسقوط الحَرَج في الاستئذان في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَيْسَ عَلَيْكُمْ وَلا عَلَيْهِمْ جُنَاحٌ بَعْدَهُنَّ طَوَّافُونَ عَلَيْكُمْ بَعْضُكُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ﴾، ثم أسقط رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حرج نجاسة سؤر الهرة بحكم هذه العلة. القياسُ الشرعي: لما فرغ المصنف من بيان شرائط القياس شرع في تعريفه وركنه وهو العلة، فقال في بيان الأول: القياس الشرعي، وفي بيان الثاني: إنما يعرف كون المعنى. ترتب الحكم إلخ : اعلم أن القياسين اختلفوا في أن الحكم في المنصوص عليه يثبت بعين النص أو بالعلة التي في النص، قال مشايخ العراق الحكم في المنصوص عليه بعين النص لا بالعلة، وإنما العلة وضعت للدلالة على ثبوت الحكم في الفرع، وقال مشايخ سمرقند: إن الحكم يثبت بالعلة التي في النص لا بالنص، فمتى وجد مثله في موضع آخر يتعدى إليه، وإنما النص لمعرفته لا لثبوته وهو قول الشافعي، فعلى هذا قوله: ترتب الحكم إلى آخره إشارة إلى القول الثاني. "المعدن" ثم إنما يُعرفُ إلخ: اعلم أن الأصل في النصوص التعليل عند العامة، لكنهم اتفقوا على أنه لا يصح التعليل بجميع أوصاف النص؛ لأنه لا تأثير لكثير من الأوصاف في الحكم، فإن التركي والهندي ونحوهما سواء في قوله عليه السلام للجامع في نهار رمضان: "أعتق رقبة"، ولا أثر لها في إيجاب عتق رقبة، وكذا وصف الحرية ووقاع الأهل حتى تجب الكفارة على العبد بالزنا وبوطء الأمة، واتفقوا أيضاً على أنه لا يصح بأي وصف شاء المعلل من غير دليل، فإذن لابد من دليل يعرف به كون المعنى علته، وهو إما الكتاب أو السنة أو الإجماع أو الاجتهاد كذا في "الفصول". جُنَاحٌ: أي لا إثم عليكم ولا عليهم في الدخول في هذه الأوقات الثلاث، وبين علته بقوله: "طوافون عليكم". بَعْدَهُنَّ: أي الأوقات الثلاثة قبل صلاة الفجر، وحين تضعون ثيابكم من الظهيرة، ومن بعد صلاة العشاء. بحكم هذه العلة: أي كثرة الطواف فالمقيس الهرة والمقيس عليه العبيد والجواري، والعلة كثرة الطواف، والحكم هو سقوط حرج نجاسة سؤر الهرة التي هو من جنس سقوط حرج الاستئذان عن العبيد والإماء كذا قال المولوي عين الله.
Chapter on Legal Analogy: Legal analogy is the attachment of a ruling to an unstated case based on a meaning that is the effective cause for that ruling in the stated case. Then, that the meaning is a cause is known by the Book, by the Sunnah, by consensus, by ijtihad, and by deduction. An example of a cause known by the Book: frequency of coming and going, for it was made a cause for removal of difficulty in seeking permission in His saying, Most High: 'There is no blame upon you nor upon them after them, they are frequent comers to you, some of you upon others.' Then the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, removed the difficulty of the impurity of the cat's leftover by virtue of this cause. Legal analogy: When the author finished explaining the conditions of analogy, he began defining it and its pillar, which is the cause. So he said regarding the first: Legal analogy. And regarding the second: That the meaning is known. 'The attachment of the ruling', etc.: Know that the two groups of analogy scholars disagreed about whether the ruling in the stated case is established by the very text or by the cause in the text. The scholars of Iraq said: The ruling in the stated case is by the very text, not by the cause. The cause is only placed to indicate the establishment of the ruling in the branch. The scholars of Samarqand said: The ruling is established by the cause in the text, not by the text. Whenever a similar [cause] is found in another place, it extends to it. The text is only for its knowledge, not for its establishment. That is the statement of al-Shafi'i. According to this, his saying: 'the attachment of the ruling' etc. refers to the second statement. 'al-Ma'din'. Then 'That it is known', etc.: Know that the principle in texts is that they are reasoned, according to the majority. But they agreed that it is not valid to reason by all attributes of the text, because many attributes have no effect on the ruling. For example, the Turk and the Indian and the like are equal in his saying, peace be upon him, to the one who had intercourse during Ramadan: 'Free a slave.' And [the attribute of nationality] has no effect on obligating freeing a slave. Likewise the attribute of freedom and cohabitation with the wife, such that expiation becomes obligatory upon the slave due to adultery and intercourse with a slave-girl. And they also agreed that it is not valid to reason by any attribute the reasoner wishes without evidence. So there must be evidence by which the meaning is known to be a cause. That is either the Book, or the Sunnah, or consensus, or ijtihad. As in 'al-Fusul'. 'Junah': i.e., there is no sin upon you nor upon them in entering at these three times. He explained its cause by His saying: 'frequent comers to you'. 'After them': i.e., the three times: before the Fajr prayer, when you put off your clothes at noon, and after the Isha prayer. 'By virtue of this cause': i.e., frequency of coming and going. So the analogized case is the cat, and the case being analogized to is the slaves and slave-girls, and the cause is frequency of coming and going, and the ruling is the removal of difficulty of the impurity of the cat's leftover, which is of the same kind as the removal of difficulty of seeking permission for slaves and maidservants. Thus said Mawlawi 'Ayn Allah.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of qiyas (legal analogy) from a Hanafi usul work. The author defines qiyas as: 'the attachment of a ruling to an unstated case based on a meaning that is the effective cause ('illa) for that ruling in the stated case.' The 'illa must be known from valid sources: the Quran, Sunnah, consensus (ijma'), ijtihad, or deduction (istinbat). The example from the Quran: the verse about no blame on entering at three times, where the cause is frequent coming and going. The Prophet (peace be upon him) then applied this cause to remove the difficulty regarding the cat's leftover (i.e., it is pure). This shows how qiyas works: the original case (slaves frequent coming) has a ruling (no blame), the cause (frequent coming) is identified, and the branch case (cat frequent coming) receives the same ruling (no impurity). The passage then discusses a deeper theoretical dispute: do rulings in the original case attach by the very text, or by the 'illa? The Iraq scholars (Hanafi tradition) say the ruling is by the text itself; the 'illa only serves to extend the ruling to new cases. The Samarqand scholars and al-Shafi'i say the ruling is established by the 'illa, so wherever the 'illa exists, the ruling applies, and the text merely indicates the 'illa. This difference affects the scope of qiyas: if ruling is by text, the text cannot be extended beyond its explicit words unless the 'illa is extracted; if by 'illa, the 'illa is the basis and can apply broadly. The author sides with the Iraq scholars (Hanafi view). Finally, the passage emphasizes that not every attribute of a text is a valid 'illa; only those that are relevant and have a demonstrated effect on the ruling. An 'illa must be proven by evidence, not chosen arbitrarily.

Key Terms
علة ('illa): The effective cause that necessitates the ruling; known from text or ijtihad.
قياس شرعي (qiyas shar'i): Legal analogy: applying a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared 'illa.
ترتب الحكم (tarattub al-hukm): The attachment/assigning of the ruling; in the definition, the ruling of the original is placed on the branch.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is the 'illa known?
A) Only from the Quran and Sunnah.
B) From the Quran, Sunnah, consensus, ijtihad, and deduction.
C) From the consensus of the companions only.
D) From the mujtahid's personal preference.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, the ruling in the text is by the text; the 'illa is only for extending the ruling to new cases, and it must be proven from valid sources.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Definition of Qiyas and Recognizing the 'Illa
Definition of legal analogy and identification of the effective cause with Quranic example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qiyas as per Hanafi usul, identify the four sources for recognizing the 'illa, and apply the definition to the cat's saliva example.

Core Idea
Qiyas attaches a ruling to a new case by proving a shared effective cause ('illa) known through Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, or Ijtihad.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi defines legal analogy (qiyas) and explains how the effective cause ('illa) is recognized. Understanding qiyas is essential for deducing rulings in cases not explicitly mentioned in the primary sources. The passage also illustrates the method with the famous example of the cat's saliva, which is purified despite its frequency in houses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and its components
Read the definition carefully: 'trattub al-hukm fi ghayr al-mansus 'alayhi 'ala ma'na huwa 'illa li-dhalika al-hukm fi al-mansus 'alayhi.' Break it down: the ruling (hukm) from a textual case (mansus 'alayhi) is attached (yutarattab) to a non-textual case (ghayr al-mansus 'alayhi) based on a meaning (ma'na) that is the effective cause ('illa) of that ruling.
The definition implies the 'illa is the basis for extension, not just any similarity.
2
Recognize the four sources for knowing the 'illa
The passage states the 'illa is known by al-Kitab, al-Sunnah, al-Ijma, and al-Ijtihad/al-Istinbat. For each source, understand that a description must be proven as the effective cause, not merely assumed. The Quranic example of 'kathrat al-tawaf' is a direct textual indication.
Not all descriptions in a text are valid 'illas; they must be supported by evidence.
3
Understand the dispute about the 'illa's role
The passage presents two views: (1) The ruling in the original text is established by the text itself, and the 'illa is only for extension; (2) The ruling is established by the 'illa, and the text merely informs us of the 'illa. The author sides with the second view, as the definition ties the ruling directly to the 'illa.
This dispute affects whether the extended case includes all similar animals (e.g., mice) or only the specific animal (cat) mentioned in the hadith.

"المعدن"

الهرة
فقال علي: "الهرة ليست بنجسة، فإنها من الطوافين عليكم والطوافات". فقاس أصحابنا لله جميع ما يسكن في البيوت كالفأرة والحية على الهرة بعلة الطواف. وكذلك قوله تعالى: ﴿يُرِيدُ اللهُ بكُمُ الْيُسْرَ وَلا يُرِيدُ بِكُمُ الْعُسْرَ﴾ بين الشرع أن الإفطار للمريض والمسافر لتيسير الأمر عليهم ليتمكنوا من تحقيق ما يترجح في نظرهم من الإتيان بوظيفة الوقت، أو تأخيره إلى أيام أخر.
العبادة المقررة في الوقت الإتيان
وباعتبار هذا المعنى قال أبو حنيفة: المسافر إذا نوى في أيام رمضان واجباً آخر يقع

عبد
ليست بنجسة وبهذا يستدل على أن سؤرها ليس بنجس، وعليه كثير من الاعتماد، ولذا ذهب أبويوسف والشافعي ومالك وأحمد والثوري والأوزاعي وإسحاق وأبو عبيد إلى أنه غير مكروه، وقيل: هو قول مالك وغيره من أهل المدينة، والليث وغيره من أهل مصر والأوزاعي وغيره من أهل الشام والثوري وغيره من أهل العراق، والشافعي وأصحابه وأحمد وإسحاق وأبي عبيد وعكرمة وإبراهيم وعطاء بن يسار والحسن كما قاله البر، واختاره الطحاوي من الحنفية، ورواية عن محمد أيضاً لكن ما ذكره الطحاوي في "معاني الآثار" يدل على أنه مكروه تحريماً، واختار الكرخي من أصحابنا أنه مكروه تنزيهاً وهو الأصح الأقرب إلى موافقة الأخبار والآثار كذا في "الحصول". وكذلك قوله تعالى إلخ بيانه: أنه أبيح الإفطار للمريض والمسافر تيسيراً عليهم بأن يساوي الإفطار والصوم عندهم ويتمكنوا من تحقيق ما يترجح منهما في نظرهم لمصلحة كذا في "الفصول". ما يترجح بعد موازنة ذلك في كفتي ميزان العقل. إلى أيام أخر: إن اختاروا تيسير الإفطار بمشقة السفر والناس في الاختيار متفاوتون، فصار التخيير بين الصوم والإفطار لطلب اليسر اعتباراً للعبد ما هو اليسر عنده من الصوم والإفطار، بخلاف الصلاة، فإن اليسر فيها متعين القصر؛ فلا يجوز فيه التخيير بين القصر والإكمال؛ لأن في الإكمال ما يبقى اليسر أصلاً كذا في "المعدن". واجباً آخر: قيد بقوله: "واجباً أخراً؛ لأنه لو نوى النفل لا يقع في صحيح الرواية عن أبي حنيفة رحله كذا في "المنهاج".
أخرجه مالك في "الموطأ" رقم ٤٢ باب الطهور للوضوء، وأحمد في مسنده" رقم ٢٢٥٨١ ، وأبو دواد في باب سؤر الهرة رقم ٧٥ ، والترمذي في باب ما جاء في سؤر الهرة رقم ۹۲ قال الترمذي: هذا حديث حسن صحيح، وابن ماجه في باب الوضوء بسؤر الهرة رقم ٣٦٧ ، والدارمي في باب الهرة إذا ولغت في الإناء، وصحيح ابن حبان، ٤ / ١١٥ عن كبشة بنت كعب بن مالك الهلال المهن.
Chapter on Legal Analogy. Fourth Research on Analogy. Legal analogy: It is the attachment of the ruling in a non-textual case to a meaning that is the effective cause of that ruling in the textual case. Then, the meaning is known to be an effective cause by the Book, the Sunnah, consensus, ijtihad, and deduction. An example of the effective cause known by the Book: the frequency of circumambulation, for it was made a cause for the removal of hardship in seeking permission in His statement: 'There is no blame upon you nor upon them after them, frequenting you, some of you from others'. Then the Messenger of God removed hardship regarding the impurity of the cat's leftover water by virtue of this cause. ... The scholars differed: the scholars of Iraq said the ruling in the textual case is established by the text itself, not by the cause; the scholars of Samarkand said the ruling is established by the cause, and the text is only for its knowledge. This definition refers to the second view. ... It is known that the innate nature of texts is to be reasoned, but they agreed that reasoning with all descriptions of the text is invalid, because many descriptions have no effect on the ruling... The example of 'kathrat al-tawaf' is that the cat is the analogized case, the slaves (the original case), the cause is frequency of coming and going, and the ruling is removal of hardship of impurity, similar to the removal of hardship of seeking permission. ... Ali said: 'The cat is not impure, for it is among those that frequent you.' Our companions analogized all domestic animals like mice and snakes to the cat by the cause of frequenting. Similarly, the verse 'God intends ease for you and not hardship' shows the permissibility of breaking fast for the sick and traveler to facilitate ease. The correct view in the madhhab is that cat's leftover water is makruh tanzihan.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a definition of qiyas (legal analogy) and an exposition on how the effective cause ('illa) is recognized. It begins by defining qiyas as the application of a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared effective cause. The 'illa is known through four primary sources: the Quran, Sunnah, Ijma, and Ijtihad (including istinbat). The example of frequency of circumambulation (kathrat al-tawaf) from the Quran (Surah an-Nur) illustrates how the 'illa is extracted from the text; this 'illa was used by the Prophet to declare that the cat's saliva is not impure, removing hardship. The commentary then presents a dispute: some Hanafi scholars (Mashayikh al-Iraq) hold that the ruling in the original case is established by the text itself, while others (Mashayikh Samarqand and al-Shafi'i) hold it is established by the 'illa, and the text only informs us of the 'illa. The author indicates that the definition given ('tarattub al-hukm...') aligns with the second view. The passage further emphasizes that not all descriptions of a text can be considered 'illa; there must be evidence (dalil) from one of the four sources. The discussion then moves to the cat example, where Ali's statement is used as a proof that the cat is not impure due to its frequent coming and going. This 'illa is extended to other domestic animals. The ruling on cat's saliva is discussed: many scholars consider it permissible but the relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is makruh tanzihan (slightly disliked) according to al-Karkhi. Finally, another example from the Quran on ease is used to show how the 'illa of seeking ease justifies breaking fast for travelers and the sick, with a distinction from prayer where ease is fixed to shortening.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): The attachment of the ruling in a non-textual case to a meaning that is the effective cause for that ruling in the textual case.
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause or rationale for a ruling, known through textual sources or ijtihad.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Independent reasoning to deduce the 'illa when not explicit in the text.
الاستنباط (al-istinbat): Deduction of the 'illa from the text by extracting the underlying meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how is the effective cause ('illa) known in qiyas?
A) Only from the Quran.
B) From the Book, the Sunnah, Ijma, and Ijtihad.
C) From the consensus of scholars only.
D) From the qiyas itself.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas depends on a proven effective cause ('illa) identified through textual or ijtihad-based evidence, and not all apparent descriptions qualify.

Extending the Illah of Sleep to Unconsciousness and Drunkenness
Extension of the illah of sleep to greater states of unconsciousness and intoxication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qiyas rule to extend the illah of sleep (relaxation of joints) to unconsciousness (ighma) and drunkenness (sukr) and justify the Hanafi position using the principle of greater cause.

Core Idea
Unconsciousness and drunkenness share a stronger illah than sleep, so the ruling (wudu) applies a fortiori.

In this lesson, we examine how the Hanafi school expands the effective cause (illah) of sleep—which breaks wudu—to cases of fainting and intoxication. The underlying principle is that the illah is the relaxation of the joints, and these states involve an even greater loss of control. Thus, the same ruling applies.

Guided Path
1
Recall the original illah of sleep
From earlier usul, the illah for sleep breaking wudu is the relaxation of joints (irtikha' al-mafasil). Identify this as the asl.
2
Compare the new cases to the asl
Unconsciousness (ighma) and drunkenness (sukr) both exhibit a greater degree of joint relaxation and loss of sensory control. The student should note that these surpass sleep in the intensity of the illah.
The Hanafi medical understanding: ighma is caused by cold phlegm overwhelming the brain.
3
Confirm the illah is the same
The common effective cause is the relaxation of joints. Since it is present more strongly in the far, the ruling transfers via qiyas awla (a fortiori).
Qiyas awla is a stronger form of analogy: if a weaker case gets a ruling, a stronger case certainly does.
4
Apply the ruling
Thus, wudu becomes necessary for a person who was in a state of wudu before experiencing ighma or sukr. The ruling is the same as for sleep.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكذلك يتعدى الحكم بهذه العلة إلى الإغماء والسكر. وكذلك قوله عليه: الوضوء وصلي وإن قطر الدم على الحصير قطراً، فإنه دم عرق انفجر جَعَل إنفجار الدم علة فتعَدَّى الحكم بهذه العلة إلى القصد والحجامة. * أخرجه الترمذي في باب ما جاء في المستحاضة، رقم: ۱۲۵ ، قال الترمذي: حديث حسن صحيح، وأبو داود في باب من روى أن الحيضة إذا أدبرت لا تدع الصلاة، رقم: ۲۸۲ ، وابن ماجه في باب ما جاء في المستحاضة التي قد عدت أيام أقرائها قبل أن يستمر بها الدم رقم ٦٢٤ ، والدارمي في باب في دم الحيض يصيب الثوب عن عائشة لها.
And similarly the ruling is extended by this cause to unconsciousness (al-ighma') and drunkenness (al-sukr). And also his saying (peace be upon him): 'Perform wudu and pray, even if blood drips on the mat drop by drop, for it is blood from a burst vein.' He made the bursting of the vein a cause, so the ruling is extended by this cause to cupping (al-qasd) and hijamah (bloodletting). * Narrated by al-Tirmidhi in the chapter on al-mustahadah, no. 125; al-Tirmidhi said: hasan sahih; Abu Dawud in the chapter on who narrated that when menstruation ends she does not abandon prayer, no. 282; Ibn Majah in the chapter on the mustahadah who has counted the days of her menstrual periods before the blood becomes continuous, no. 624; and al-Darimi in the chapter on menstrual blood staining clothes, from A'ishah (may Allah be pleased with her).
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage demonstrates how the established illah from the sleep hadith (relaxation of joints) is applied to new cases by analogy. The author states that the ruling for wudu after sleep extends to both fainting (ighma') and drunkenness (sukr), because both involve a greater loss of bodily control than sleep. The Hanafi understanding is that fainting is due to a cold phlegm filling the brain, overpowering the intellect, while drunkenness also impairs the senses; thus they surpass sleep in relaxation of joints. Next, the author introduces a second illah known from the Sunnah: from the hadith about one who suffers from chronic bleeding (istihadah), the Prophet instructed her to perform wudu for each prayer, explaining that the blood is from a burst vein, not menstruation. The effective cause (illah) is the bursting of the vein (an ongoing flow from a specific origin), so the same ruling—that wudu is required but not ghusl—extends to blood drawn by cupping (qasd) and hijamah (bloodletting). This is an example of deriving a legal ruling from a specific text and applying it to other scenarios through the identified cause.

Key Terms
الإغماء (al-ighma'): Unconsciousness caused by a cold phlegm filling the brain, overwhelming the intellect.
السكر (al-sukr): Drunkenness from intoxication, involving loss of mental and physical control.
العلة (al-illah): The effective cause that justifies transferring a ruling from one case to another in qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Wudu is required because the illah of sleep applies even more strongly
C) Only ghusl is required
D) It depends on the duration of fainting

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses qiyas awla to extend wudu after sleep to unconsciousness and drunkenness because they share the same cause, which is even stronger.

Illah from the Hadith of Istihadah: Extending to Cupping
Deriving the illah from the hadith of istihadah and applying it to cupping via qiyas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the illah from the hadith of istihadah (burst vein) and apply qiyas to derive the ruling for cupping (hijamah) and bloodletting (qasd).

Core Idea
The Prophet's description of 'blood from a burst vein' provides a cause that applies to all similar blood from veins, not just istihadah.

In this lesson, we analyse a prophetic hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructs a woman with chronic bleeding to perform wudu for each prayer and explains that the blood comes from a burst vein. The Hanafi school extracts this explicit cause (illah) and extends it via qiyas to cases like cupping and hijamah, where blood is deliberately drawn from a vein. This shows how a single textual descriptor can become a principle for multiple rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its context
The hadith concerns a woman with istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding). The Prophet orders wudu for each prayer and explains the blood's origin: 'it is blood from a burst vein.'
The hadith is hasan sahih, narrated by multiple compilers.
2
Extract the illah from the text
The Prophet explicitly states the cause: the blood is from a burst vein (عرق انفجر). This is the stated illah. The student must identify that this is a jali (explicit) cause, suitable for qiyas.
3
Confirm the illah applies to the new case (cupping/hijamah)
Cupping and hijamah involve drawing blood from a vein, often from the same source (veins). The student should note that the cause (blood from a vein) is present identically, not just analogously.
The text says 'burst vein', but cupping also draws from a vein; the illah is the source being a vein, not necessarily bursting itself.
4
Apply the ruling from the hadith
The hadith rules that only wudu is required for each prayer, not ghusl. Therefore, for cupping/hijamah, the same applies: wudu is required (if the person was in a state of wudu), but no ghusl.
This overrides the general rule that any blood invalidates wudu? Actually, istihadah blood does not invalidate wudu if it is continuous; but here the focus is on the requirement of wudu for the prayer, not invalidation. The lesson is about the ruling of blood from a vein.

المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): A woman experiencing non-menstrual uterine bleeding (istihadah).

Extracting the 'Illa from Text and Consensus
Examples of effective cause known by text and consensus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the 'illa from textual and consensus evidence, and apply the Hanafi method of qiyas to extend a ruling to new cases.

Core Idea
The 'illa is the effective cause from text or consensus that justifies analogical extension in Hanafi usul.

This lesson examines how the Hanafi school identifies the effective cause ('illa) for qiyas from two sources: explicit textual indication and consensus. Using the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh and the consensus on guardianship over minors, we will see how the 'illa is extracted and applied to new cases. The passage also introduces a key intra-madhhab debate on the 'illa for marriage guardianship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl) and its ruling
For the mustahada example, the original case is the woman with chronic bleeding who is commanded to pray and perform wudu despite blood dripping. The ruling is that her impurity is invalidated, requiring wudu. For the guardianship, the asl is the father's guardianship over his minor son.
The asl is the scenario where the ruling is already established.
2
Extract the 'illa from the text
In the hadith, the Prophet says 'it is only a vein that burst' (إنما ذلك عرق انفجر). The burst vein (infijar al-dam) is the 'illa for the invalidation of purity, because the command to perform wudu implies the prior invalidation. This 'illa is textually indicated.
The 'illa is an explicit description in the text, not inferred from the ruling alone.
3
Extend the ruling to new cases (far')
Since the 'illa is the bursting of a vein, the ruling extends to any case where blood flows from a vein, such as cupping (hijama) and bloodletting (qar'). Similarly, fainting (ighma) and intoxication are comparable to sleep in relaxation of joints, so the ruling from sleep extends to them.
The far' must share the same 'illa as the asl.
4
Analyze the 'illa from consensus (ijma)
The text states that minority (sughr) is the 'illa for the father's guardianship over a minor son. This is known by consensus among the companions and scholars. The ruling is then extended to the minor daughter because the 'illa (inability to manage interests) is present in both.
Consensus establishes the 'illa even if not explicitly stated in a single text.
5
Evaluate the disputed 'illa in marriage guardianship
The Hanafi position holds that minority is the 'illa for guardianship over a woman in marriage, while al-Shafi'i considers virginity (bakara) as the 'illa. The text presents the Hanafi view and the Shafi'i counterargument, with the preference for the Hanafi position based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas.
This step highlights the importance of 'illa in intra-madhhab disputes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في القياس الشرعي

وكذلك يتعدى الحكم بهذه العلة إلى الإغماء والسكر.

وكذلك قوله عليا : [الوَضَنِي؟] وصَلّي وإن قطر الدم على الحصير قطراً، فإنه دم عرق انفجر جَعَل إنفجار الدم علة فتعَدَّى الحكم بهذه العلة إلى القصد والحجامة.

ومثال العلة المعلومة بالإجماع: فيما قلنا: الصغرُ علة لولاية الأب في حق الصغير، فيثبت بالإجماع الحكم في حقٌّ الصَّغيرة لوجود العلة، والبلوغ عن عقل علة لزوال ولاية الأب في ولاية الأب

الإغماء هو امتلاء بطون الدماغ من بلغم بارد غليظ، وهو ساتر للعقل، والجنون: تغيير في القوة المفكر بسبب العقل فالمغمى عليه مغلوب العقل، والمجنون مسلوب العقل، وجه تعدي الحكم إليهما؛ لكونهما فوق نوم المضطجع في استرخاء المفاصل. تَوَضَّي: هذا قطعة من حديث فاطمة بنت أبي حبيش في آخره: "ثم اغتسلي وصلي وتوضيء لكل صلاة وإن قطر الدم على الحصير"، وفي رواية: "إنما ذلك عرق وليست بالحيضة" إلخ أخرجه أحمد وصححه الترمذي كذا في "الحصول". فيما قلنا إلخ أي أصحاب أبي حنيفة وغيرهم أن الصغر علة لولاية الأب في حق الصغير؛ وهذا لأن الصغير عاجز عن القيام لمصالحه، فلذا جعل المولى ولاية عليه ليقوم بأموره كذا في "المعدن". الصغرُ علةٌ إلخ: اعلم أن المختلف فيه ههنا ثلاث مسائل: الأولى: أنه يجوز نكاح البالغة بغير إذن الولي أو لا، فذهب الطرفان وبعض أهل العلم بجوازه، وقال أكثرهم: إنه لا يجوز، وقال ابن المنذر : لا يعرف عن أحد من الصحابة خلاف ذلك، والمسألة الثانية: أنه هل يجوز أن تتولى البالغة بنفسها لنكاحها، وهل ينعقد النكاح بعبارة النساء أو لا، فعند أصحابنا يجوز، وعند الأكثر لا يجوز. المسألة الثالثة: أن علة الولاية على المرأة في النكاح هل هي الصغر كما في الغلام أو البكارة، فأخترنا الأول، واختار الشافعي محليه الثاني كذا في "الحصول".

حق الغلام، فيتعدى الحكم إلى الجارية بهذه العلة.

أي الذكر الصبي

البلوغ مع عقل

وانفجار الدم علة الانتقاض للطهارة في حق المستحاضة فيتعدى الحكم إلى غيرها [لسيلانه؟] لوجود العلة.

للطهارة لأن الشرع أمرها بالتوضي، وذلك لا يستقيم إلا بعد انتقاض الطهارة، فيكون خروج الدم في حقها ناقضا للطهارة كذا في "المعدن".
Chapter on Legal Analogy. Similarly, the ruling extends by this cause to fainting and intoxication. Likewise, his saying (Ali?) '... and pray even if blood drips onto the mat, for it is a burst vein.' He made the bursting of blood a cause, so the ruling extends by this cause to cupping and bloodletting. An example of a cause known by consensus: as we said, minority is a cause for the father's guardianship over the minor son, so by consensus the ruling is established for the minor daughter due to the existence of the cause. Puberty with intellect is a cause for the removal of the father's guardianship... Fainting is the filling of the brain's cavities with cold thick phlegm, which veils the intellect; insanity is a change in the thinking faculty due to the intellect. The one who faints is overcome in intellect, the insane is stripped of intellect. The way of extending the ruling to them is that they are above the sleep of one lying on his side in relaxation of joints. 'Perform wudu' is a portion of the hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh at its end: 'Then perform ghusl and pray and perform wudu for every prayer even if blood drips on the mat.' In another narration: 'It is only a vein and not menstruation' etc. Narrated by Ahmad and authenticated by Tirmidhi, as in 'al-Husul'. 'As we said' etc. meaning the companions of Abu Hanifa and others that minority is a cause for the father's guardianship over the minor; this is because the minor is incapable of managing his interests, so the guardian was given authority over him to handle his affairs, as in 'al-Ma'din'. 'Minority is a cause' etc. Know that the disputed matter here is three issues: First, whether the marriage of a mature woman without the guardian's permission is permissible. The two parties and some scholars allowed it, but most said it is not permissible. Ibn al-Mundhir said no companion is known to have opposed that. The second issue: whether a mature woman can conduct her own marriage, and whether the marriage contract is valid by the words of women. According to our scholars it is permissible, according to most it is not. The third issue: whether the cause of guardianship over a woman in marriage is minority as in a boy, or virginity. We chose the first, and al-Shafi'i chose the second, as in 'al-Husul'. 'For the boy, so the ruling extends to the girl by this cause.' Meaning the male child. 'Puberty with intellect'. 'And the bursting of blood is a cause for the invalidation of purity for the mustahada, so the ruling extends to other than her due to its flowing, due to the existence of the cause.' 'For purity because the Law commanded her to perform wudu, and that is not valid except after invalidation of purity, so the emission of blood in her case invalidates purity.', as in 'al-Ma'din'.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on qiyas provides examples of 'illa (effective cause) known through textual evidence (naqli) and consensus (ijma). The author extends a previously established ruling to fainting and intoxication, then cites a hadith about a mustahada (woman with chronic bleeding) where the Prophet instructed her to pray despite blood dripping, indicating that the 'illa is the bursting of a blood vessel (infijar al-dam). This 'illa is then extended to cupping and bloodletting. Next, the 'illa known by consensus: minority (sughr) is the 'illa for the father's guardianship over his minor son, and by consensus this ruling is established for the minor daughter as well. The commentary clarifies the nature of fainting and insanity as states that veil or strip intellect. It then explains the hadith and the three disputed issues regarding guardianship in marriage, affirming the Hanafi position that minority is the 'illa, not virginity. Finally, the 'illa of blood bursting is extended to all cases of istihada, based on the command to perform wudu, which implies invalidation of purity.

Key Terms
علة ('illa): The effective cause or ratio legis that justifies extending a ruling from an original case to a new case.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a common 'illa.
إنسفجار الدم (infijar al-dam): Bursting of a vein, the 'illa in the mustahada hadith for invalidation of purity.
الصغر (al-sughr): Minority; the state of being a minor, which is the 'illa for guardianship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Minority; known by textual evidence from the Quran
B) Incapacity to manage affairs; known by consensus (ijma)
C) Virginity; known by textual evidence from the hadith
D) Puberty; known by consensus

Key Takeaway
The 'illa is the essential link in qiyas, and its extraction from text or consensus is a foundational skill in Hanafi usul.

8 min
Two Types of Qiyas: Same Kind vs Same Genus
Classification of qiyas into two types based on the ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two types of qiyas (naw' and jins) and apply the definition of qiyas al-naw' to analyze a Hanafi derivation, distinguishing it from a Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
Qiyas al-naw' transfers an identical ruling when the 'illa is the same; qiyas al-jins transfers a similar but not identical ruling.

In the previous lesson, we introduced the concept of qiyas and its pillars. Now, we delve into the classification of qiyas based on the nature of the ruling transferred. The text distinguishes between two types: qiyas al-naw' (same kind) where the branch ruling is identical in kind to the original, and qiyas al-jins (same genus) where the rulings share a common category but differ in specifics. The guardianship example illustrates qiyas al-naw' and also reveals a key dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is on the effective cause ('illa).

Guided Path
1
Understand the Two Types
Identify the overarching classification: qiyas is divided into two types based on the relationship between the original ruling (hukm al-asl) and the transferred ruling (hukm al-far'). One type is 'from its kind' (min naw'ihi) meaning the ruling is identical in essence; the other is 'from its genus' (min jinsihi) meaning the ruling is similar but not identical.
This classification is about the ruling itself, not the strength of the analogy.
2
Define Qiyas al-Naw'
Focus on the first type. The text defines it as the ruling of the branch being 'ayn (identical to) the ruling of the original, with only the locus (mahall) differing. Study the example of minority as the 'illa for marriage guardianship: the same ruling (wilayat al-inkah) applies to both a minor boy and a minor girl.
The 'illa must be present in both cases, and the ruling is exactly the same in content.
3
Examine the Dispute on the 'Illa
The text presents a disagreement: Hanafis hold that minority (sughr) is the universal 'illa for guardianship for both genders, while Shafi'is claim that for females, the 'illa is virginity (bakara). Track how the Hanafis use the hadith of Ibn Abbas to support their view.
This dispute is not about the type of qiyas but about determining the correct 'illa.
4
Relate the Dispute to Qiyas al-Naw'
Note that both schools agree on the minor virgin and adult non-virgin. The disagreement on the adult virgin shows that if the 'illa were virginity, the ruling would differ between male and female, breaking the identity of the ruling required for qiyas al-naw'.
The Hanafi position preserves identity of ruling (naw'); the Shafi'i position would make the ruling genus-level (jins) if accepted.

ثم بعد ذلك نقول: القياس على نوعين: أحدهما: أن يكون الحكم المعدى من نوع الحكم الثابت في الأصل والثاني: أن يكون من جنسه.

من الأصل إلى الفرع

الحكم الثابت في الأصل مثالُ الإتحاد في النوع: ما قلنا: إنّ الصِّغر علة لولاية الإنكاح في حق الغلام، فيثبت ولاية الإنكاح في حق الجارية لوجود العلة فيها، وبه يثبت الحكم في الثيب الصغيرة. وكذلك قلنا: الطواف علةً سقوط نجاسة السؤر في سؤر الهرة، فيتعدى الحكم إلى سُور [سواكن البيوت؟] - فيتعدى الحكم إلخ أي عندنا الصغر علة لولاية الأب في حق الصغير، فيتعدى الحكم في حق الصغيرة بعلة الصغر، فعندنا الصغر مطلقاً، وعنده الصغير في الذكر، والبكارة في الأنثى، فالبكرة الصغيرة يولي عليها اتفاقاً، والثيب البالغة لا يولي عليها إجماعاً ، والبكرة البالغة لا يولي عليها عندنا لا عنده ولنا: حديث ابن عباس لما في قصة جارية بكر مرفوعاً: وزوجها أبوها وهي كارهة فخيرها" أخرجه أحمد ورجاله ثقاة، والمقام حققه حق البسط ابن الهمام محله في "فتح القدير" كذا في "الحصول". [ثم بعد ذلك: أي بعد بيان العلة المعلومة في الكتاب والسنة والإجماع نقول إلخ كذا في "المنهاج". من جنسه الاتحاد في الجنس: أن يشترك الحكمان في وصف ويختلفان في وصف كالإضافة، والوصف مثل ولاية المال، ومثل حرج الاستئذان الاستئذان وحرج النجاسة كذا في "الفصول". مثالُ الإتحاد في إلخ المراد بالاتحاد في النوع أن يكون حكم الفرع عين حكم الأصل لكنه يتغاير المحلان كما أن ولاية الإنكاح اتحدت في المحلين في الجارية والغلام وكذلك نجاسة السور في المحلين في الهرة وسواكن البيوت كذا في "الحصول". وبه يثبت الحكم: أي بالصغر يثبت الحكم في الثيب الصغيرة لا بالبكارة كما زعم الشافعي محله فتقديم قوله : "به" اهتماماً بشأن بيان علية الصغر رداً لقول الشافعي له كذا في "المعدن".
Then after that we say: Qiyas is of two types: one is that the transferred ruling is of the same kind as the ruling established in the original; the second is that it is of its same genus. From the original to the branch. The ruling established in the original. Example of unity in kind: what we said: minority is the cause of the guardianship of marriage over the boy, so the guardianship of marriage is established for the girl due to the existence of the cause in her, and by it the ruling is established for the minor non-virgin. Likewise we said: tawaf is a cause for the removal of impurity from the residual water in the case of the cat's leftover water, so the ruling extends to [domestic animals]. - 'So the ruling extends' etc. meaning according to us minority is the cause for the father's guardianship over the minor boy, so the ruling extends to the minor girl by the cause of minority. Thus with us minority is absolute, while with him (al-Shafi'i) it is minority for the male and virginity for the female. The minor virgin is under guardianship by agreement, the adult non-virgin is not under guardianship by consensus, and the adult virgin is not under guardianship according to us but is according to him. We have the hadith of Ibn Abbas in the story of a virgin girl raised to the Prophet: 'Her father married her while she was unwilling, so he gave her the choice' narrated by Ahmad with trustworthy narrators. The matter has been thoroughly investigated by Ibn al-Humam in his place in 'Fath al-Qadir' as in 'al-Husul'. [Then after that: i.e. after the explanation of the cause known from the Book, Sunnah, and consensus we say etc. as in 'al-Minhaj'. 'Of its genus' is unity in genus: that the two rulings share a description but differ in another, like addition and description such as guardianship of property, and like the difficulty of permission and difficulty of impurity as in 'al-Fusul'. 'Example of unity in' etc. By unity in kind is meant that the ruling of the branch is identical to the ruling of the original but the two loci differ, as the guardianship of marriage was unified in the two loci of the girl and the boy, and likewise impurity of the residual water in the two loci of the cat and domestic animals as in 'al-Husul'. 'And by it the ruling is established': i.e. by minority the ruling is established for the minor non-virgin, not by virginity as al-Shafi'i claimed in his place, so the presentation of his saying 'by it' emphasizes the explanation of minority being the cause, refuting al-Shafi'i's statement as in 'al-Ma'din'.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on qiyas by classifying it into two types. The first is qiyas al-naw' (same kind), where the ruling of the branch (far') is identical in kind to the ruling of the original (asl), differing only in the subject. Example: minority as the 'illa for marriage guardianship applies to both a minor boy and a minor girl, and the ruling (guardianship) is identical. The second is qiyas al-jins (same genus), where the two rulings share a general category but differ in specifics. Example: tawaf (circumambulation) makes the leftover water of a cat pure; by genus (animals whose saliva is impure), the same ruling applies to other domestic animals. The commentary explains that according to Hanafis, minority is the 'illa for guardianship in all minors, while Shafi'is differentiate between male (minority) and female (virginity). The hadith of Ibn Abbas is cited as evidence for the Hanafi position that a virgin woman can choose her spouse.

Key Terms
نوع (naw'): Kind or species: a category where the ruling is exactly the same in essence.
جنس (jins): Genus: a broader category where rulings share a common aspect but may differ in specific details.
علة ('illa): Effective cause: the attribute that is common to the original and branch and upon which the ruling is based.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is an example of qiyas al-naw' from the passage?
A) The ruling on cat's leftover water extended to other domestic animals
B) The ruling on guardianship for a minor boy extended to a minor girl
C) The ruling on cupping based on bloodbursting
D) The ruling on fainting based on sleep

Key Takeaway
Qiyas al-naw' transfers an identical ruling when the 'illa is the same; the dispute on the 'illa for guardianship illustrates how correct identification of the 'illa preserves the integrity of this type of qiyas.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
The Two Types of Qiyas: Union in Type and Union in Genus
Explaining the two types of legal analogy: union in type and union in genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between union in type (naw') and union in genus (jins) in qiyas, and correctly classify a given analogy into one of the two types based on the nature of the transferred ruling.

Core Idea
Qiyas transfers a ruling either exactly (type) or as a shared genus (genus), depending on the cause.

Legal analogy (qiyas) is a fundamental source of Islamic law, but not all analogies are alike. The Hanafi school distinguishes between two types of qiyas based on how closely the branch case's ruling matches the original. Understanding this distinction is key to correctly deriving rulings and resolving juristic disagreements, such as the famous dispute over the father's authority to marry his minor daughter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of qiyas
In the passage, the author states that qiyas is divided into two types: one where the transferred ruling is of the same type (naw') as the original, and another where it is of the same genus (jins). Locate these definitions in the Arabic text and note the key difference.
The terms 'naw'' and 'jins' are technical; 'naw'' indicates an exact match, while 'jins' indicates a shared general category.
2
Analyze the example of union in type
The passage gives the example of minority (al-sighr) as the cause for marriage guardianship (wilayat al-inkah). For a minor boy, the father has authority; it is transferred to a minor girl because the cause (minority) exists in both. This is union in type: the ruling is exactly the same (authority over marriage).
The dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i is also introduced here: Shafi'i argues that virginity (bikarah) is an additional condition for the girl, but Hanafis hold minority alone is sufficient.
3
Analyze the example of union in genus
The passage provides the example of frequent tawaf (circling) as the cause for removing the hardship (haraj) of seeking permission to enter at all times for servants. The same frequent tawaf is used to remove the hardship of impurity from the saliva of animals that live in homes. The two rulings (removal of hardship in permission vs. impurity) are not identical but share the genus 'hardship' (haraj).
Union in genus applies when the transferred ruling falls under a common description with the original but differs in specific details.
4
Examine the cross-madhhab dispute
In the example of union in type, the passage contrasts the Hanafi and Shafi'i views. Identify the cause each school uses for the father's authority over a daughter. The Hanafi response relies on a hadith from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet gave a virgin girl a choice after her father married her, indicating that minority is the cause.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the case of a non-virgin minor: Hanafis give the father authority (since minority applies), while Shafi'is do not.

Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi defines the two types of qiyas: union in type (نوع) and union in genus (جنس). Union in type means the ruling of the branch case is exactly the same ruling as the original case, just applied to a different subject. For example, minority (صغر) is the cause (علة) for the father's authority to marry off a minor son; it also applies to a minor daughter. The passage includes a dispute with Imam Shafi'i, who holds that virginity (بكارة) is the cause for the daughter, not minority. The Hanafi position relies on a hadith from Ibn Abbas where the Prophet gave a virgin girl the choice after her father married her. Union in genus means the rulings share a common description but differ in another. For example, the frequent coming and going of servants is the cause for the exemption from seeking permission at all times; that 'hardship' (حرج) is of the same genus as the hardship from impurity in the case of animals living in homes. Similarly, minority is a cause for guardianship over property, and by the same genus, it establishes guardianship over the person. The passage clarifies that in union in genus, the two rulings share a general category (e.g., 'guardianship' or 'hardship') but differ in the specific subject (e.g., property vs. person, or permission vs. impurity). The commentary expands on these examples and cites earlier works like al-Ma'din and al-Husul.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Transferring a ruling from an original case to a branch case due to a shared effective cause.
النوع (al-naw'): The specific kind of ruling; union in type means the ruling is exactly the same.
الجنس (al-jins): The general category of rulings; union in genus means the rulings share a general description but differ in specific details.
العلة (al-illa): The effective cause that connects the original and branch cases in qiyas.
ولاية الإنكاح (wilayat al-inkah): The father's authority to contract marriage on behalf of his minor children.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is an example of union in genus (اتحاد في الجنس) in qiyas?
A) Using minority (صغر) as the cause to transfer the father's marriage authority from son to daughter.
B) Using frequent tawaf (كثرة الطواف) as the cause to remove the hardship of seeking permission for slaves and the hardship of impurity from leftover water.
C) Using puberty with intellect (البلوغ مع العقل) as the cause to remove marriage authority from both son and daughter.
D) Using minority (صغر) as the cause for both marriage authority and guardianship over property.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas transfers a ruling either exactly (type) or as a shared genus (genus), and recognizing this distinction is essential for correct analogical reasoning in Hanafi usul.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Identity in Genus (Ittihad fi al-Jins): The Second Type of Qiyas
Defines and illustrates qiyas with identity in genus

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define identity in genus (ittihad fi al-jins) and apply the condition of tajnis al-illah to validate analogies in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Two rulings share a genus but differ in species — that is sufficient for valid qiyas.

This lesson from Usul al-Shashi introduces the second type of qiyas: identity in genus. Unlike identity in species, where the cause is exactly identical, here the cause belongs to the same genus but different species. The passage illustrates this with examples from guardianship and hardship, and introduces the necessary condition of tajnis al-illah (making the cause a genus). Understanding this type is crucial for applying analogical reasoning in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the concept
Understand that qiyas can be based on identity in genus, not just species or individual. The passage gives examples: hardship from circumambulation and impurity; guardianship over property and person; and analogy from minor to marriage guardianship.
2
Analyze the examples
Work through each example: (1) circumambulation removes hardship of seeking permission; similarly, it removes hardship of impurity of residual water. (2) Minority causes father's authority over property; similarly, over the person. Note that the hardships and authorities are of the same genus but different species.
3
Define ittihad fi al-jins formally
The formal definition: two rulings share a common attributed (mudaf) but differ in the attributing (mudaf ilayh). For instance, 'guardianship' is common, but 'of property' and 'of person' differ. Similarly, 'hardship' is common but 'of permission' and 'of impurity' differ.
4
Apply tajnis al-illah
For this type of qiyas, the cause must be generalized to a genus level (tajnis). For example, the cause for father's authority is 'incapacity to manage affairs' — a general meaning covering both property and personal matters. This generalization allows the analogy.
5
Note the dispute on non-existents
The passage addresses the dispute about using non-existent attributes (al-‘adami) as causes. The preferred Hanafi position is that only existential attributes can serve as causes, as per Abu Zayd al-Dabusi, Fakhr al-Islam, and Ibn al-Humam.

Source Text

لوجود العلة
أي مال الجارية
نفس الجارية
العلة وهي الطواف وسقوط نجاسة سؤر سواكن البيوت؛ لأنه عينه كذا في "المعدن". هذه العلة وهي البلوغ عن عقل، وزوال هذه الولاية من نوع زوال تلك الولاية؛ لأن زوال هذه الولاية عين تلك الولاية كذا في "المعدن". الإتحاد في الجنس: المراد بالاتحاد في الجنس: أن يتحد الحكمان في وصف أي: "المضاف"، ويفترقان في وصف أي: "المضاف إليه" كالاتحاد في الإضافة، والوصف مثل ولاية النفس وولاية الاستئذان المال، ومثل حرج وحرج النجاسة، فإن فيهما المضاف وهي "الولاية" مشترك ومتحد، والمضاف إليه مختلف ومغاير؛ لأن النفس والمال مغايران وكذا الحرج المضاف إلى الاستئذان والنجاسة متحد، والمضاف إليه مختلف؛ لأن النجاسة والاستئذان مغايران فمطلق الولاية جنس وولاية الإنكاح نوع، وولاية المال نوع آخر، وولاية الصغر الفلاني فرد، وكذا الحرج جنس، وحرج الاستئذان نوع وحرج النجاسة نوع آخر، وحرج الاستئذان الفلاني فرد، وكذا حرج نجاسة كذا فرد فافهم. حَرَج الاستئذان إلخ بيانه أن الله تعالى أمرنا بأن يستأذن العبيد الذين لم يحكموا في ثلاث أوقات من قبل صلاة الفجر، وحين وضع الثياب من الظهيرة، ومن بعد صلاة العشاء، وأسقط الإذن بعد هذه الأوقات، وبين علته كثرة الطواف بقوله : طوافون عليكم بعضكم على بعض" يعني أن بكم وبهم حاجة إلى المخالطة والمداخلة يطوفون عليكم أي للخدمة وتطوفون عليهم بالاستخدام فلو جرى الأمر بالاستئذان في كل وقت لأدى إلى الحرج كذا في الشرح.
وإن بلوغ الجارية عن عقل علة زوال ولاية الأب في المال، فيزول ولايته في حق النفس بهذه العلة.ثم لابد في هذا النوع من القياس من تجنيس العلة بأن نقول: إنما يثبت ولاية الأب في مال الصَّغيرة؛ لأنها عاجزة عن التصرف بنفسها فأثبت الشرعُ ولاية الأب كيلا يتعطل والصغيرة مصالحها المتعلقة بذلك، وقد عجزت عن التصرف في نفسها، فوجَبَ القول بولاية أي تدابير أموالها مال الصغيرة الأب عليها، وعلى هذا نظائره. الذي ذكرنا لا من نوعه إلخ: لأن هذا حرج النحاسة، وذلك حرج الاستئذان فاختلفا باعتبار النوع، وإن اتحدا باعتبار الجنس؛ لأن كلا منهما من جنس واحد وهو نفس الحرج كذا في الشرح. بحكم هذه العلة: وهي الصغر وهذه الولاية من جنس تلك الولاية لا من نوعها؛ لأن الولاية في النفس غير الولاية في المال كذا في "المعدن". زوال ولاية إلخ أو يقال: زوال الصغر علة لزوال الولاية، أو يقال: بلوغها علة لخيارها في نفسها، أو يقال: زوال الصغر علة الخيارها وولايتها على نفسها، وبهذا عرفت أن المقصود الواحد يكون له عبارات ومفاهيم مختلفة تعبيرية وجودية وعدمية، يجوز التعبير عنه بأيها كان ولا يختلف المطلوب، فالنزاع في صلوح العدمي للوجودي مما لا يلائم عند أهل التحقيق، وقد نقل عن أبي زيد الدبوسي وفخر الإسلام من الحنفية: أنه لا يجوز، وتبعه الإمام كمال الدين بن الهمام في "التحرير" ، وكثير من المتأخرين له. وهو في حق النفس إلخ: أي في حق نفس الغلام والجارية بهذه العلة أي: البلوغ عن عقل، وزوال هذه الولاية من جنس زوال تلك الولاية لا من نوعها؛ لأن زوال هذه الولاية غير زوال تلك الولاية. هذا النوع: أي النوع الثاني اتحاد الجنس. [الشافي: ص ٢٦٩] من تجنيس العلة: أي من جعل العلة جنساً أي معنى عاما يعم المنصوص وغيره ليؤثر في حكم المنصوص، وفي جنسه من حكم المنصوص كما إذا عللنا ولاية الأب في مال الصغيرة بمعنى العجز عن التصرف، وهذا المعنى يعم المال والنفس، ولهذا أثبتنا الولاية على النفس أيضاً كما أثبتنا على المال كذا في "وصول الأصول".
فوجَبَ القول إلخ كيلا يتعطل مصالحاً المتعلقة بالنفس، فالعجز عن التصرف معنى عام يعم المال والنفس، فلهذا أثبتنا ولاية الأب على النفس أيضاً كما أثبتنا على المال لوفور شفقته وكمال رأيه في نفسه وماله كذا قيل. نظائره: وكذلك من نظائره التيمم عند خوف فوت صلاة العيد. [الشافي: ص ٢٦٩]
Fourth Section on Qiyas Chapter on Legal Qiyas. (Examples:) The creatures of houses due to existence of cause. Like the mouse and the snake. And the boy reaching puberty with intellect is a cause for removal of guardianship of marriage, so guardianship over the girl is removed by this ruling. And an example of identity in genus: it is said: frequent circumambulation is a cause for removing the hardship of seeking permission regarding those whom your right hands possess, so the hardship of impurity of residual water is removed by this cause, for this hardship is from the genus of that hardship, not its species. (Margin: 'Seeking permission hardship'). Similarly, minority is a cause for the father's authority to act in property, so authority to act regarding the person is established by this ruling. (Margin: 'due to existence of cause'; 'i.e., property of the girl'; 'person of the girl'). The cause which is circumambulation and removal of impurity of residual water of house-dwellers; because it is the same (as in al-Ma'din). This cause which is reaching puberty with intellect, and removal of this authority is from the type of removal of that authority; because the removal of this authority is the same as that authority (as in al-Ma'din). Identity in genus: what is meant by identity in genus is that two rulings agree in a description, i.e., the 'mudaf' (thing attributed), and differ in a description, i.e., the 'mudaf ilayh' (that to which it is attributed), like identity in attribution. The description is like guardianship of the person and guardianship of property, and like hardship and hardship of impurity. In them, the mudaf which is 'guardianship' is common and identical, while the mudaf ilayh is different and opposite; because the person and wealth are opposite, and similarly the hardship attributed to seeking permission and impurity is common, while the mudaf ilayh is different; because impurity and seeking permission are opposite. So absolute guardianship is a genus, guardianship of marriage is a species, and guardianship of property is another species, and the particular guardianship of a certain minor is an individual. Similarly, hardship is a genus, hardship of seeking permission is a species, hardship of impurity is another species, and the particular hardship of a certain seeking permission is an individual, and similarly for impurity of such-and-such is an individual; understand. The explanation of 'hardship of seeking permission etc.' is that Allah Almighty commanded us that slaves who have not attained maturity should seek permission in three times: before the dawn prayer, at noon when putting off garments, and after the night prayer; and He removed the requirement of permission after these times, and explained its cause to be frequent circumambulation by His saying: 'They are those who circulate among you, some of you from others' meaning that you and they have need for mixing and entering, they circulate among you for service and you circulate among them for employment; so if the command of seeking permission were to apply at all times, it would lead to hardship (as in al-Sharh). And the girl reaching puberty with intellect is a cause for removal of the father's authority over property, so his authority over the person is removed by this cause. Then in this type of qiyas it is necessary to make the cause a genus (tajnis al-illa) by saying: The father's authority over the property of a minor girl is established because she is incapable of managing her own affairs, so the law established the father's authority so that her interests related to that are not disrupted; and she is incapable of managing her own person, so it is necessary to say that the father has authority over her person as well. (Margin: 'and the minor'). This is its like. What we mentioned: 'not from its species etc.' because this hardship of impurity and that hardship of seeking permission differ in type, though they are identical in genus; because each of them is from one genus which is the same hardship (as in al-Sharh). 'By this cause': which is minority, and this authority is from the genus of that authority, not its species; because authority over the person is different from authority over property (as in al-Ma'din). 'Removal of authority etc.' or it is said: Removal of minority is a cause for removal of authority; or it is said: Her reaching puberty is a cause for her option over her own person; or it is said: Removal of minority is a cause for her option and her authority over herself. By this you know that one intended meaning can have different expressions and concepts, existential and non-existential, and it is permissible to express it by any of them without the desired meaning differing. So the dispute regarding the suitability of the non-existent for the existential is not suitable according to the people of verification. It has been narrated from Abu Zayd al-Dabusi and Fakhr al-Islam from the Hanafis that it is not permissible, and Imam Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam in al-Tahrir and many later scholars followed him. 'And it is regarding the person etc.': i.e., regarding the person of the boy and girl by this cause which is reaching puberty with intellect, and removal of this authority is from the genus of removal of that authority, not its species; because removal of this authority is not the same as removal of that authority. 'This type': i.e., the second type which is identity in genus. (From al-Shafi pg 269). 'Making the cause a genus': i.e., making the cause a genus, meaning a general meaning that encompasses the explicitly stated and other to effect the ruling of the explicitly stated and in its genus of the ruling of the explicitly stated, as when we explain the father's authority over the minor's property by the meaning of incapacity to manage, and this meaning encompasses property and person; thus we establish authority over the person as we established over property (as in Wusul al-Usul). 'So it was necessary to say etc.': so that her interests related to the person are not disrupted; so incapacity to manage is a general meaning that encompasses property and person; therefore we establish the father's authority over the person as we established over property due to the abundance of his compassion and completeness of his opinion regarding her person and property (as was said). 'Its likes': and among its likes is tayammum when fearing missing the Eid prayer. (From al-Shafi pg 269).
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi discusses the second type of qiyas (analogical reasoning), known as identity in genus (ittihad fi al-jins). The author begins by giving two initial examples to illustrate the concept: first, the creatures of houses (like mice and snakes) share the same cause (presence of filth) that makes their residual water impure; second, a boy reaching puberty with intellect removes the father's guardianship of marriage for a girl. Then, the core example of identity in genus is presented: frequent circumambulation (tawaf) is the cause for lifting the hardship of seeking permission for slaves in certain times; analogously, this same cause lifts the hardship of impurity from the residual water of house-dwellers. The key point is that the hardship in both cases is from the same genus, not from the same species—one hardship is the burden of seeking permission, the other is the burden of impurity. Similarly, minority is the cause for the father's authority over property; by analogy, it also establishes authority over the person (like marriage). Again, the two authorities are from the same genus (guardianship) but different species. The text then defines identity in genus more formally: two rulings share a common attribute (the 'mudaf') but differ in the attribute to which it is attached (the 'mudaf ilayh'). For example, 'guardianship' is the common mudaf, but attached to property or person, it becomes different species. The same applies to 'hardship'. After explaining the examples, the author introduces a necessary condition for this type of qiyas: 'tajnis al-illa' (making the cause a genus). This means the cause must be a general meaning that encompasses both the original and the analogical case. He illustrates with the father's authority: the cause is the minor's incapacity to manage affairs, which applies to both property and person, thus allowing the analogy. The text also touches on a dispute about using non-existent (al-‘adami) as a cause. Abu Zayd al-Dabusi and Fakhr al-Islam held it impermissible, and later scholars like Ibn al-Humam followed them. The author implies this is the correct view. The passage concludes by stating that many analogies fall under this type, such as tayammum when one fears missing the Eid prayer. Overall, the lesson clarifies that qiyas can be valid even if the cause is not identical in every detail, as long as it belongs to the same genus.

Key Terms
الاتحاد في الجنس (al-ittihad fi al-jins): A type of qiyas where two rulings share a cause that is identical in genus (jins) but differ in species (naw‘)
تجنس العلة (tajnis al-‘illah): The process of making the cause a genus (jins) by abstracting a general meaning that encompasses both the original and analogical cases
العدمي (al-‘adami): A non-existent attribute (like the removal of something) considered as a potential legal cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi classification of qiyas, what is meant by 'identity in genus' (al-ittihad fi al-jins)?
A) The cause in the original case and analogical case are exactly the same in every respect.
B) The two rulings share a common attribute (mudaf) but differ in the attribute to which it is attached (mudaf ilayh).
C) The cause in the analogical case is stronger than the original case.
D) The rulings are identical without any difference.

Key Takeaway
Qiyas is valid when original and analogical cases share a cause of the same genus, provided the cause is generalized to encompass both.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
First Type of Qiyas: Tajnis al-Illah and Its Ruling
Explains the first type of qiyas with tajnis al-illah and its ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the first type of qiyas (tajnis al-illah), apply it to a case, and explain why differentiation does not invalidate the analogy.

Core Idea
In qiyas, the cause must be a genus covering both original and branch; any other difference does not invalidate.

The Hanafi school distinguishes types of qiyas based on how the cause (illa) is formulated. In the first type, the cause is expressed as a genus (jins) that encompasses both the original and the new case. This lesson explores that type through the example of a father's guardianship over a minor's property and person, and establishes the key ruling: differences between the cases in non-cause attributes do not break the analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case and its ruling
The original case (asl) is the father's guardianship over his minor daughter's property. The ruling is that this guardianship is established.
This is the base example from the text.
2
Extract the cause (illa) as a genus
The cause given is the minor's incapacity to manage her affairs ('ajz 'an al-tasarruf). This is a general meaning (genus) that applies to both property and person.
This is tajnis al-illa: making the cause a genus.
3
Apply the cause to the new case
Since the cause (incapacity) is also present in the minor's person, the same ruling of guardianship is extended to the person.
The branch (far') is the guardianship over the person.
4
Note any differences between asl and far'
There are differences: property vs. person are different types. But these are non-causal differences (farq).
The text states this is a difference in type (naw'), not in genus.
5
State the ruling of the analogy
The analogy is valid and not invalidated by the differences, because the cause is shared. This is the ruling of the first type: it is not invalidated by farq.
The text: 'وحكم القياس الأول: أن لا يبطل بالفرق'

البحث الرابع في القياس

فصل في القياس الشرعي
وحكم القياس الأول: أن لا يبطل بالفرق؛ لأن الأصل مع الفرع لما اتحد في العلة
وَجَبَ اتحادُهما في الحكم، وإن افترقا في غير هذه العلة.
الأصل والفرع
بالفرق: أي مطلق الفرق بين المقيس والمقيس عليه؛ إذ لا يشترط في القياس الاتحاد في جميع الأوصاف بل في البعض، فمطلق الفرق مؤيد للقياس لا مثل. وإن افترقا إلخ وصورة الفرق في هذا النوع: أن يقول السائل مثلاً: لا يلزم من الولاية في الغلام الولاية في الجارية الثيب؛ لأن الثيب صارت لها قدرة التصرفات بنفسها لزوال حيائها. فنقول في جوابه هذا لا يضرنا لثبوت الاتحاد بين الغلام والصغيرة في العجز الثابت بالصغر، فيثبت الاتحاد في الحكم وهو ثبوت الولاية للأب مع وجود الافتراق بوصف آخر، فلا يبطل القياس بالفرق فافهم كذا في "معدن الأصول".
The fourth research on analogy. 217. Chapter on legal analogy. And that the reaching of puberty of a girl with reason is a cause for removal of the father's guardianship over property, so his guardianship over her person is removed by this cause. Then it is necessary in this type of analogy to make the cause a genus by saying: Indeed, the father's guardianship over the property of a minor girl is established because she is incapable of disposing of herself, so the law established the father's guardianship so that her interests related to that are not neglected, and she is incapable of disposing of her person, so it becomes necessary to say with guardianship of the father over her, and similarly for its parallels. That which we mentioned. (Commentary: not of its type etc.: because this is hardship of impurity, and that is hardship of seeking permission, so they differ by type, though they are united by genus; because each of them is from one genus, which is hardship itself, as in the commentary. By this cause: i.e., minority, and this guardianship is of the genus of that guardianship, not of its type; because guardianship over the person is not guardianship over property, as in al-Ma'din. Removal of guardianship etc. Or it is said: removal of minority is a cause for removal of guardianship, or it is said: her reaching puberty is a cause for her choice over herself, or it is said: removal of minority is a cause for her choice and her guardianship over herself, and by this it is known that the single intended meaning can have different expressions and concepts, existential and non-existential, and it is permissible to express it by any of them without the object differing, so the dispute about the suitability of the non-existential for the existential is not appropriate according to the people of verification. And it is narrated from Abu Zayd al-Dabusi and Fakhr al-Islam among the Hanafis that it is not permissible, and Imam Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam followed him in al-Tahrir, and many later scholars. And it is regarding the person etc.: i.e., regarding the person of the boy and girl by this cause i.e., reaching puberty with reason, and the removal of this guardianship is of the genus of removal of that guardianship, not of its type; because removal of this guardianship is not removal of that guardianship. This type: i.e., the second type of unity of genus. [al-Shafi: p.269] Making the cause a genus: i.e., making the cause a genus, meaning a general meaning that includes the textually indicated and others, so that it affects the ruling of the textually indicated, and in its genus from the ruling of the textually indicated, as when we justify the father's guardianship over the property of a minor with the meaning of incapacity to dispose, and this meaning includes property and person, and therefore we established guardianship over the person as well as we established over property, as in Wusul al-Usul. So it becomes necessary to say etc. so that her interests related to the person are not neglected, so incapacity to dispose is a general meaning that includes property and person, so we established the father's guardianship over the person as well as we established over property due to his abundant compassion and complete opinion regarding her person and property, as it is said. Its parallels: among its parallels is tayammum when fearing missing the Eid prayer. [al-Shafi: p.269] [PAGE_219] The fourth research on analogy. 218. Chapter on legal analogy. And the ruling of the first analogy: that it is not invalidated by differentiation; because when the original and the branch are united in the cause, their unity in the ruling is obligatory, even if they differ in other than this cause. The original and branch. By differentiation: i.e., absolute differentiation between the analogized and the analogized upon; since unity in all attributes is not required in analogy, but only in some, so absolute differentiation supports the analogy, not opposing. And even if they differ etc. And the form of differentiation in this type: that the questioner says, for example: guardianship over the boy does not necessitate guardianship over the previously married girl; because the previously married girl has gained ability to dispose of herself due to the removal of her shyness. So we say in response: this does not harm us due to the proven unity between the boy and the minor girl in the incapacity established by minority, so unity in the ruling is established, which is the establishment of the father's guardianship, despite the existence of differentiation by another attribute, so the analogy is not invalidated by differentiation, so understand, as in Ma'dan al-Usul.

Commentary
This passage discusses the first type of qiyas (analogy) where the cause (illa) is made a genus (tajnis al-illa). The author explains via the example of a father's guardianship (wilaya) over his minor daughter's property and person. The cause is her incapacity to manage her affairs due to minority. This incapacity is a general meaning (genus) that applies both to property and person, allowing the analogy from property to person. The commentary emphasizes that the unity of the cause in genus is sufficient; differences in type (like property vs. person) do not invalidate the analogy. The ruling of this first type: the analogy is not invalidated by any difference between original and branch as long as they share the cause. The commentary further illustrates with a hypothetical objection: guardianship over a minor boy does not necessarily apply to a previously married girl (thayyib) because she is no longer shy. The response is that the cause (incapacity due to minority) is present in both, so the analogy holds. This passage is from the Hanafi usul tradition, highlighting the importance of the genus (jins) of the cause.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: deriving a ruling for a new case (far') from an original case (asl) based on a shared effective cause (illa).
تجنيس العلة (tajnis al-illa): Making the cause a genus: expressing the cause in general terms so that it encompasses both the original and the branch.
الفرق (al-farq): Differentiation: any difference between original and branch besides the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of the first type of qiyas regarding differentiation (farq) between the original and branch?
A) It invalidates the qiyas if the difference is in a non-causal attribute.
B) The qiyas is invalidated by any difference, regardless of the cause.
C) The qiyas is not invalidated by differentiation as long as they share the cause.
D) The qiyas is only valid if there is no difference at all.

Key Takeaway
The first type of qiyas requires the cause to be a genus (tajnis al-illah), and it is not invalidated by any non-causal difference between original and branch.

Second Type of Qiyas: Invalidation by Muman'at al-Tajnis and al-Farq al-Khas
Explains invalidation of second qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two factors that invalidate the second type of qiyas and distinguish them from a general difference.

Core Idea
The second type of qiyas is invalid if the cause fails to be general or if its effect is stronger in the original.

In this lesson, we explore the second type of qiyas according to Hanafi usul. The passage explains that this type of analogy is vulnerable to two specific objections that can invalidate it: muman'at al-tajnis, where the objector claims the cause does not encompass both cases, and al-farq al-khas, where the effect of the cause is stronger in the original than in the branch. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying qiyas in deriving rulings.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the three types of qiyas
The passage categorizes qiyas into three types; the second type is defined by a cause that is not explicit in the text but is derived and apparent.
2
Identify the two invalidating factors
The text states that the second type is invalidated by two things: muman'at al-tajnis and al-farq al-khas.
3
Analyze the example of minority
The passage uses the example of minority and guardianship to illustrate al-farq al-khas: the effect of minority on property guardianship is stronger than on person guardianship.
4
Understand the response to the objector
The text gives a hypothetical objection and shows that the analogy is not invalidated because the cause (incapacity) is common, showing that the difference is not a valid farq khas.
5
Connect to the third type
The passage transitions to the third type where the cause is derived by ijtihad and must be a suitable description (wasf munasib).

الوصف المناسب
