By differentiation: i.e., absolute differentiation between the analogized and the analogized upon; since unity in all attributes is not required in analogy, but only in some, so absolute differentiation supports the analogy, not opposing. And even if they differ etc. And the form of differentiation in this type: that the questioner says, for example: guardianship over the boy does not necessitate guardianship over the previously married girl; because the previously married girl has gained ability to dispose of herself due to the removal of her shyness. So we say in response: this does not harm us due to the proven unity between the boy and the minor girl in the incapacity established by minority, so unity in the ruling is established, which is the establishment of the father's guardianship, despite the existence of differentiation by another attribute, so the analogy is not invalidated by differentiation, so understand, as in Ma'dan al-Usul. By prevention of making a genus: by the questioner preventing the generality of the cause and its inclusion of the original and branch, so it does not affect the ruling of the original as in Ma'dan al-Usul. And the specific difference: coordinated with 'by prevention of making a genus', meaning the invalidation of the second analogy by two things: by prevention of making a genus and the specific difference, as it is said. Above its effect etc. because the need for disposal in property occurs frequently, every day a hundred times, for civilization in food, drink, clothing, housing, etc., and it is immediate, not tolerating delay, and she is incapable of disposing of them, so due to this necessity, guardianship over her property for her father becomes obligatory, and like this is not found regarding the person due to the absence of desire; because this previously married girl is a minor not yet adult, so there is no necessity for her father's guardianship over her person, but rather after her adulthood, after adulthood she consults about it. So this difference refers to the fact that the cause is not general for the branch based on the probability that the cause is minority not absolutely itself, but rather accompanied by necessity, i.e., the composite and the subject as such. A suitable description: and its meaning is that the relation entails a benefit that brings benefit and repels harm from the servants. [al-Shafi: p.271] With consideration to it: i.e., apparently, and he only said 'with consideration to it apparently' because the verification of the cause in analogy is not definitive, but we say: this description is a cause apparently, because our discussion is about cases where the cause is not textually indicated.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage covers the second type of qiyas, which is invalidated by two factors: (1) muman'at al-tajnis (prevention of making the cause a genus) – when someone objects that the cause does not apply to both original and branch in a general sense, and (2) al-farq al-khas (specific difference) – when the effect of the cause in the original is stronger than in the branch, as shown by the example of minority: its effect on property guardianship is greater than on person guardianship because property needs are more frequent and urgent. The commentary explains that the objection in the second type challenges the generality of the cause, unlike the first type where only absolute difference is raised. The passage also introduces the third type: qiyas with a cause derived by ijtihad, where a suitable description (wasf munasib) that brings benefit or repels harm is identified as the cause, but only as an apparent cause since it is not textually explicit.

Key Terms
ممانعة التجنيس (muman'at al-tajnis): Prevention of making the cause a genus: an objection that the cause as expressed does not truly encompass both original and branch.
الفرق الخاص (al-farq al-khas): Specific difference: a difference that shows the cause's effect is stronger in the original than in the branch, invalidating the analogy.
الوصف المناسب (al-wasf al-munasib): Suitable description: a description that entails a benefit (maslaha) bringing benefit or repelling harm, used as a cause in derived qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the two factors that invalidate the second type of qiyas?
A) Muman'at al-tajnis and al-farq al-mutlaq
B) Muman'at al-tajnis and al-farq al-khas
C) Al-farq al-khas and lack of a suitable description
D) Lack of ijtihad and absence of the original

Key Takeaway
The second type of qiyas is invalidated only by muman'at al-tajnis (cause not general) or al-farq al-khas (cause's effect stronger in original).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Qiyas with a Derived Cause: Definition and Suitable Description
Defines the third type of qiyas and the concept of suitable description

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the third type of qiyas (qiyas bi-illa mustanbata) and explain the role of al-wasf al-munasib as the basis for deriving the cause.

Core Idea
In qiyas bi-illa mustanbata, the cause is derived by ijtihad from a suitable description that entails benefit, and this cause is only apparent (zahir), not definitive.

We have already covered two types of qiyas: qiyas with a textually indicated cause and qiyas with a cause inferred from text. Now we encounter the third and most flexible type: qiyas where the cause is derived purely by ijtihad based on a suitable description (wasf munasib). This lesson will define this type, clarify the nature of the suitable description, and underscore why the cause derived here is only apparent (zahir) rather than decisive.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the Third Type
Note that this qiyas does not rely on an explicit textual cause. The cause is identified through ijtihad by finding a description that is suitable (munasib) for the ruling.
Compare with the first two types where the cause is either textually stated or inferred from text.
2
Define 'Suitable Description' (Wasf Munasib)
A suitable description is one that entails a benefit (maslaha) by either bringing benefit or repelling harm. The text defines it as a description that, when considered, necessitates and demands the ruling.
This is the core criterion for deriving the cause in this type of qiyas.
3
Understand the Epistemological Status
The passage stresses that the verification of the cause is not definitive (qat'i) but only apparent (zahir). This is because the cause is derived by ijtihad, leaving room for differing opinions.
This distinguishes derived causes from textually indicated ones which are conclusive.
4
Connect to Earlier Discussions on Differentiation
The text revisits the example of guardianship over a minor vs. a previously married girl to illustrate how a specific difference (farq khas) can challenge the generality of the cause.
This reinforces that the derived cause must be general enough to cover the branch; otherwise the analogy may fail.

Commentary
This passage explains the third type of qiyas, where the cause is not textually indicated but is derived through ijtihad. القياس بعلة مستنبطة (al-qiyas bi-illa mustanbata): Analogical reasoning where the cause is derived by ijtihad based on a suitable description, not directly from text.
الوصف المناسب (al-wasf al-munasib): A description that entails a benefit (maslaha) by bringing benefit or repelling harm, and is used to derive the cause in qiyas bi-illa mustanbata.

D) The literal meaning of the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The third type of qiyas relies on a suitable description (wasf munasib) to derive a cause, but the cause is only apparent (zahir), not definitive, due to its basis in ijtihad.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
8 min
Valid and Invalid Qiyas: Mere Difference vs. Specific Difference
Defines valid and invalid forms of qiyas with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between valid and invalid qiyas by identifying whether a difference between original and branch is mere or specific, and apply the Hanafi rule that qiyas is not invalidated by mere difference.

Core Idea
Qiyas is invalidated only by a difference that negates the illah, not by any difference at all.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi introduces two fundamental types of qiyas: one that is valid and one that is invalid. Understanding the difference between a harmless variant attribute and a specific difference that destroys the analogy is crucial for correct istinbat. The text clarifies that qiyas does not require absolute identity between original and branch.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of qiyas
Read the passage carefully to note that the first type is not invalidated by any mere difference, while the second type is invalidated by two specific reasons: opposition to generality (man' al-tajnis) and the specific difference (al-farq al-khas).
2
Distinguish between 'mere difference' and 'specific difference'
A mere difference is any difference in attributes other than the illah; it does not invalidate qiyas. A specific difference shows that the illah is not operative in the branch, thus invalidating the analogy.
3
Analyze the example of guardianship
The example illustrates: the questioner claims the previously-married minor girl differs because she can act for herself (loss of shyness). The Hanafi response shows that both share the illah of incapacity due to minority for property, but for self (marriage) the necessity is absent, so the difference is specific and invalidates the qiyas.
4
Apply the concepts to a new hypothetical
Test your understanding by considering a new qiyas scenario: determine whether a difference between original and branch is mere or specific, and state whether the qiyas is valid or invalid per the Hanafi rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وحكم القياس الأول: أن لا يبطل بالفرق؛ لأن الأصل مع الفرع لما اتحد في العلة وَجَبَ اتحادُهما في الحكم، وإن افترقا في غير هذه العلة.
وحكم القياس الثاني : فساده بممانَعَة التجنيس، والفرق الخاص وهو بيان أن تأثير الصغر في ولاية التصرف في المال فوق تأثيره في ولاية التصرف في النفس.
بالفرق: أي مطلق الفرق بين المقيس والمقيس عليه؛ إذ لا يشترط في القياس الاتحاد في جميع الأوصاف بل في البعض، فمطلق الفرق مؤيد للقياس لا مثل. وصورة الفرق في هذا النوع: أن يقول السائل مثلاً: لا يلزم من الولاية في الغلام الولاية في الجارية الثيب؛ لأن الثيب صارت لها قدرة التصرفات بنفسها لزوال حيائها. فنقول في جوابه هذا لا يضرنا لثبوت الاتحاد بين الغلام والصغيرة في العجز الثابت بالصغر، فيثبت الاتحاد في الحكم وهو ثبوت الولاية للأب مع وجود الافتراق بوصف آخر، فلا يبطل القياس بالفرق. بممانعة التجنيس بأن يمنع السائل عموم العلة وشمولها الأصل والفرع، فلا تؤثر في حكم الأصل. والفرق الخاص: عطف على قوله: بممانعة التجنيس يعني فساد القياس الثاني بأمرين: بممانعة التجنيس والفرق الخاص. لأن الحاجة في التصرف في المال كثير الوقوع له في كل يوم مائة مرة للتمدن في المأكل والمشارب والملابس والمساكن وغيرها وناجزة لا يحتمل التأخير وهي عاجزة عن التصرف فيها، فبهذه الضرورة وجب الولاية عليها لأبيها في مالها، ومثل هذه لم توجد في النفس لانعدام الشهوة؛ لأن هذه الثيب صغيرة غير بالغة، فلا يضطر إلى الولاية عليها لأبيها، وإنما هي بعد بلوغها، فبعد البلوغ تشاور فيه، فهذا الفرق راجع إلى أن العلة ليست عامة للفرع بناء على احتمال أن العلة هو الصغر لا نفسه مطلقا بل هو مع الضرورة.
The ruling of the first qiyas: that it is not invalidated by difference, because when the original and the branch are united in the effective cause, they must be united in the ruling, even if they differ in something other than this cause. The ruling of the second qiyas: its invalidity by opposition to the generality [of the cause] and the specific difference, which is the explanation that the effect of minority in guardianship over property is greater than its effect in guardianship over the self. 'By difference': i.e., any difference between the analogized and the analogized-upon; for qiyas does not require unity in all attributes but only in some, so any difference supports qiyas, not [invalidates] it. The image of the difference in this type: that the questioner says, for example: the guardianship over a boy does not necessitate guardianship over a previously-married girl, because the previously-married girl has the ability to act for herself due to the loss of her shyness. We say in response: this does not harm us because of the established unity between the boy and the minor girl in the incapacity established by minority, so unity in the ruling is established—the guardianship of the father—despite the difference in another attribute, so qiyas is not invalidated by difference. 'By opposition to generality': that the questioner prevents the generality of the cause and its inclusion of the original and branch, so it does not affect the ruling of the original. 'And the specific difference' is conjuncted to his statement 'by opposition to generality', meaning the invalidity of the second qiyas is by two things: opposition to generality and the specific difference. Because the need for disposal of property occurs frequently, a hundred times a day, for civilization in food, drink, clothing, housing, etc., and it is immediate and cannot be delayed, and she is incapable of disposing of it, so due to this necessity, guardianship over her property is obligatory for her father. The like of this is not found regarding the self due to the absence of desire; because this previously-married girl is a minor, not an adult, so she is not forced into guardianship over her by her father; rather, it is after her maturity, then she is consulted. So this difference reverts to the fact that the cause is not general to the branch based on the possibility that the cause is minority not absolutely but along with necessity.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage deals with two types of qiyas (analogical reasoning) and their rulings. The first type is valid qiyas: it is not invalidated by any mere difference between the original case (asl) and the branch (far') because the rule depends on the shared effective cause (illah). Differences in other attributes do not harm the analogy. The second type is invalid qiyas, which is invalidated by either (a) man' al-tajnis: denying the generality of the illah such that it does not cover both cases, or (b) farq khas: pointing out a specific difference that shows the illah is not truly effective in the branch. The example given is about guardianship (wilaya) over a minor: a boy and a previously-married minor girl both have guardianship of property due to necessity, but guardianship over the self (marriage) differs because the need is not as urgent for a minor girl. The author explains that the difference here shows the illah (minority) is not absolute but contingent on necessity. Thus, the qiyas fails because the illah does not fully apply to the branch.

Key Terms
الفرق (al-farq): Any difference between the original and the branch in attributes other than the illah
ممانعة التجنيس (mumana'at al-tajnis): Denying that the illah is general enough to cover both the original and the branch
الفرق الخاص (al-farq al-khas): A specific difference that shows the illah is not operative in the branch

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the example about guardianship, why is the qiyas from the boy to the previously-married minor girl considered invalid?
A) Because the girl is not a minor
B) Because the illah of minority is not general to the branch due to the specific difference of necessity
C) Because the guardianship over property is not established by consensus
D) Because the boy and girl have no shared attributes

Key Takeaway
Valid qiyas is not invalidated by any difference, only by a specific difference that negates the illah or by denying its generality.

The Third Type of Qiyas: Extracted Illah and the Role of Consensus
Defines extracted illah and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions for a valid extracted illah in Hanafi qiyas and apply them to a given attribute.

Core Idea
An extracted illah requires suitability and consensus to create ghalabat al-zann.

In this passage, Imam al-Shashi explains the third type of qiyas, where the cause is derived through ijtihad. Unlike a cause explicitly stated in the text, an extracted illah must be suitable for the ruling and must have been associated with the ruling in a place of consensus. This combination produces a preponderant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the attribute is the true cause. The lesson unpacks these conditions and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of qiyas
Distinguish between qiyas with explicit illah and with extracted illah. The extracted illah is derived through opinion and ijtihad.
This is the third type of qiyas.
2
Define the conditions for a valid extracted illah
The attribute must be suitable (munasib) for the ruling, and the ruling must have been associated with it in a place of consensus (ijma).
Suitability alone is insufficient.
3
Understand the role of consensus
The consensus provides the necessary link that attributes the ruling to the cause, not explicit textual evidence.
Without consensus, the link is not established.
4
Apply to the analogy
The giving-a-dirham example shows how we infer a cause: the act of giving to a poor person is preponderantly assumed to be for relieving need.
This creates ghalabat al-zann.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبيان القسم الثالث: وهو القياسُ بعلة مستنبطة بالرأي والاجتهاد ظاهر، وتحقيق ذلك: إذا وجَدْنا وصفاً مناسباً للحكم، وهو بحال يوجب ثبوت الحكم ويتقاضاه بالنظر إليه، وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يضاف الحكمُ إليه للمناسبة لا لشهادة الشرع بكونه علةً. ونظيره: إذا رأينا شخصاً أعطى فقيراً درهماً غلب على الظن أن الإعطاء لدفع حاجة الفقير، وتحصيل مصالح الثواب. إذا عُرف هذا فنقول: إذا رأينا وصفاً مناسباً للحكم، وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يغلب الظن بإضافة الحكم إلى ذلك الوصف. وغلبة الظن في الشرع توجبُ العَمَل عند انعدام ما فوقها من الدليل بمنزلة المسافر إذا غلب على ظنه أن بقربه ماءً لم يجز له التيمم، وعلى هذا مسائل التحري. وحكمُ هذا القياس أن يبطل بالفرق المناسب؛ لأن عنده يوجَدُ مناسب سواه في صورة يضاف الحكم إليه.
And the explanation of the third type: it is qiyas with an extracted cause by opinion and ijtihad, apparent, and its verification: when we find an attribute suitable for the ruling, and it is in a state that necessitates establishing the ruling and demands it by consideration, and the ruling has been associated with it in a place of consensus, the ruling is attributed to it due to suitability, not because of evidence from the Law that it is a cause. Its analogy: if we see a person give a dirham to a poor person, it is preponderantly thought that the giving is to fulfill the need of the poor and to obtain the benefits of reward. If this is known, we say: when we see an attribute suitable for the ruling, and the ruling has been associated with it in a place of consensus, preponderance of opinion attributes the ruling to that attribute. And preponderance of opinion in the Law necessitates action when there is no proof above it, like a traveler if he preponderantly thinks that there is water near him, he is not permitted to perform tayammum, and on this are the matters of taharri. And the ruling of this qiyas is that it is invalidated by a suitable difference, because according to it, there is found another suitable [attribute] in a form to which the ruling is attributed.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage introduces the third type of qiyas: analogical reasoning based on an extracted (mustanbitah) effective cause, discovered through ijtihad. The key condition is that the attribute (wasf) must be 'suitable' (munasib) for the ruling—meaning that associating the ruling with it brings benefit or prevents harm. Additionally, this attribute must have been associated with the same ruling in a place of consensus (ijma), so that the ruling is attributed to it due to its suitability, not because the Law explicitly declared it as the cause. The text gives an analogy: if we see someone give money to a poor person, we infer that the cause is to relieve need. This creates a preponderant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the attribute is the cause. In Islamic law, such preponderant assumption necessitates action when no stronger evidence exists, just as a traveler who strongly suspects water is nearby cannot perform tayammum (dry ablution) because the likely presence of water prevents it. Finally, the text states that this type of qiyas can be invalidated by a 'suitable difference' (farq munasib)—i.e., pointing out another suitable attribute in a different scenario that would lead to a different ruling.

Key Terms
الوصف المناسب (al-wasf al-munasib): An attribute that is suitable for the ruling, meaning it brings benefit or prevents harm
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Preponderant assumption that something is true, which suffices for action in the absence of stronger evidence

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the minimum requirement for an extracted attribute to be considered a valid cause in qiyas?
A) It must be explicitly stated in the Quran
B) It must be suitable and accompanied by the ruling in a place of consensus
C) It must be supported by a hadith
D) It must be agreed upon by all scholars

Key Takeaway
A valid extracted illah requires both suitability and prior consensus association to establish ghalabat al-zann.

Ghalabat al-Zann and the Invalidation of Extracted Qiyas
Explains the effect of ghalabat al-zann and the condition of invalidation by farq munasib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the legal force of ghalabat al-zann in Hanafi usul and identify when an extracted qiyas is invalidated by a suitable difference (farq munasib).

Core Idea
Ghalabat al-zann from extracted illah necessitates action, but a farq munasib invalidates the qiyas.

This passage continues the discussion of extracted qiyas by addressing two further points: the binding nature of ghalabat al-zann and the vulnerability of this qiyas to invalidation. The author compares ghalabat al-zann to a traveler's assumption of water, which prevents tayammum. He then states that if another suitable attribute (farq munasib) is found, the qiyas is invalidated because the cause could be that other attribute.

Guided Path
1
Understand ghalabat al-zann
It is a preponderant assumption that the attribute is the cause, arising from suitability and consensus.
This is not certainty, but a strong probability.
2
Learn the legal effect of ghalabat al-zann
In the absence of stronger evidence, this assumption necessitates action.
It is binding in practice.
3
Analyze the traveler analogy
If a traveler is confident water is nearby, he cannot perform tayammum; he must seek water.
The preponderant assumption makes water 'effectively present'.
4
Recognize invalidation by farq munasib
If another suitable attribute is found in a case to which the ruling could be attributed, the qiyas is invalidated.
The presence of an alternative suitable cause breaks the original causal link.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبيان القسم الثالث: وهو القياسُ بعلة مستنبطة بالرأي والاجتهاد ظاهر، وتحقيق ذلك: إذا وجَدْنا وصفاً مناسباً للحكم، وهو بحال يوجب ثبوت الحكم ويتقاضاه بالنظر إليه، وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يضاف الحكمُ إليه للمناسبة لا لشهادة الشرع بكونه علةً. ونظيره: إذا رأينا شخصاً أعطى فقيراً درهماً غلب على الظن أن الإعطاء لدفع حاجة الفقير، وتحصيل مصالح الثواب. إذا عُرف هذا فنقول: إذا رأينا وصفاً مناسباً للحكم، وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يغلب الظن بإضافة الحكم إلى ذلك الوصف. وغلبة الظن في الشرع توجبُ العَمَل عند انعدام ما فوقها من الدليل بمنزلة المسافر إذا غلب على ظنه أن بقربه ماءً لم يجز له التيمم، وعلى هذا مسائل التحري. وحكمُ هذا القياس أن يبطل بالفرق المناسب؛ لأن عنده يوجَدُ مناسب سواه في صورة يضاف الحكم إليه.
And the explanation of the third type: it is qiyas with an extracted cause by opinion and ijtihad, apparent, and its verification: when we find an attribute suitable for the ruling, and it is in a state that necessitates establishing the ruling and demands it by consideration, and the ruling has been associated with it in a place of consensus, the ruling is attributed to it due to suitability, not because of evidence from the Law that it is a cause. Its analogy: if we see a person give a dirham to a poor person, it is preponderantly thought that the giving is to fulfill the need of the poor and to obtain the benefits of reward. If this is known, we say: when we see an attribute suitable for the ruling, and the ruling has been associated with it in a place of consensus, preponderance of opinion attributes the ruling to that attribute. And preponderance of opinion in the Law necessitates action when there is no proof above it, like a traveler if he preponderantly thinks that there is water near him, he is not permitted to perform tayammum, and on this are the matters of taharri. And the ruling of this qiyas is that it is invalidated by a suitable difference, because according to it, there is found another suitable [attribute] in a form to which the ruling is attributed.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage introduces the third type of qiyas: analogical reasoning based on an extracted (mustanbitah) effective cause, discovered through ijtihad. The key condition is that the attribute (wasf) must be 'suitable' (munasib) for the ruling—meaning that associating the ruling with it brings benefit or prevents harm. Additionally, this attribute must have been associated with the same ruling in a place of consensus (ijma), so that the ruling is attributed to it due to its suitability, not because the Law explicitly declared it as the cause. The text gives an analogy: if we see someone give money to a poor person, we infer that the cause is to relieve need. This creates a preponderant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the attribute is the cause. In Islamic law, such preponderant assumption necessitates action when no stronger evidence exists, just as a traveler who strongly suspects water is nearby cannot perform tayammum (dry ablution) because the likely presence of water prevents it. Key Terms
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Preponderant assumption that something is true, which suffices for action in the absence of stronger evidence
الفرق المناسب (al-farq al-munasib): Another suitable attribute that could be the cause, thus invalidating the current qiyas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition is extracted qiyas invalidated?
A) When there is any attribute in the new case that differs
B) When a suitable difference (farq munasib) is found
C) When consensus is absent

Key Takeaway

The Foundation of Valid Qiyas: Appropriateness and Consensus Linkage
Explains the appropriate descriptor and its evidentiary weight

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a descriptor that is both suitable for the ruling and linked to the ruling in a consensus case creates a strong presumption obligating action, and distinguish this from mere suitability.

Core Idea
Strong presumption obligates action when the descriptor is both appropriate and linked to consensus.

In Hanafi usul, not every suitable descriptor qualifies as a valid cause ('illa) for qiyas. The text lays down a crucial condition: the descriptor must be linked to the ruling in a case of consensus (ijma'). Only then does suitability generate a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the descriptor is the cause. This lesson unpacks that condition and its evidentiary weight, using analogies from travel and tayammum, and ranks descriptors in a hierarchy similar to witness testimony.

Guided Path
1
Define Key Concepts
Identify and define 'descriptor' (wasf), 'appropriateness' (munasaba), 'consensus' (ijma'), and 'strong presumption' (ghalabat al-zann) as they appear in the text.
These terms form the foundation of the rule.
2
State the Condition
Extract the condition from the text: a suitable descriptor linked to the ruling in a consensus case yields strong presumption that it is the cause.
The text says 'إذا رأينا وصفاً مناسباً للحكم، وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يغلب الظن بإضافة الحكم إلى ذلك الوصف'.
3
Analyze the Ruling Strength
Understand that this strong presumption obligates action in the absence of stronger evidence, just as a traveler's presumption of water prohibits tayammum.
The traveler analogy demonstrates that ghalabat al-zann is treated like certainty for practical rulings.
4
Study the Example
Work through the example of guardianship in marriage for a minor: minority is suitable because it causes inability, and it is linked to consensus in guardianship of property.
This shows how the condition works in a real fiqhi case.
5
Identify the Limitation
Note that mere suitability (munasaba) alone makes the descriptor a possible cause but does not obligate action – 'يُحَوِّزُهُ ولا يُوجِبُهُ'.
This is the key distinction: suitability is necessary but not sufficient without consensus linkage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
البحث الرابع في القياس فصل في القياس الشرعي وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يضاف الحكمُ إليه للمناسبة لا لشهادة الشرع هذا الوصف من الأكل واللبس بكونه علةً. ونظيره: إذا رأينا شخصاً أعطى فقيراً درهماً غلب على الظن أن الإعطاء لدفع حاجة الفقير، وتحصيل مصالح الثواب. إذا عُرف هذا فنقول: إذا رأينا وصفاً مناسباً للحكم، وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع الإجماع يغلب الظن بإضافة الحكم إلى ذلك الوصف. وغلبة الظن في الشرع توجبُ العَمَل عند انعدام ما فوقها من الدليل بمنزلة المسافر إذا غلب على ظنه أن بقربه ماءً لم يجز له التيمم، وعلى هذا مسائل التحري. وحكمُ هذا القياس أن يبطل بالفرق المناسب؛ لأن عنده يُوجَدُ مناسب سواه في صورة يضاف الحكم إليه: جواب إذا أي: إذا وجدنا مناسباً للحكم وقد اقترن به الحكم في موضع آخر من نص أو إجماع يضاف الحكم إلى ذلك الوصف كذا في "معدن الأصول". للمناسبة: لمناسبة ذلك الوصف الحكم بكونه علة: أي بكون الوصف علة كما إذا عللنا في ولاية الإنكاح في الصغير بعلة الصغر للمناسبة؛ لأن ولاية الإنكاح لم تشرع إلا على وجه النظر للصغير باعتبار عجزه عن مباشرة النكاح مع حاجة إلى مقصوده، والصغير مورث للعجز، فكان هذا تعليلاً بوصف ملائم للحكم، وقد ظهر أثر هذا الوصف في موضع الإجماع وهو ولاية المال، فإنها ثابتة في مال الصغير بالإجماع، وإنما يشترط هذا الوجوب العمل بالوصف؛ لأن الوصف في القياس بمنزلة الشاهد العدالة من وهو اجتنابه عن محظورات دينه، واجتنابه عنها يدل ظاهراً على أنه يجتنب عن الكذب في الشهادة أيضاً، فظهور أثر الوصف في موضع آخر يدل ظاهراً على أنه مؤثر في موضع النزاع، فهذا يوجب العمل بالقياس بهذه العلة، وأما مجرد المناسبة فيُحَوِّزُهُ ولا يوجبه كذا في "الفصول" و "المعدن". لم يجز له التيمُّمُ: لأن غلبة الظن عند انعدام ما فوقها من الدليل بمنزلة المتحقق. مسائل التحري كما إذا اشتبهت عليه القبلة وتحرى ووقع تحريه على شيء لغلبة الظن وليس عنده من يسأله فيجب العمل به بالفرق المناسب : أي بالفرق بين الأصل والفرع في الوصف المناسب؛ لأن عنده وجود الفرق = الحكم، فلا يبقى الظنُّ بإضافة الحكم إليه، فلا يثبتُ الحكم به؛ لأنه كان بناء على غلبة الظن، وقد بَطَل ذلك بالفرق. غلبة الظن الوصف الحكم وعلى هذا كان العَمَلَ بالنوع الأوّل بمنزلة الحكم بالشهادة بعد تزكية الشاهد وتعديله، والنوع الثاني بمنزلة الشهادة عند ظهور العدالة قبل التزكية، والنوع الثالث بمنزلة شهادة المستور. ...
The fourth inquiry on analogy. Chapter on legal analogy. And the ruling was linked to it in a place of consensus: the ruling is attributed to the descriptor for suitability, not because the law indicates this descriptor. Its example: eating and clothing as a cause. Its parallel: if we see a person giving a dirham to a poor person, it is strongly presumed that the giving is to fulfill the poor person's need and to obtain the benefits of reward. When this is known, we say: if we see a descriptor suitable for the ruling, and it was linked to the ruling in a place of consensus, strong presumption arises that the ruling is attributed to that descriptor. Strong presumption in law necessitates action when there is no evidence above it, like a traveller who strongly presumes that there is water near him – he is not permitted to perform tayammum, and similarly the cases of ijtihad (taharrī). The ruling of this analogy is that it is invalidated by an appropriate difference, because with it there exists another suitable descriptor in a different case that could be attributed the ruling. Response to 'if': i.e., if we find a descriptor suitable for the ruling and it was linked to the ruling in another place from text or consensus, the ruling is attributed to that descriptor, as in Ma'dan al-Usul. 'For suitability': because of the suitability of that descriptor to the ruling as being a cause, i.e., the descriptor being a cause – as when we give the cause for guardianship in marriage for a minor as the suitability of minority, since guardianship in marriage was legislated only for the benefit of the minor due to his inability to perform marriage despite his need for its purpose, and minority causes inability, so this is an explanation with a descriptor suitable for the ruling. And the effect of this descriptor appeared in a place of consensus, which is guardianship over property, as it is established for the minor's property by consensus. This obligation to act by the descriptor is only required because the descriptor in analogy is like the witness's 'adāla (integrity) from avoiding religious prohibitions, and his avoidance of them ostensibly indicates that he also avoids lying in testimony. So the appearance of the descriptor's effect in another place ostensibly indicates that it is effective in the disputed case, so this necessitates acting by this analogy with this cause. As for mere suitability, it makes it possible but does not necessitate it, as in al-Fusūl and al-Ma'dan. 'He is not permitted tayammum': because strong presumption when there is no evidence above it is like certainty. Cases of taharrī: like when the direction of the qibla is unclear for him, he performs taharrī and his taharrī leads to something by strong presumption, and there is no one to ask, so he must act by it. 'By an appropriate difference': i.e., by the difference between the original and the branch in the appropriate descriptor, because with him the existence of a difference = the ruling, so the presumption of attributing the ruling to the original descriptor does not remain, so the ruling is not established by it, because it was based on strong presumption, and that was nullified by the difference. Strong presumption, the descriptor, the ruling. And upon this, action with the first type is like ruling by testimony after the witness's tazkiya and ta'dīl; the second type is like testimony when integrity appears before tazkiya; the third type is like the testimony of a person of unknown character (mastūr). ...
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions of valid qiyas (analogy) in Hanafi usul. It explains that when a descriptor (wasf) is suitable (munasib) for a ruling and is linked to that ruling in a consensus case, this creates a strong presumption (ghalabat al-zann) that the descriptor is the cause ('illa). This presumption obligates action in the absence of stronger evidence, similar to the case of a traveler who presumes water is near – he cannot perform tayammum. The passage then states that such an analogy can be invalidated by a 'farq munasib' – showing an appropriate difference between the original and branch that provides another suitable descriptor. The author analogizes the descriptor's evidentiary value to witness testimony: a descriptor explicitly stated in text is like a witness after tazkiya (verified integrity); one known by consensus is like a witness whose integrity is apparent; one based solely on suitability is like a witness of unknown character (mastūr). The discussion includes examples from Hanafi fiqh, such as guardianship in marriage for minors based on minority, and the traveler analogy.

Key Terms
غلبة الظن (ghalabat al-zann): Strong presumption that the descriptor is the cause, arising from its appropriateness and linkage in consensus
المناسبة (al-munāsaba): Suitability of the descriptor to the ruling, meaning the descriptor is appropriate for achieving the ruling's purpose
الفرق المناسب (al-farq al-munāsib): An appropriate difference between original and branch that provides another suitable descriptor, invalidating the original qiyas

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the effect of a descriptor being suitable (munasib) for a ruling but not linked to the ruling in a place of consensus?
A) It creates a strong presumption obligating action.
B) It makes the descriptor a possible cause but does not necessitate action.
C) It invalidates any qiyas based on that descriptor.
D) It has no effect; suitability is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
A descriptor must be both suitable for the ruling and linked to the ruling in a consensus case to create a strong presumption that obligates action in qiyas.
